# plan.md ŌĆö Feature scope & build log

> _Created: 2026-06-03 ┬Ę Last updated: 2026-06-20_

> [!IMPORTANT]
> **PRODUCT NAME: CADENCE.** The product is **Cadence**, and that is the only name to use. A brief 2026-06-10 rename experiment to a different brand was reverted on 2026-06-16; the retired name must not be reintroduced anywhere (code, docs, DB, env, caches, APIs). Any stray legacy token from that experiment is to be read as equivalent to `cadence`/`Cadence`.
>
> _Do not perform destructive refactoring of database column/table names or folder structures that are bound to Lovable Cloud and pgvector schemas. All modifications should map the name logically at the user and documentation level while keeping underlying plumbing compatible._

> The canonical record of **what Cadence is built to be** (the full feature scope), **the order we build it**, and **what already exists to reuse**. Product framing: [`README.md`](./README.md). Operating rules: [`AGENTS.md`](./AGENTS.md). Architecture: [`architecture/`](./architecture/). UI contract: [`DESIGN.md`](./DESIGN.md).
>
> **No MVP1/MVP2/MVP3 gating, no far-future phase deferral.** We build the full intended scope on the current stack ([`docs/decisions/tech-stack.md`](./docs/decisions/tech-stack.md)) and ship continuously. This doc is written to be read straight into a coding session (Claude Code / Lovable) and acted on.

---

## How this file is organized

1. **Feature scope** ŌĆö the whole product, stress-tested as if nothing is built. The high-level feature list.
2. **Competitive feature comparison** ŌĆö factory.ai ┬Ę hyperagent ┬Ę Linear ŌåÆ what Cadence should build.
3. **Granular feature catalog** ŌĆö every feature from login/logout to agent-transfer/workspace level, with _what_ and _why_. This is the dev-ready map.
4. **Build order** ŌĆö the sequence to build it, production-grade, reusing legacy code where it fits.
5. **Active build log** ŌĆö what we actually ship, updated as we go (starts near-empty).
6. **Legacy build log (retained)** ŌĆö the previous source build, kept as a reuse reference, not the plan.
7. **Product-agent roster** ŌĆö re-examined (explicit vs. implicit).
8. **Testing, lessons, out-of-scope.**

---

## 1. Feature scope (stress-tested from scratch)

> [!IMPORTANT]
> **v4 supersedes this section for scope (2026-06-11).** The canonical feature scope is now [`docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md) ŌĆö 7 platform laws, 6 stations over the 12-stage engine, the 19-agent mesh with handoff contract + HITL gate matrix, the 7-surface IA, station feature catalogs (SEN/DEC/DEF/BLD/LCH/LRN/ENG/OPS), and milestones M1ŌĆōM5. The adversarial reasoning behind it: [`docs/strategy/archive/v4-stress-test.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v4-stress-test.md). The 12-stage engine description below remains valid as the _internal_ loop reference; where wording differs, **the v4 map wins**. **v5 overlay (2026-06-11):** the _felt product_ ŌĆö wedge UX, nav, vocabulary, June 22 demo scope ŌĆö is governed by [`docs/strategy/archive/v5-chief-of-staff.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v5-chief-of-staff.md) (PM Chief of Staff; 4 felt surfaces + Trust drawer; phases `F-V5-RITUAL` ŌåÆ `F-V5-DEMO`). v4 remains the expansion map.

Cadence runs the full product lifecycle as one governed, autonomous loop. The scope below is the target product ŌĆö not a discovery tool. Each stage is run by autonomous agents; the human approves at the gates.

### Who we serve, what they expect, and the gap (grounding for the feature list)

The feature list below is a deliberate response to who the customer is and what the market already sets as table-stakes ŌĆö not a wish list. Inspiration drawn from products worth learning from is captured in [`docs/references/competitive-reference.md`](./docs/archive/competitive-reference.md) (deferred; inspiration only).

**Personas (who orchestrates Cadence):**

- **P1 ŌĆö Enterprise Director / VP of Product (The Portfolio Governor)**: owns portfolio-level alignment, agent spend budgets, and compliance. Pain: Swarm drift, lack of visibility into agent actions, security audits, budget overruns, and multi-product roadmap health.
- **P2 ŌĆö Lead / Senior PM (The Daily Cockpit Operator)**: runs day-to-day discovery, spec definition, and feature delivery. Pain: Mechanical process work (spec writing, ticket updates, release logs, alert triage) eating up time needed for strategic judgment.
- **P3 ŌĆö Engineering Lead / Tech Architect (The Code Gatekeeper)**: guards repository health, code quality, and branch stability. Pain: Agent-written code drifting from internal architecture guidelines, introducing regressions, or breaking sandboxed environments.
- **P4 ŌĆö UX/UI Designer (The Visual Validator)**: ensures design tokens and brand style guide alignment. Pain: Generated code failing to match design system tokens or looking off-brand in mockups.
- **P5 ŌĆö GTM Lead / Product Marketer**: handles positioning and product launch. Pain: Generating changelogs, marketing collateral, newsletter posts, and distribution updates by hand for every release.
- **P6 ŌĆö Customer Success & Support Lead**: monitors product support feedback. Pain: High ticket volumes, slow bug triage, and user signals getting lost before reaching the product manager.

**Market expectations (table-stakes ŌĆö must-haves, or we're not credible):** auth + SSO-ready tenancy; real (not mocked) data; connectors to the tools they live in; an assistant/chat surface; observability + cost visibility; approvals/audit for anything autonomous; multi-project support; export/no-lock-in.

**The gap (where the market is underserved ŌĆö our opening):** point tools own single bands (engineering autonomy, or issue tracking, or research synthesis). **No one runs the _whole_ lifecycle ŌĆö discover ŌåÆ build ŌåÆ ship ŌåÆ launch ŌåÆ support ŌåÆ learn ŌĆö as one governed, autonomous, multi-product loop.** That gap is the spine of the feature catalog in section 2.

**What the customer actually wants (the job):** "Take this intent and run it end-to-end ŌĆö autonomously, in parallel, across my products ŌĆö and only stop me for the calls that matter." Every feature below maps to that job.

**The feature list derives from the PM's actual day.** The product manager is the cockpit operator ŌĆö the features below exist to run the PM's day (triage inbox ŌåÆ decide ŌåÆ synthesize ŌåÆ spec ŌåÆ tickets ŌåÆ build/test/ship ŌåÆ launch/update ŌåÆ answer "why is this on the roadmap?" ŌåÆ report ŌåÆ repeat). The day-to-features mapping and the PM/eng-lead lenses are in [`docs/planning/considerations.md`](docs/planning/considerations.md). If a feature does not serve a real PM task, question it.

### Lifecycle stages (the 12-Stage Product Loop)

**S1 ŌĆö Signal Capture**

- Multi-source signal ingest: support tickets, churn, usage telemetry, sales notes, reviews, NPS, interviews.
- Agent clustering ŌåÆ themes ŌåÆ ICE-scored opportunities; continuous (not one-shot) synthesis; dedupe by similarity.
- A continuously-updated discovery feed per product.

**S2 ŌĆö Audio Sync (WhisperFlow)**

- High-context audio recording, transcription, and meeting spec extraction.
- Translates voice memos or team meetings into feature specs and backlog tickets with zero friction.

**S3 ŌĆö ICE Prioritization**

- Prioritization queue management: opportunity scoring based on Impact, Confidence, and Ease.
- Automated re-prioritization as new signals arrive or existing ones scale in severity.

**S4 ŌĆö Spec Definition**

- Opportunity ŌåÆ PRD/spec, retrieval-grounded and cited; inline `/ai` editing; versioned with diff.
- Acceptance criteria, non-goals, risks, success metrics auto-drafted; human edits and approves.

**S5 ŌĆö Sprint Planning**

- Spec ŌåÆ dependency-aware task graph with estimates, owners, risk flags.
- Outcome-oriented roadmap (Now/Next/Later) synced automatically to Linear/Jira.

**S6 ŌĆö Agentic Build**

- In-product multi-file coding: Builder Agent claims file locks, checks out branches, and writes code.
- Surgical modifications across files, committing atomically and resolving conflict flags.

**S7 ŌĆö Visual QA**

- Sandbox preview environments generated automatically for visual validation of UI changes.
- Let designers and PMs audit layout and styling against design system tokens before merging.

**S8 ŌĆö Safe Release**

- Merges PRs, runs deploy checklists, deploys, and monitors production health.
- Automated rollback triggered if error metrics or exception counts spike post-deploy.

**S9 ŌĆö GTM Launch**

- Growth agent drafts release changelogs, marketing blog posts, newsletter copies, and announcement text.

**S10 ŌĆö Support Triage**

- Support agent triages incoming customer tickets, drafts answers, and routes bug logs back into Signal Capture (S1).

**S11 ŌĆö Cohort Analytics**

- Automated feature adoption tracking, cohort analysis, and outcome funnel monitoring.

**S12 ŌĆö Learn & Reflect**

- Outcome evaluation: compares performance telemetry with the original PRD spec.
- Updates the Product Memory Graph and publishes a learning brief to the portfolio dashboard.

### Cross-cutting platform (mandatory, spans all stages)

**X1 ŌĆö Orchestration & automation engine**

- Workflow definitions across stages; event/schedule/webhook triggers; an automation builder.
- **Many sub-agents running in parallel** within a mission; **many agent sessions running in parallel** across missions.
- A live orchestration view (the mission/agent graph) with per-node status, cost, and approval state.
- Planner/executor loop with max-step/max-cost caps, replay-and-branch, cancellation, checkpoints.

**X2 ŌĆö Multi-product & multi-workspace**

- **Multiple products in flight ŌĆö Product A/B/C ŌĆö grouped under Workspaces (A/B/C).**
- Per-product/workspace isolation of data, agents, memory, budgets, and access (RLS by `user_id` + `workspace_id`; see [`architecture/data.md`](./architecture/data.md)).
- Product switcher; cross-product portfolio view.

**X3 ŌĆö Trust & governance (the AI trust stack)**

- Per-call telemetry, LLM-as-judge scoring, guardrails (input + output), RAG with citations, prompt versioning + A/B, eval harness with regression gate, drift watch, budgets, live trace waterfall, incidents log, approval gates everywhere.

**X4 ŌĆö Product Memory**

- Queryable graph of signals ŌåÆ themes ŌåÆ opportunities ŌåÆ decisions ŌåÆ experiments ŌåÆ outcomes, with `supersedes` lineage; the institutional context agents reason over; exportable as skill packs.

**X5 ŌĆö Interop (agent-native)**

- MCP server (Cadence as a tool surface) + MCP client (consume external tools) + A2A (Agent Cards, delegate-to-agent, peer registry). Capability scopes, rate limits, prompt-injection guard on external results, audit log.

**X6 ŌĆö Identity, auth, billing**

- Auth (email + OAuth), session management, per-workspace membership (future: roles/teams), BYO model keys (encrypted), usage/billing metering against budgets. See [`architecture/security.md`](./architecture/security.md).

---

## 2. Granular feature catalog (login to agent-transfer, with what + why)

> **Sub-feature-level expansion:** [`docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`](docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md) takes every area below down to addressable sub-features with stable IDs, states, acceptance signals, dependencies, and a status ├Ś build-order rollup. This section stays the narrative catalog; the backlog is the flat, ticket-ready list. Keep both true.

Every feature, grouped by area. Format: **Feature ŌĆö what it is ŌĆö _why we need it_.** This is the build checklist; each becomes an issue/spec. Status tags: `[reuse]` legacy survives, `[extend]` legacy base + new work, `[new]` build from scratch.

> **Inspiration, not comparison.** This catalog absorbs the best ideas from products worth learning from ŌĆö factory.ai's autonomous build/ship + live "mission" view (we extend it past code into launch/support), hyperagent's team-of-agents with per-agent budgets and self-improving memory, and Linear's agents-as-first-class-users + saved-workflow skills + event automations. We take the inspiration and build it into _our_ features below; we are not maintaining a competitor scorecard.

### A. Identity & access

- **Sign up / onboarding** ŌĆö email+password + Google OAuth; create first workspace + product; set display name, timezone, working hours. ŌĆö _Entry point; personalization and scheduling depend on it._ `[reuse]`
- **Login / logout** ŌĆö authenticated session, sign-out everywhere, session refresh, `Last-Event-ID` resume for streams. ŌĆö _Baseline security and reliable streaming._ `[reuse]`
- **Password reset / email verification** ŌĆö standard flows; verification on by default. ŌĆö _Account safety._ `[reuse]`
- **Profile & preferences** ŌĆö display name, role, timezone, working hours, default model per surface. ŌĆö _Drives greeting, scheduling, model routing._ `[reuse]`
- **BYO model keys** ŌĆö add/test/rotate/delete provider keys, encrypted; masked display. ŌĆö _Model-agnostic; cost control; enterprise trust._ `[reuse]`
- **Roles & membership (future)** ŌĆö invite, per-workspace roles, SSO/SAML. ŌĆö _Team and enterprise readiness._ `[new]`

### B. Workspaces & products

- **Create / switch workspace** ŌĆö top-level tenancy boundary. ŌĆö _Isolates a client/company/initiative._ `[extend]`
- **Create product under workspace** ŌĆö Product A/B/C inside a workspace; vision/problem/target-users/metrics/stage. ŌĆö _Run several products in parallel without bleed._ `[extend]`
- **Product switcher + portfolio view** ŌĆö fast switch; cross-product overview. ŌĆö _One operator, many products._ `[new]`
- **Per-product isolation** ŌĆö data, agents, memory, budgets scoped by `user_id`+`workspace_id`+product. ŌĆö _Security + correctness across products._ `[extend]`
- **Archive / delete product** ŌĆö lifecycle hygiene. ŌĆö _Avoid clutter; data governance._ `[new]`

### C. Agents ŌĆö configuration

- **Agent roster** ŌĆö list durable agents + spawned sub-agents per product. ŌĆö _See the team you command._ `[extend]`
- **Create / clone / configure agent** ŌĆö system prompt, tool allow-list, model, temperature/top*p/seed, max tokens, schedule, approval mode, memory toggle. ŌĆö \_Tailor behavior + governance per role.* `[reuse]`
- **Enable / disable / schedule agent** ŌĆö cron schedules with next-run preview. ŌĆö _Autonomy on a clock._ `[reuse]`
- **Agent detail + run history** ŌĆö last runs (status/duration/score/cost), memory inspector. ŌĆö _Trust through observability._ `[reuse]`

### D. Agent execution

- **Run on-demand / scheduled** ŌĆö manual trigger or cron fan-out. ŌĆö _Both reactive and proactive autonomy._ `[reuse]`
- **Planner/executor loop** ŌĆö plan ŌåÆ tool calls ŌåÆ observe ŌåÆ reflect ŌåÆ answer; max-step/max-cost caps. ŌĆö _Reliable multi-step autonomy._ `[reuse]`
- **Approval gates + Decision Queue** ŌĆö `auto|confirm|review`; queue of runs awaiting review; one-click resume from checkpoint. ŌĆö _Governed autonomy; the trust core._ `[reuse]`
- **Cancellation / replay-and-branch / checkpoints** ŌĆö stop mid-run (save partial), re-run against different model/prompt, resume. ŌĆö _Control + iteration._ `[reuse]`

### E. Agent communication, coordination & transfer (mandatory)

- **Sub-agent spawning** ŌĆö Orchestrator spawns ephemeral specialists per task. ŌĆö _Scale to the work without fixed seats._ `[new]`
- **Agent-to-agent messaging** ŌĆö structured internal A2A messages between agents in a mission. ŌĆö _Coordination without a human relaying context._ `[new]`
- **Agent transfer / handoff** ŌĆö pass a mission + its context, memory, and artifacts from one agent to another (e.g. Planner ŌåÆ Engineer ŌåÆ QA ŌåÆ Release). ŌĆö _Work flows across the lifecycle with zero context loss; this is the spine of the autonomous loop._ `[new]`
- **Parallel sub-agents** ŌĆö many specialists working a single mission concurrently. ŌĆö _Speed; mirrors a real team._ `[new]`
- **Parallel agent sessions** ŌĆö many missions running at once across products. ŌĆö _One operator, many things in flight._ `[new]`
- **Orchestration / mission graph view** ŌĆö live DAG of agents/sessions with per-node status, cost, approval state; pause/steer. ŌĆö _See and command the swarm._ `[new]`
- **Shared vs. private memory** ŌĆö mission-shared context + per-agent long-term memory with importance decay. ŌĆö _Coordination without leakage._ `[extend]`

### F. Discover

- **Signal ingest** ŌĆö paste/CSV now; connectors (Intercom/Zendesk/reviews/sales) next; sentiment on insert. ŌĆö _Raw material of discovery._ `[extend]`
- **Clustering ŌåÆ themes ŌåÆ opportunities** ŌĆö embed + cluster + synthesize with evidence ids; ICE scoring; dedupe by similarity. ŌĆö _Turn noise into ranked opportunities._ `[reuse]`
- **Continuous discovery feed** ŌĆö always-fresh per-product feed. ŌĆö _The lead use case; ongoing, not one-shot._ `[extend]`

### G. Define

- **PRD/spec generation** ŌĆö opportunity ŌåÆ structured cited draft. ŌĆö _Specs downstream of evidence, not vibes._ `[reuse]`
- **Doc editor + `/ai` + versions/diff** ŌĆö Tiptap, inline AI commands, autosave, version diff, citation pills. ŌĆö _Author + iterate with provenance._ `[reuse]`

### H. Plan

- **Task graph** ŌĆö spec ŌåÆ dependency-aware tasks with estimates/owners/risk. ŌĆö _Executable plan agents can run._ `[reuse]`
- **Outcome roadmap** ŌĆö Now/Next/Later; each item declares its outcome + measure. ŌĆö _Anti-feature-factory; ties work to results._ `[extend]`
- **Scheduling** ŌĆö agent proposes work blocks in working hours. ŌĆö _Time-aware execution._ `[reuse]`

### I. Build (autonomous)

- **Studio multi-file coding** ŌĆö agents write across files; per-hunk diff accept/reject; atomic revisions. ŌĆö _Agents build, not just suggest._ `[extend]`
- **Watch-the-agents-build surface** ŌĆö live per-session view: step, files, tool calls, cost, status; pause/steer/approve. ŌĆö _Trust + control over autonomous code._ `[new]`
- **Branch/worktree isolation per mission** ŌĆö each mission on its own branch. ŌĆö _Parallel safe building._ `[new]`

### J. Test (autonomous)

- **Test generation + run** ŌĆö agents author and run unit/integration/E2E + evals. ŌĆö _Quality without a human writing every test._ `[new]`
- **QA gate + self-correct loop** ŌĆö failing tests feed back to the build agent until green or escalate. ŌĆö _Closed-loop quality before ship._ `[new]`

### K. Ship

- **PR / deploy / release notes** ŌĆö open PRs, run deploy checklist, deploy, draft notes ŌĆö behind approval. ŌĆö _Autonomous delivery, governed._ `[new]`
- **Rollback triggers** ŌĆö documented per release. ŌĆö _Safe shipping._ `[new]`

### L. Launch / GTM / price

- **Launch + positioning + pricing + distribution drafts** ŌĆö agent-drafted, human-approved before external. ŌĆö _The lifecycle past code, that point tools skip._ `[new]`
- **Customer-facing pages / announcements** ŌĆö generated, approved. ŌĆö _Close the go-to-market gap._ `[new]`

### M. Operate / support

- **Ticket triage + draft answers + route/escalate** ŌĆö agents handle inbound; themes flow back to Discover. ŌĆö _Support closes the loop into discovery._ `[new]`

### N. Learn

- **Decisions + `supersedes`** ŌĆö outcomes write decisions with lineage. ŌĆö _Auditable "why," and belief updates._ `[reuse]`
- **Re-score + insight memo + daily brief** ŌĆö outcomes re-rank opportunities; memo surfaces in the brief. ŌĆö _The loop compounds._ `[extend]`

### O. Product Memory

- **Knowledge graph + query** ŌĆö signalsŌåÆdecisionsŌåÆoutcomes, typed nodes/edges. ŌĆö _Institutional context agents reason over._ `[new]`
- **Currency / drift on facts + skill packs** ŌĆö flag stale facts; export versioned skill bundles over MCP. ŌĆö _Memory stays true; reusable expertise._ `[new]`

### P. Trust & observability

- **Telemetry + traces + judge scores** ŌĆö per-call events, trace waterfall, LLM-as-judge. ŌĆö _Measure every AI action._ `[reuse]`
- **Guardrails + prompt studio + eval harness + drift + budgets + incidents** ŌĆö input/output guards, versioned prompts + A/B, regression-gated evals, drift watch, budget caps, incident log. ŌĆö _Make autonomy safe, improvable, affordable._ `[reuse]`
- **AI message contract** ŌĆö score/model/latency/tokens/cost/citations/feedback/trace/replay on every AI message. ŌĆö _Trust is the UI._ `[reuse]`

### Q. Interop (agent-native)

- **MCP server + client** ŌĆö expose Cadence as tools; consume external tools. ŌĆö _Be the place agents plug in._ `[new]`
- **A2A server/client + Agent Cards + scopes/limits/audit** ŌĆö peer agents, delegate-to-agent, governed. ŌĆö _Cross-vendor agent ecosystem._ `[new]`

### R. Platform & ops

- **Command palette (ŌīśK) + global search** ŌĆö resolve every destination/action/artifact. ŌĆö _Keyboard-first speed._ `[reuse]`
- **Connectors / integrations** ŌĆö Docs, Notion, Linear, Calendar, GitHub, Slack, CRM. ŌĆö _Act on the systems the operator lives in._ `[extend]`
- **Notifications + budgets config + settings** ŌĆö approvals, breaches, guardrail rules, integration health. ŌĆö _Operate the platform._ `[extend]`

---

## 3. Build order (v4 milestones ŌĆö each independently demo-able)

> Canonical milestone definitions with proof bars: [`docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md) ┬¦9. The foundation invariants (blast-radius limits, spend caps, kill-switch, prompt-injection defense, provider fallback, durable runtime, sandboxed execution ŌĆö see [`docs/planning/considerations.md`](docs/planning/considerations.md)) remain P0 architecture, already largely in place; every milestone below builds on them, never around them.

1. **M1 ŌĆö The Golden Path (demo-ready).** One continuous, watchable run: connect Slack/GitHub ŌåÆ Scout themes ŌåÆ Strategist ranks (Critic attached) ŌåÆ approve ŌåÆ Scribe cited spec ŌåÆ approve ŌåÆ Planner task graph ŌåÆ Builder PR + CI green ŌåÆ release-note draft ŌåÆ outcome card. Includes `F-IA-V4` (collapse 34 routes to the 7-surface IA), vocabulary enforcement, cost-per-mission chip, narrated empty states. _This fixes "not demo-ready" before anything new is added._
2. **M2 ŌĆö The Loop Closes (the differentiator).** The right half becomes real: support triage loop (LRN-01), analytics inbound (SEN-05), launch kits (LCH-01), outcome reviews (LRN-02), visible re-score (LRN-03), memory consult/write on every mission (ENG-05), cost-per-artifact (ENG-06). Proof: a support-ticket cluster re-ranks the opportunity queue with zero human transport.
3. **M3 ŌĆö The Team Arrives.** Roles + per-persona approval lanes (ENG-08), design scaffolds + handoff (DEF-04/05), visual validation (BLD-06), enablement notes (LCH-04), spec comments, multi-seat.
4. **M4 ŌĆö The Org Runs Itself.** Portfolio view, budget enforcement UX, MCP server/client + A2A delegate-out (ENG-07, BLD-04), skill packs (LRN-05), enterprise plane (ENG-09), pricing briefs (LCH-03).
5. **M5 ŌĆö Compounding.** Memory-graph querying as product surface, stale-fact drift, cross-product learnings, connector breadth, outcome-priced enterprise plans.

Sequencing rule unchanged: architecture first, so later stages are _additions, not rewrites_. See [`docs/decisions/tech-stack.md`](./docs/decisions/tech-stack.md).

---

## 4. Active build log (update as we ship)

### 2026-06-25 (lane 3 - SANDBOX #23 cont'd: the $0 Preview pane + the procurement inventory)

Founder follow-on: "go with (a)" ŌĆö build the $0 sandboxed-iframe Preview pane behind the seam ŌĆö plus a master spend record. **Feasibility first (queried the Lovable MCP live):** Lovable is NOT a sandbox/compute provider (17 connectors, all MCP integrations, zero code-execution) ŌĆö it only hosts our app, so "ask Lovable for Cloudflare Sandboxes" is impossible; "Lovable-hosted" is automatic and free for any in-app feature. The demo needs no spend: the repo already renders untrusted output in a sandboxed iframe (`p.$slug`). **Built (2nd seam consumer):** a "Preview" tab on the Build session ŌĆö `getStudioPreview` (`studio.functions.ts`, RLS-scoped; selects paths first then reads `new_content` for only the chosen file; prefers `index.html`) returns the changeset's best standalone HTML; `PreviewPanel.tsx` renders it in `<iframe sandbox="allow-scripts allow-forms allow-modals" srcDoc>` (null-origin, can't reach app cookies/APIs ŌĆö the proven prototype-share isolation); the seam gains `previewsBuilds` (floor=false) + `resolveBuildPreview()` so a future microVM upgrades the pane with no edit. Honest empty states. **Gate-green:** tsc 0, bun test 1549 (`provider.test.ts` 17, +2). **3-lens adversarial review (iframe-security+RLS ┬Ę correctness ┬Ę doctrine-UX): 2 ship + 1 blocker FOUND & FIXED** ŌĆö the doctrine lens caught mechanism-leaking user copy ("sandbox backend", "isolated frame", "sandboxed", "stages a changeset") violating engine-room rule 2 (which I'd cited in my own seam comment); re-authored to outcomes ("Live preview", "drafts changes", "appears here when the build produces a standalone page"). Also fixed 2 minors: a stale-query key (now keyed on `changeset.id`) and an unbounded `new_content` read (now paths-first + single-file fetch). Honest known limit: single self-contained HTML only ŌĆö multi-file asset inlining / live multi-file preview is the deferred microVM's job. **Procurement record:** new `docs/operations/procurement-inventory.md` ŌĆö the single shopping list (web-verified 2026-06-25 pricing for 11 vendors: sandbox/embeddings/inference/rerank/Stripe/email/ingest/Lovable/domain), with what/why/cost/vendor/recommendation/when-to-buy; demo runs ~$0, first real spend is Lovable Pro (~$25/mo, custom domain) + Cloudflare Sandbox (~$12/mo). Standing rule added to AGENTS.md ┬¦5 (+ matrix): any new spend/vendor decision updates that sheet in the same unit of work. Decision + the Lovable-later prompt logged in `session-decisions.md`; a postable insight in `brand-feed.md`.

### 2026-06-25 (lane 3 - SANDBOX #23: make the ExecProvider seam load-bearing via a live consumer)

Founder directed: "start with #23 - SANDBOX." The seam (`src/lib/exec/provider.ts`) had been scaffolded (ŌŚÉ, 2026-06-21) but was **parallel** to the real merge gate ŌĆö both it and the chokepoint-pinned `registry.server.ts` read `studio-ci.ts` directly, so the seam was in no decision path. ### 2026-06-24 (lane 2 ŌĆö CORE-UX-FELT ŌŚÉ: harden the wedge's first-run failure path)

**WHY:** v11 #11, the last substantive `ŌŚÉ` slice on the autonomous front. The Critic-teardown wedge is the cold-start FIRST IMPRESSION (name an idea, get a teardown, no setup). Per KI-06 (cold/local environments have no AI key) this path is realistic. _(Untouched Ō¼£ is exhausted: ORCH = Linear key, POS/LANDING = founder copy, REPO-DECLUTTER = lane 1's active doc domain.)_

**Shipped (lane 2):**
- **The classifier** ŌĆö new pure `src/lib/wedge-cold.ts`: `classifyWedgeFailure(message)` sorts a run failure into `cold` (gateway unconfigured/capped ŌĆö reassuring "your idea is safe, try again once connected"), `transient` (network/timeout/5xx/429 ŌĆö "give it a moment and try again"), or `other` (keeps the real message, framed calmly so a genuine bug stays legible). `isGatewayColdError`. 8 tests.
- **The calm first-run** ŌĆö `WedgeTeardown` now classifies the error and shows a calm inline `role="alert"` banner (rose only for `other`), with the form preserved for an immediate retry, instead of a raw technical toast. `onMutate` clears stale failures.

**Verification (ran):** tsc 0, `bun test` 1459/1459 (8 new). **Adversarial review (ts + security):** security CLEAN (no ReDoS ŌĆö all patterns linear; no NEW info-leak ŌĆö the raw message was already shown via `toast.error`; no XSS ŌĆö React escapes the text child). TS folded one MEDIUM: a 429 rate-limit was in COLD but is actually transient (the gateway is connected, it just needs a cooldown) ŌĆö moved to `transient` + softened the transient note to fit both.

**Status ŌŚÉ [~85%] (done on the board):** all three substantive CORE-UX-FELT fixes are now shipped (brief-leads-with-stakes + Today declutter, cycle 9; cold-gateway hardening, now). **Shipped (lane 2):**

- **Wired with zero extra cost** ŌĆö `listGovernApprovals` already fetched the decided history for the per-agent track record; rejected rows ARE decided rows, so it now derives `rejectionsByKey` from that SAME RLS-scoped fetch (no new query) and returns it.
- **At the point of decision** ŌĆö the `ApprovalsPanel` card now shows a quiet "declined N├Ś before" chip on a pending gate whose (agent, tool) the caller has rejected before ŌĆö so the correction registers instead of the agent silently re-asking.

**Verification (ran):** tsc 0, `bun test` 1452/1452 (6 new). **Adversarial review (ts + security):** security CLEAN (tenant-isolation correct ŌĆö only the caller's own rejections, scoped by `user_id` + RLS; the decline reason is computed but never rendered, only the count). ### 2026-06-24 (lane 2 ŌĆö TRUST-VERIFY ŌŚÉ: a normal "Integrity check" for the Trust Ledger, all users, NOT blockchain)

**WHY:** v11 #26, the lowest-rank UNTOUCHED item buildable without founder input (ORCH-DELEGATE needs a Linear key, POS/LANDING are founder-voice copy, DELEGATE-DESK is a product-IA call). Gives every user a way to confirm their decision-and-outcome record has not been altered. _Founder steer mid-build: NO blockchain anywhere now; this is NOT enterprise-only; keep it a normal, simple feature. Reframed accordingly (memory: no-blockchain-trust-integrity)._

**Shipped (lane 2):**
- **The integrity primitive** ŌĆö new pure `src/lib/trust-verify.ts`: a plain SHA-256 hash chain over the ledger records (a CHECKSUM, not a blockchain ŌĆö no chain/tokens/keys/external service). `canonicalizeReceipt` (only integrity-relevant fields; derived `evidenceCount`/`source.label` excluded so the fingerprint does not flap), `sealReceipts` (chain head = the fingerprint, total read-order-independent order), `verifyReceipts` (detects + can pinpoint alter/insert/remove/reorder), `shortHead`. Web Crypto (`crypto.subtle`), works in bun + Workers. 13 tests.
- **Server fns** ŌĆö refactored `trust-ledger.functions.ts` to a shared `loadReceipts` loader (listTrustReceipts behavior preserved, review-confirmed) + `getLedgerSeal` (the current fingerprint) + `verifyLedgerSeal` (check the live record against a saved fingerprint; head validated as exactly 64 hex). RLS-scoped: the fingerprint only ever covers records the caller may already read.
- **The surface** ŌĆö a calm `SealPanel` on `/trust-ledger`: "Integrity check ┬Ę <fingerprint> ┬Ę N records ┬Ę as of <time>", a Copy-fingerprint affordance, and a "paste a saved fingerprint ŌåÆ Unchanged / Changed" verify. Hidden when the ledger is empty (an empty ledger hashes to a fixed constant, so it would be a meaningless match).

**Verification (ran):** tsc 0, `bun test` 1411/1411 (13 new). **Adversarial review (4-lens Workflow ŌĆö crypto-soundness, tamper-completeness, security/RLS, TS+behavior-preservation):** chain cryptographically SOUND, tamper-detection COMPLETE, behavior preservation + circular-import CLEAN. Folded: the empty-ledger genesis-hash guard (count===0), a total-order tie-break, the 64-hex head validator, head-only-live-path documentation. The "co-tenant workspaceId" + "no rate limit" notes are won't-fix-with-rationale (identical to the existing listTrustReceipts surface; RLS is the gate; a non-member gets only the hidden genesis fingerprint).

**Status ŌŚÉ:** the autonomous slice (the fingerprint + verify + surface, all users) is shipped; the OPTIONAL deferred add-ons are an Ed25519 signature (non-repudiation) + persisting the fingerprint at write time (which also lights up per-record pinpointing) ŌĆö both need a provisioned key / write-path migration, and per the founder ruling stay optional, never blockchain, never enterprise-gated.

Root cause: prod's `supabase_migrations.schema_migrations` (78 rows, newest `20260621154025`) tracks **Lovable's own** migration timestamps, NOT the repo's `supabase/migrations/` filenames ŌĆö so the repo migrations and the live schema can silently drift, and this one slipped. The bug was masked because the call site (`listWorkspaceMembers`) degrades gracefully to a null-identity fallback, so the Members list rendered (roles only, no names/emails) with no crash or console error. **The fix:** applied the committed function verbatim to prod via Lovable `query_database` (additive, idempotent `create or replace`, read-only SECURITY DEFINER, `set search_path=public`, execute granted to `authenticated`); confirmed it now exists with the right signature and that its identity-join returns `display_name`/`email` on a real workspace. Members list now renders identities live. **Closure:** dashboard row 16 ŌåÆ Ō£ģ, ledger `done WM-F4`. **Systemic follow-up (logged for the founder):** the repoŌåöprod migration drift is a class risk ŌĆö other committed migrations may also not have reached prod; a drift audit (repo migration objects vs live `pg_proc`/`information_schema`) is the next high-leverage verify-to-close lever. **Branch:** `parallel/lane-2`. **UI breadcrumb:** Settings > Workspace > Members.

**[WM-F1b ┬Ę WM-F2 ┬Ę WM-F3 ┬Ę WM-F6 ┬Ę WM-F9, 2026-06-22, Lane 2 (Opus, ultracode)] Tenancy isolation cluster verified live on prod by a 6-lens adversarial RLS leak-hunt and closed (5├Ś ŌŚÉŌåÆŌ£ģ); FOUND + FIXED one latent prod landmine.** Continuing the partial-closure pass: the whole WM-F tenancy spine was ŌŚÉ "live on publish, verify pending." Now the app is published, so I ran a full **migration-drift + RLS-correctness audit** against prod via the Lovable MCP (`query_database`). **Drift audit:** all 15 tenancy tables (10 WM-F9 isolation + 5 WM-F1/F1b agent) carry `workspace_id` + the `trg_set_*_workspace` filler trigger + RLS-on + Ōēź1 policy, and every function landed (`match_agent_memory`/`recent_agent_reflections` with `for_account` = WM-F2; `move_product` = WM-F6; `has_workspace_role`/`has_account_role`/`is_account_member`; the `prevent_workspace_owner_demotion` trigger fn = WM-F3). **RLS leak-hunt (ultracode Workflow):** 6 independent adversarial security lenses (cross-user, cross-workspace, anon/public, write-path/WITH CHECK, RBAC-escalation, dead-policy) + a synthesis over the LIVE prod policy set -> **0 critical/high, safe_to_close.** The tenancy invariant holds: every in-scope table is a single PERMISSIVE dual-key policy `(auth.uid()=user_id AND is_workspace_member(workspace_id))` in both USING and WITH CHECK, no OR-able widener; co-member reads fail on `A=B`, non-members fail the membership conjunct, anon collapses to no-rows (only the `is_public` prototype shares are anon-readable, column-grant-restricted). **The one real finding (FIXED):** the `accounts` "account members read" policy had drifted to a self-compare `m.account_id = m.id` - root cause is a latent SQL-scoping bug in source `20260619210000` (`m.account_id = id`: the unqualified `id` binds to the inner `account_members.id`, not `accounts.id`). Dead today (0/6 rows self-equal) but a footgun: any future row with `id == account_id` flips the uncorrelated EXISTS to always-true -> full `accounts`-table exposure. Dropped the redundant dead policy on prod (member reads correctly served by the sibling `is_account_member(id)`; verified all 6 owners are account_members so zero read-gap; behavior-preserving) + added the forward-only repo migration `20260622010000_wm_f3_drop_dead_accounts_read_policy.sql` to keep source in lockstep. **Closures:** WM-F1b (NOT NULL/unique-key remain the founder-gated WM-F1c), WM-F2 (behavioral pooling obs needs a paid 2+-workspace account), WM-F3 (drift fixed), WM-F6 (WM-F6b `artifact_lineage` deferred), WM-F9 (isolation core; WM-F9c read-filtering is an additive UX follow-up, not a leak). **Method note (systemic):** this confirms the repoŌåöprod migration-drift risk is real and recurring (WM-F4's members RPC + this accounts policy) - the verify-on-publish discipline is what catches it. **Branch:** `parallel/lane-2`. **UI breadcrumb:** Settings > Workspace (members/invite/roles), sidebar product Ōŗ» > Move to workspace.

**[WM-F8 / WM-F8b, 2026-06-22, Lane 2 (Opus, ultracode - a BUILD slice)] Workspace switch hardening closed (ŌŚÉŌåÆŌ£ģ) with an account-tier cache-reset fix.** Auditing WM-F8's cache-clear-on-switch preserve-list against the app's actual TanStack query-key roots found a real gap: the flat 8-root global allowlist preserved `billing`/`connections`/`integrations` on EVERY switch, but a switch can cross ACCOUNTS (multi-account membership is now reachable via the WM-F5 invites just closed), so a cross-account switch left the previous account's billing/connections cached - a stale cross-account flash. **Built (TDD):** split the allowlist in `src/hooks/workspace-query-scope.ts` into USER-global (`workspaces`/`profile`/`api-keys`/`mcp-tokens`) vs ACCOUNT-global (`billing`/`connections`/`calendar-connections`/`integrations`); added pure `accountChangedOnSwitch(workspaces, from, to)` (proves same-account only when both known + equal `account_id`, else fail-safe to clear, so it never preserves stale cross-account data) + `shouldClearOnWorkspaceSwitch(key, {accountChanged})`; rewired `setActiveWorkspaceId` in `use-workspace.tsx`. A same-account switch is provably byte-identical to before; a cross-account switch additionally clears account-globals; first mount preserves them (gated on `activeWorkspaceId !== null`). 12 scope tests (77 asserts). **Method (ultracode):** a focused adversarial typescript-review -> SHIP_WITH_FIXES, no critical/high; its one medium (account-globals wrongly cleared on first mount under SSR hydration) was FOLDED. **Verification:** tsc 0 in my files; `bun test` 920/920; my files lint-clean (the lone react-refresh warning is pre-existing). The "thread activeWorkspaceId into every query key" belt-and-suspenders is intentionally NOT built (redundant with the cache-clear + account tier; velocity "nothing speculative"). Remaining: the coupled WM-F9c server-side read-filtering (separate item). **Branch:** `parallel/lane-2`. **UI:** AppShell workspace switcher.

**[WM-M12 + credit-engine grant lockdown, 2026-06-22, Lane 2 (Opus, ultracode) ŌĆö CRITICAL pre-go-live billing-security fix] Closed WM-M12 (ŌŚÉŌåÆŌ£ģ) by finding + fixing a credit-mint/drain hole on prod.** The founder lifted the "Lovable-owned/frozen" rule on monetization (engine ~90% built; verify/fix/close it), so I audited the live credit engine's grants. **The gap:** seven SECURITY DEFINER credit-mutation RPCs ŌĆö `debit_account_credits`, `grant_subscription_credits`, `apply_topup_credits`, `reset_subscription_cycle`, `backfill_account_credits`, `_ensure_account_credits`, `check_mission_caps` ŌĆö were **anon/authenticated-EXECUTABLE via PostgREST with NO internal authorization guard** (no `has_role`/`auth.uid`/`auth.role`/`service_role` check; two retained the default PUBLIC grant). They are called ONLY server-side with the service-role client (debit from `runtime.server.ts`; grant/topup/reset from the Stripe `webhook.ts`), confirmed by grepping the call sites. So a client could have `POST /rest/v1/rpc/grant_subscription_credits` to mint itself credits, `apply_topup_credits` to credit without paying, or `debit_account_credits` to drain a victim ŌĆö once metering goes live. Metering is dormant (credits OFF), so no live exploitation, but a critical hole armed for go-live. **The fix (applied on prod + forward migration `20260622020000_credit_rpc_grant_lockdown.sql`):** `revoke execute ... from public, anon, authenticated` + `grant execute ... to service_role` on all 7; verified on prod all 7 are now `anon=false/auth=false/service_role=true` so the chokepoint + webhook still work but no client can. Also revoked the unused anon/auth SELECT grant on the `account_billing_secrets`/`workspace_billing_secrets` vaults (RLS-locked already; defense-in-depth). **Documented-not-fixed:** the `stripe_customer_id`/`stripe_subscription_id` columns still report anon-readable at the column level, but RLS denies anon every row (no live leak); a true column lockdown needs the invasive revoke-table-then-grant-column-list pattern, left as an RLS-mitigated follow-up. **Same lockdown secures** WM-M3 (grant/topup/reset rails), WM-M13 (top-up), WM-M14 (caps). **Method note:** same repoŌåöprod drift class as WM-F4/WM-F3 ŌĆö the secure posture was assumed but not live; empirical prod grant-audit caught it. **Coord:** this falls in Lane 1's held M-C-DB-HYGIENE scope ŌĆö the prod fix + migration are idempotent, flagged so they fold it, no duplication harm. WM-M12 Ō£ģ: engine built + dry-run-verified + now SECURE; live activation is the founder's key-dependency (live Stripe keys + the go-live flag). **Branch:** `parallel/lane-2`.

Lexical-only suspicion can at most `flag` (kept, still fenced+escaped). Folded: the structural-signal gate (the fix), presence-cap, homoglyph fold, encoding-evasion tightening, vocabulary broadening + an exfil-channel signal, and quarantine telemetry; re-probed the reviewer's exact strings to confirm benign content is now allow/flag (never stripped) while real fence-breakout/forged-turn attacks quarantine. **Verification (what I ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bun test` 647/647 (29 in `injection-classifier.test.ts`, incl. an explicit over-redaction regression suite); `bun run build` red = the pre-existing Lovable vite-config ESM-cycle baseline (`ERR_REQUIRE_ESM` at config-load, before any of my source) + Node 20.9.0 < Vite's 20.19, proven not mine. **ŌŚÉ not Ō£ģ:** built + gate-green + reviewed + driven, but the live quarantine renders + behaviorally verifies on the founder's next publish (a real fence-breakout chunk stripped in a `/chat` answer). **Deliberate follow-ups (documented, not hidden):** FND-0.7-b cross-chunk aggregation (a payload split across chunks stays sub-threshold), FND-0.7-c apply the seam to the reactor `untrusted_signal` ingest path (higher-trust-risk than first-party RAG), FND-0.7-d a governance UI to view/tune the classifier. **Branch:** `parallel/lane-3` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **UI breadcrumb:** none (runtime, behind the RAG retriever). **[H2-WRITES, 2026-06-21 02:20, Lane 0] Outcome-roadmap GOVERNED commit path shipped (ŌŚÉ).** Advances the H2 outcome roadmap from a lenient kanban toward governed outcome curation (the v6 anti-feature-factory thesis): a Now/Next/Later commitment must carry a declared outcome AND measure. **Pick rationale (Lane 0, parallel):** with Lane 0's Monetization/Credit rows all founder-gated (Stripe/pricing/taste) or design-pass and the Decision Brain founder-gated/other-lane, this was the highest-priority eligible non-gated unclaimed item (P1, Decide), advancing the autonomous-execution North Star (a governed write path the agent can commit roadmap changes through). **What shipped:** new pure `src/lib/roadmap-governance.ts` (`isCommitmentGoverned`/`validateCommitment`/`findGovernanceGaps`/`governanceGapCount` + the `RoadmapBucket` type, 8 unit tests) - the single governance rule both the write path and the surface read; a new `commitRoadmapItem` server fn in `roadmap.functions.ts` (atomic bucket+outcome+measure write that REJECTS a bucketed commitment lacking outcome/measure, mirroring `updateRoadmapItem`'s RLS hardening: `.eq(user_id)` + `.select()` + loud 0-row throw; trims blanks to null so the governance read stays honest); `getRoadmap` now also returns `governanceGaps` (count of ungoverned commitments). The board (`RoadmapBoard.tsx`) routes the outcome-save through the governed path, shows a calm gap-count header line, and leads each ungoverned committed card with an ember `VerdictChip` ("Needs outcome"). **Design decision (the lenient/strict split):** the drag/select MOVE stays unconstrained (`updateRoadmapItem`) so you can still place an item first; the governance binds at the SAVE of the outcome and at the gap surface, so the UX is non-breaking but a commitment can never be SAVED half-declared. **Design pass (founder front-end ruling):** ran `impeccable` against the Ember Editorial DESIGN.md - it corrected my first cut (a recolored ember link, which risks reading as a CTA) to the canonical `VerdictChip` per the verdict-chip ruling ("a needs-human judgment leads with a chip, don't bury it"); role-color law honored (ember = needs-human), no banned pattern (no hero-metric/card-grid/gradient), header is a plain calm sentence. **Verification (what I ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on the 4 touched files (after prettier); `bun run build` Ō£ō (Node 26; session Node 20.9 < Vite floor = environmental); `bun test` 446/446 (8 new governance tests). Adversarial self-review (additive, non-destructive, so no multi-agent workflow): governed fn matches the hardened update pattern; the widened `getRoadmap` return only feeds the board; the optimistic-move header flicker self-heals on refetch; behavior change (can't save a committed item's outcome half-declared, and clearing requires moving to backlog first) is the intended governance, surfaced via a clear toast. **ŌŚÉ not Ō£ģ:** the governed write + validation + gap surface are built + unit-verified + design-passed + gate-green, but render on the founder's publish (not render-verified locally), and the autonomous agent-commit wiring + a richer write surface remain. **Branch:** `parallel/lane-0` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **UI breadcrumb:** /roadmap (the product roadmap board). Detail: [`docs/features/h2-writes.md`](./docs/features/h2-writes.md). **Next (Lane 0):** continue the ledger loop.

**[DATA-RETENTION-b, 2026-06-21 01:48, Lane 0] Right-to-be-forgotten erase cascade shipped (ŌŚÉ, dormant).** The destructive other half of `DATA-RETENTION` (c47 shipped the time-based telemetry purge; that migration's header explicitly named this follow-up). Closes the `considerations.md` Data/Privacy P1 gap "Data retention + deletion (GDPR/CCPA right-to-be-forgotten)" and completes the data-governance triad with U6-AUDIT (c48) + SUBPROC-DISCLOSURE (c49). **Pick rationale (Lane 0, parallel build):** Lane 0's preferred Monetization/Credit rows are nearly all founder-gated (Stripe/pricing/taste) or design-pass; roaming by strategic impact, this is the cleanest highest-impact non-gated item - a self-contained, dormant, dry-run-verifiable migration + pure TS, file-disjoint (low collision), squarely in Lane 0's migration/server-fn strength. **What shipped:** `supabase/migrations/20260621012900_data_retention_b_right_to_erasure.sql` - `right_to_erasure_enabled()` (dormant flag, false) + `forget_workspace`/`forget_account` + read-only `erasure_residue` + the internal `_erasure_delete_by_column` engine; plus pure `src/lib/compliance/erasure.ts` (`summarizeErasure` receipt + `isErasureComplete`) + tests. **Design - a dynamic, FK-order-agnostic, single-tenant delete:** the engine lists every public BASE TABLE carrying the tenant column from `information_schema` (auto-covers all 61 `workspace_id` tables + any added later - no hand-list to rot), then deletes `where <col> = $1` per table in a fixed-point retry loop that resolves FK ordering with no hand-maintained topo sort, bounded + raises if anything can't clear (never silently incomplete). **Why not a naive `delete from workspaces` (verified on the live schema):** of the 61 `workspace_id` FKs, 22 are CASCADE, 22 RESTRICT, 6 SET NULL - a bare parent delete would be BLOCKED by the 22 RESTRICT children and would merely NULL the 6 SET NULL (the agent moat: `agent_memory`/`agents`/`agent_runs`/`agent_tools`/`agent_run_checkpoints` + `idempotency_keys`), leaving data present-but-unlinked (the worst erasure outcome). The explicit sweep erases every tenant row regardless of FK action. **Safety:** single-tenant by construction (every delete is `where <col> = $1` with the id bound as a parameter AND `_col` whitelisted to `workspace_id|account_id`); no injection surface (catalog-sourced, `quote_ident`'d); ships INERT (the primitive self-gates on the flag too); execute service-role-only (operator/DPO action, not self-serve). **Adversarial review (HARD GATE 4) - a 4-lens Workflow** (sql-fk-correctness CLEAN; tenant-isolation; gdpr-completeness; ts-receipt): folded all 4 must-fix - (1) the `_col` whitelist (the most serious: an uncontrolled `_col` would let a typo/compromised service-role caller delete cross-tenant, since SECURITY DEFINER bypasses RLS - the whitelist makes "single-tenant by construction" actually enforced); (2) `isErasureComplete` null-residue crash guard (the exact on-publish verification path); (3) the primitive's own dormancy gate (so "Ships INERT" is total); (4) a structural `isAccount` discriminator. Added tests for the null-residue + discriminator-confusion cases. The 6 GDPR-completeness findings are genuine but stated scope boundaries (this is TENANT-data erasure, not PERSON erasure) ŌåÆ documented as DATA-RETENTION-c. **Verification (what I ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on the new files; `bun run build` Ō£ō (Node 26; the session default Node 20.9 is below Vite's floor - environmental, not the change; my new files import into nothing, so they are provably out of the build graph); `bun test` 398/398 (11 new erasure tests). **Zero-destruction live dry-run on the real prod schema** (Lovable MCP, `BEGIN..ROLLBACK`): created the functions, set the flag true, ran the engine for both `workspace_id` + `account_id` against a random non-existent uuid (every delete = 0 rows) + `erasure_residue` - all clean (`{passes:1,tables:{}}`, residue `{}`), proving the dynamic discovery + `quote_ident` over every real table + whitelist + dormancy gate + loop termination all work live, then `ROLLBACK` (prod untouched). **ŌŚÉ not Ō£ģ:** tenant-data erasure built + dormant + offline-gated + zero-destruction-dry-run-verified, but it is NOT person-level GDPR Art. 17 (auth.users / `user_id`-only rows / Supabase Storage objects / account-scope residue ŌåÆ DATA-RETENTION-c), and the DESTRUCTIVE FK-order dry-run on a workspace WITH rows + live activation (flag flip + operator invoke) are publish-verify. **Branch:** `parallel/lane-0` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **UI breadcrumb:** none (operator/DPO RPC; a gated DPO console is DATA-RETENTION-c). Detail: [`docs/features/right-to-erasure.md`](./docs/features/right-to-erasure.md). **Next (Lane 0):** continue the ledger loop - re-sync, reap, claim the next highest-impact non-gated row.

**[O1 / DBR-1 v1, 2026-06-20] The knowledge-graph explorer shipped (parallel/knowledge lane).** The remaining slice of `O1` (the typed graph explorer over the provenance walk) is now built, as the first lane-built increment of the Decision Brain (DBR-1 v1, the "B+" cut, founder-enriched + approved this session). Spec: [`docs/features/knowledge-graph-explorer.md`](./docs/features/knowledge-graph-explorer.md). It DERIVES a typed `{nodes, edges}` graph deterministically from the existing `artifact_lineage` (no LLM extraction, no new tables, migration-free, fail-safe), rendered as a bounded, Obsidian-style visual graph at `/knowledge?tab=graph`: nodes color-coded by kind and sized by influence, pan/zoom, click-a-node-for-its-story (reusing `getLineage`/`getProvenance`), a truthful "as of" time axis over real edge `created_at`, and the `supersedes`/`contradicts` + `validTo` supersession SEAM laid in empty and ready (so the future inference engine renders with zero UI change). Pure core `src/lib/knowledge-graph-explorer.ts` (+`.test.ts`, 13 TDD tests: typing, rings, influence, bounding, time filter, supersession classification, fail-safe), server fn `src/lib/knowledge-graph-explorer.functions.ts` (RLS-scoped bounded both-ways walk, batched `.in()`, a fresh empty graph on any error), UI `src/components/knowledge/{GraphExplorer,GraphNodeStory,GraphPanel}.tsx`, route `_authenticated.knowledge.tsx` (new `graph` tab + `?focusKind`/`?focusId`). **Why B+ and not the full graph:** the bi-temporal supersession ENGINE (inferring `contradicts`/`supersedes` from outcomes) needs an AI write-path = recurring spend + the AI chokepoint, both founder-gated and out of this lane, so it is the explicit next DBR increment; v1 ships the visual + read substrate against a schema already shaped for it. **Gate:** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bun test` 328/328 (13 new); `bun run build` green; an adversarial review found and fixed a shared empty-graph singleton and added `.in()` batching, with a non-blocking `filterByTime` maxRing-gap logged as debt. **[WM-M10, 2026-06-19 15:58, overnight cycle 29] credit unit + cost-to-credit conversion + the calm legibility layer (Ō£ģ; pure module, fully unit-tested).** Added the credit metering math to `src/lib/ai/pricing.ts` (+ a new `pricing.test.ts`), the "what one credit is" the dormant `WM-M4` seam was waiting for. **What it does:** `CREDIT_COGS_USD` (the USD of blended COGS one credit represents; margin lives in grant-sizing, not the per-credit price; founder-tunable placeholder, ┬¦7) + an optional per-model `MODEL_CREDIT_RATE`/`creditRateFor` (defaults to 1 = pure COGS pass-through); `creditsForCost(estCostUsd, model) = ceil(estCostUsd / CREDIT_COGS_USD * rate)`, which is **0 for a non-billable call** (zero / negative / non-finite cost) and **never 0 for a billable one** (a positive cost always rounds up to >= 1 credit, margin-positive); `estimateCreditsForCall(model, prompt, completion)` composes the existing `estimateCostUsd` so the projection and the real post-call debit share one source of truth; and the **legibility layer** `actionCreditRange(actionKind)` returning a display-only `{min,max}` credit range per user-facing action (chat_reply / research / prd_draft / mission_step / embedding), derived by running calibrated representative token shapes through the SAME conversion so the shown range can never contradict the real meter (unknown kinds get a safe non-alarming default; never rendered as a flat charge). **Decisions (logged in session-decisions):** `actionCreditRange` is a PURE function (no DB, no `ai_events` query) to honor the "no DB, pricing.ts only" scope, the spec's "historical averages" being the future calibration source (WM-M16), not a live read; the numbers are documented ┬¦7 placeholders, the mechanism is final; `MODEL_CREDIT_RATE` ships empty (pure COGS pass-through) since no model needs a non-1 rate yet. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bun test src/lib/ai/pricing.test.ts` 15/15 pass (29 assertions: billable-floor, 0-for-non-billable, NaN/Infinity guard, monotonicity, premium > cheap, estimator composition, legibility ordering + consistency); `bunx tsc --noEmit` exit 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on both files; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.13s); humanization scan 0 hits. Adversarial review found no real fix (the never-0 invariant holds; Infinity/NaN ŌåÆ 0 credits; `actionCreditRange` returns a COPY of the default so callers cannot mutate the shared const; no overclaim, this is the credit LIBRARY and WM-M12 drives it into the live seam). **Marked Ō£ģ (not ŌŚÉ):** behavior is actually verified by the passing unit tests, no publish needed (a pure module, like WM-M1). **UI breadcrumb:** none yet (library; surfaces in the WM-M16 credit UI). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F1b, or now-unblocked WM-M11 (per-tier grant; needs WM-M2 + WM-M10, both done) / WM-M15 (margin levers; needs WM-M10).

**[WM-M15, 2026-06-19 18:09, overnight cycle 34] cost-aware model routing margin lever (ŌŚÉ; pure router Ō£ģ, the live routing config-gated; cache half split to WM-M15b).** The structural margin discipline: with no self-serve BYOK the platform eats LLM COGS, so routing routine work to a cheaper model keeps credits margin-positive. **What it does:** a new pure module `src/lib/ai/routing.ts` (`blendedPrice` ranks by the in+out price mean; and `eval`'s subject call IS the model under test, so routing would corrupt the benchmark. **Folded ALL 7 findings:** narrowed the routable set to `{brief, scheduler, test}` (judge/eval/embed removed) AND added a TIER GUARD (never downgrade a deliberately-chosen reasoning/premium/code/vision model, nor an unknown one), so even a routable surface only downgrades a fast/balanced request; plus the credit-coherence fixes (the pre-call halt now projects `effectiveModel` so it cannot falsely over-block, and the debit meters the credit rate on `modelUsed`, the model actually run, matching the est_cost_usd basis). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bun test src/lib/ai/routing.test.ts` 12/12 (tier guard + wedge/benchmark exclusions + cheapest-floor + unknown-model + no-sideways); the bigger lever is the WM-M15b cache. **UI breadcrumb:** none (chokepoint plumbing). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F1b (moat hardening) or WM-M15b (response cache) or WM-M5 (tier limit gates).

**[WM-F9, 2026-06-19 18:49, overnight cycle 35] tenancy isolation hardening + scope-leak audit (ŌŚÉ; migration dry-run-verified on prod, live isolation on publish).** Closed a latent cross-workspace scope-leak class. **What it does:** migration `20260619190000_wm_f9_isolation_scope.sql` adds `workspace_id` (FK `ON DELETE CASCADE`) + a deterministic backfill (`ensure_user_default_workspace(user_id)`) + a shared `set_row_workspace_from_user` BEFORE-INSERT trigger + NOT NULL + an index + a **DUAL-KEY** RLS policy `auth.uid() = user_id AND is_workspace_member(workspace_id)` to **10 tables**. **[WM-M5, 2026-06-19 19:30, overnight cycle 36] tier limit gates (ŌŚÉ; trigger behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod, gate ships dormant).** Turns the entitlements matrix (WM-M1, shipped) from feature-flags-only into enforced caps on product + workspace creation. **[WM-F1b, 2026-06-19 20:10, overnight cycle 37] agent-workspace isolation hardening (ŌŚÉ; migration dry-run-verified on prod, live isolation on publish).** The moat-hardening half of WM-F1: WM-F1 made recall workspace-aware but left the agent TABLES on the pre-tenancy owner-only RLS and let the non-loop insert paths land memory untagged. Strategic pick of the cycle: among the unblocked candidates (WM-F3 / WM-M15b / WM-F1b) it is the only one that directly advances the named memory/decision moat, and it finishes a partial. **What it does:** migration `20260619220000_wm_f1b_agent_workspace_hardening.sql` adds a `user_id`-fed BEFORE-INSERT trigger (`set_row_workspace_from_user`, reused from WM-F9, service-role-safe because it sources `NEW.user_id` not `auth.uid()`) to all 5 agent tables (`agents`, `agent_memory`, `agent_tools`, `agent_runs`, `agent_approvals`) so EVERY insert path is workspace-tagged at the DB layer (the `seed_default_agents` SQL function, the `memory.remember` tool, any service-role writer) without hand-editing a single app insert; plus a DUAL-KEY membership RLS (`auth.uid() = user_id AND is_workspace_member(workspace_id)`) replacing the owner-only `auth.uid() = user_id` policy on all 5. Code: `registry.server.ts` `memoryRemember` now tags the ACTIVE workspace (pre-migration-tolerant post-insert update, mirroring `rememberOutcome`), so a multi-workspace user's explicit memories land in the active workspace, not just the default. **Decisions (session-decisions):** (1) picked WM-F1b for strategic impact (the moat is the one North-Star item among the three candidates), navigating its risk with the proven WM-F9 patterns. (2) **Universal insert tagging via a DB trigger, not the bible's per-file audit**, editing the ~6 insert paths is fragile (easy to miss one, several are SQL/service-role), whereas the trigger guarantees every insert is tagged; strictly more robust. (3) **Dual-key, not pure membership**, the recall RPCs are user-scoped + workspace-narrowed, so the table RLS must match (a teammate must not read another member's raw memory); the dual key is strictly MORE restrictive than the prior owner-only policy, so it can never widen access or lock the owner out (`ensure_user_default_workspace` inserts a `workspace_members` row in every branch, so every backfilled row's workspace has the owner as a member). (4) **DEFERRED to WM-F1c:** NOT NULL on `workspace_id` (WM-F1's `ON DELETE SET NULL` preserves the moat across workspace deletion; NOT NULL forces `ON DELETE CASCADE` = irreversible memory loss on workspace delete, a founder-gated product call, the trigger + backfill already enforce isolation without the constraint), the `agents UNIQUE(user_id,slug) ŌåÆ UNIQUE(workspace_id,slug)` swap (verified `seed_default_agents()` uses `ON CONFLICT (user_id, slug)`, so the swap would break onboarding's seed unless its conflict target is recreated; it also couples to the WM-F8 roster read; low value with no multi-member workspaces yet, and unverifiable offline), and the types regen (the schema is not published, so a regen would emit pre-WM types). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` 0; `bun run build` Ō£ō; `bun test` 252/252; humanization scan clean on both authored files; AND a two-pass `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (via the Lovable MCP): applied WM-F1's column essentials then the full WM-F1b, 5 filler triggers + 5 dual-key policies created, **0 old owner-only policies remaining** (the dual-key actually enforces, no permissive-policy-wins bug), the trigger fills `workspace_id` on an insert that omits it (= the user's default workspace), `seed_default_agents` still succeeds (`ON CONFLICT` intact), `is_workspace_member(null) = false` (orphaned rows correctly hidden), and a **simulated-JWT read as a real owner returned all 23 of their `agent_memory` rows, no reader breakage**; a direct check found **0 memory-owners without a `workspace_members` row**; rolled back, then re-confirmed prod is untouched (still the old `own agent_memory all` policy, no `workspace_id` column, 0 triggers). Adversarial self-review folded 2 humanization fixes (em dashes in my own new comments); the highest-risk concern (owner locked out by the dual key) was disproved by reading `ensure_user_default_workspace` (it always ensures membership) + the live read. **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real prod schema, but the LIVE isolation activates only on the founder's next publish, so it is not verifiable on the published app until then. **UI breadcrumb:** none (RLS plumbing). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F3 (RBAC enforcement) or WM-M15b (response cache).

**[WM-M15b + WM-M15b-fix, 2026-06-19, overnight cycles 38-39] response cache shipped, then its 3 runtime-fatal bugs fixed (ŌŚÉ).** WM-M15b (the cache half of the WM-M15 margin lever) was shipped by a PARALLEL session (`796513d181`): a content-hash `ai_response_cache` table (7-day TTL) read/written at the AI chokepoint, with a conservative surface whitelist (`brief`/`scheduler`/`test`) and guardrails required. This cycle (39) had independently picked the same item and was building it in the worktree; the per-cycle `origin/main` sync caught the collision after the parallel push, so instead of a duplicate this became the **fix** (`7897085004`), because the shipped version was tsc/build-green but broken at runtime in three ways. **(1) Migration FATAL:** `CREATE INDEX ... WHERE expires_at > now()` is rejected by Postgres (`now()` is STABLE; index predicates require IMMUTABLE), so the migration would have FAILED to apply on the founder's next publish. Verified live: the broken DDL returns `ERROR: 42P17` on the prod DB; the corrected plain-index DDL applies cleanly (throwaway-table dry-run, dropped); the real `ai_response_cache` is confirmed not-yet-applied, so editing the migration in place is correct (a new migration could not help, since the broken `...230000` would run first and fail). **(2) Cache no-op FATAL:** `callModel` ran the provider retry loop unconditionally even on a cache hit (the `if(!cacheHit)` guard wrapped only the cache-write), so the cache saved zero COGS; the provider call is now skipped on a hit. **(3) readCache always missed:** it passed the literal string `"now()"` to `.gte("expires_at")`, which Postgres cannot cast to timestamptz, so every read errored; now `new Date().toISOString()`. **Also hardened:** `generateCacheKey` switched to Web Crypto (`crypto.subtle`, the `rag/indexer.server.ts` pattern) off a bare-`"crypto"` dynamic import whose Worker runtime was unverifiable (and would have crashed every cacheable call if it failed to resolve); `writeCache` now stores under `effectiveModel` + skips fallback responses so later reads keyed by `(model, cache_key)` stay consistent; the `supabase` params are typed (`SupabaseClient`, no-explicit-any). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.33s); `bunx eslint` 0 on the 3 files; `bun test src/lib/ai/cache.test.ts` 10/10; AND the prod migration dry-run above (broken DDL fails with 42P17, fixed DDL applies + drops cleanly). Adversarial self-review confirmed definite-assignment of `providerOut`, `lastErr` scope, no double-write on a hit, `via="cache"` preserved, and complete NOT-NULL inserts. **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** the migration now applies and the cache control-flow is correct, but live cache-serving activates only on the founder's next publish. **Lesson:** a green tsc/build does not cover a migration's apply-time validity or a cache-skip control-flow path; the K2-class floor (the prod migration dry-run + the runtime-fatal review) is exactly what caught all three. **UI breadcrumb:** none (AI chokepoint). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F2 (account-level memory pooling) or WM-F4/F5 (ownership transfer + invites).

**[WM-F2-fix, 2026-06-19 22:05, overnight cycle 40] restored the security + correctness invariants the shipped WM-F2 regressed (ŌŚÉ; behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod).** The WM-F2 ship above (`18db474d3b`, by a PARALLEL session) was tsc/build-green but rewrote the recall RPCs in a way that REGRESSED the WM-F1 baseline it replaced, and its "Acceptance criteria verified / no cross-account leak / no runtime-fatal bug" claim was not borne out. rolled back, then prod re-confirmed untouched (accounts/columns absent, recall fn reverted to its pre-WM 3-arg signature). **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** correct + behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real prod schema; **[WM-F3-fix, 2026-06-19 22:20, overnight cycle 41] the shipped RBAC migration used invalid `create policy if not exists` and would have failed to apply on publish (ŌŚÉ; dry-run-verified on prod).** NOT a collision: a PROACTIVE adversarial review of the recently-shipped SECURITY DEFINER / RLS migrations (the highest-risk parallel-built code), prompted by two prior broken parallel ships (WM-M15b, WM-F2). It found the THIRD broken ship: the WM-F3 RBAC migration (`2b1c429591`, by a parallel session) used `create policy if not exists` for all four account/account_members policies. **Postgres `CREATE POLICY` has NO `IF NOT EXISTS` clause** (unlike `CREATE TABLE`/`INDEX`), so this is a hard syntax error (`ERROR: 42601`); the migration would have FAILED to apply on the founder's next publish, blocking the entire migration run. `tsc`/`build` were green because it is pure SQL, and the shipped dashboard row claimed "verified: tsc/test/build green". **Fix (`70c0ca7db5`):** all four `create policy if not exists "X"` are now `drop policy if exists "X"` + `create policy "X"` (valid + idempotent; the four names differ from WM-M2's account policies, so no name collision and no double-grant beyond the harmless redundant SELECTs), and the `prevent_workspace_owner_demotion` trigger is now `drop trigger if exists` + `create` so the migration is genuinely re-runnable as its header claims. **Verification (what I actually ran):** confirmed on the LIVE prod DB via `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` (stubbing the unpublished WM-M2 `accounts`/`account_members` deps): a `create policy if not exists` probe errors with `42601`; the corrected full migration applies cleanly (the 6 RBAC helper functions + the 5 policies + the demotion trigger all created); rolled back, then prod re-confirmed untouched (the real `"ws owner manage"` policy I dropped inside the txn was restored, stub tables + `has_workspace_role` absent). Also DATA-checked the new role-keyed `"ws owner admin manage"` policy for owner-lockout: all 7 workspaces have their owner as a `workspace_members(role='owner')` row (0 lockouts), so swapping `owner_id = auth.uid()` for `has_workspace_role(id, ['owner','admin'])` locks no current owner out. `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.12s); full `bun test` 270/270 (SQL-only change, TS untouched). **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** the migration now applies and the owner-lockout is disproven on current data, but live RBAC enforcement activates only on the founder's publish. **Lesson:** three consecutive parallel ships (WM-M15b, WM-F2, WM-F3) were tsc/build-green but carried a publish-blocking migration, a cross-user security regression, and an unappliable migration; the standing response is now to proactively review every parallel-shipped SECURITY DEFINER / RLS / migration before the founder publishes, not only the item this loop is itself building. **UI breadcrumb:** none (RLS plumbing). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F4/F5 (ownership transfer + invites) or a continued review sweep of the remaining unverified-by-me ŌŚÉ migrations.
