Built the backend only, per the founder ruling (keep building backend, batch UI to the design pass). **What it does:** migration `20260619260000_wm_f5_invitations.sql` adds a `workspace_invitations` table (DB-generated `token` default, `role` admin/member/viewer, `status` pending/accepted/revoked/expired, 7-day `expires_at`) with manager-only RLS (`can_manage_workspace` from WM-F3; crucially the invitee has NO direct SELECT, so a pending invitation never leaks workspace data to a non-member) + a SECURITY DEFINER `accept_workspace_invitation(_token)` RPC. New `src/lib/email.server.ts` (`sendInviteEmail`, a graceful no-op that always returns the copy-paste link). New `inviteMember`/`listInvitations`/`revokeInvitation`/`acceptInvitation` server fns in `workspaces.functions.ts`. **Decisions:** (1) the accept path is a definer RPC, not RLS, because the invitee is not a member yet, so membership RLS would block the read; (2) the token is bound to the invited email (the signed-in user's `auth.users.email` must match the invitation) so a leaked or forwarded token cannot be redeemed by a different account; (3) single-use via a `FOR UPDATE` lock + a `status` flip to `accepted` (a second accept hits the `status <> 'pending'` guard, which is also how revoke takes effect: a revoked token is no longer pending); (4) outbound email is a founder-gated no-op (the link fallback always works), so invites function without an email provider and nothing is sent without the founder; (5) the join route (`/join/$token`) + the Settings members UI are deferred to the design pass. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on both files; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.07s); full `bun test` 270/270; AND a `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` behavioral dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (stubbing WM-F3's `can_manage_workspace`): inviting a real user's email (`demo@redcadence.app`) for workspace A then accepting as that user (simulated via `request.jwt.claims`) added them to the workspace with `role=member` and flipped the invitation to `accepted`; a second accept was rejected ("This invitation is no longer valid."), a token whose invited email differed from the caller was rejected ("This invitation was sent to a different email address."), and an expired token was rejected ("This invitation has expired."); rolled back, then prod re-confirmed untouched (the table + RPC absent, the seeded membership gone). **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** the table + RPC + server fns are built and behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real prod schema, but the join route + Settings UI are deferred, and live invites activate on the founder's publish (WM-F5 depends on the unpublished WM-M2 + WM-F3, the latter as fixed in `70c0ca7db5` so `can_manage_workspace` exists ŌĆö without that fix the whole migration run would have failed before reaching WM-F5). **UI breadcrumb (once UI ships):** Settings > Team > Invite, and a public `/join/$token` accept page. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F6 (move product between workspaces) or WM-F7/F8 (settings IA, switch hardening) backend.

**[WM-F8, 2026-06-19 23:18, overnight cycle 45] workspace switch hardening ŌĆö query-cache reset (ŌŚÉ; core cache-hygiene shipped + gate-green + driven, full no-flash payoff scales with server-side read-filtering).** The bug: `setActiveWorkspaceId` in `src/hooks/use-workspace.tsx` mutated React state on a workspace switch but never touched the TanStack Query cache, so any workspace-scoped query whose key omits the workspace id kept serving the PREVIOUS workspace's cached rows until it happened to refetch ŌĆö a stale-data flash that "reads like a leak" (the spec's exact framing), and worse for inactive queries (navigating to a not-yet-mounted page after a switch surfaced the old workspace's cache). **What it does:** on a real switch (`id !== activeWorkspaceId`), `setActiveWorkspaceId` now calls `queryClient.removeQueries({predicate})` to clear every workspace-scoped cache entry ŌĆö active AND inactive ŌĆö so nothing stale renders and active observers refetch under the new workspace context; a new pure module `src/hooks/workspace-query-scope.ts` (`GLOBAL_QUERY_KEY_ROOTS` + `isWorkspaceScopedQueryKey`) is the allowlist that PRESERVES the user/account-global queries (`workspaces` list, `profile`, `billing`, `connections`, `calendar-connections`, `integrations`, `api-keys`, `mcp-tokens`) and fails safe to "workspace-scoped" for any unlisted or non-string root, so a newly-added query is isolated by default. **Decisions:** (1) chose the single-site cache reset over threading `activeWorkspaceId` into ~40 query keys ŌĆö the one switch chokepoint catches every workspace-scoped query (including the un-keyed ones) in one surgical, offline-verifiable change, whereas the per-key approach is a sprawling ~40-file diff easy to miss one of; the per-key work is logged as defense-in-depth follow-up WM-F8b. (2) `removeQueries` (not `invalidateQueries`) because invalidate keeps the stale data visible during the background refetch ŌĆö the exact flash we're killing ŌĆö while remove clears it so observers show loading then fetch fresh. (3) exact-match Set membership (not a prefix test) so `workspace-bindings`/`workspace-brief` are correctly treated as workspace-scoped, never confused with the global `workspaces` key. (4) extracted the predicate into its own React/supabase-free module so the unit test runs without initializing the supabase client (which reads env at module load). **Adversarial review (HARD GATE 4):** no runtime-fatal bug ŌĆö `useQueryClient()` is safe (the same component already calls `useQuery`, so a provider exists); the Case-1 stale-closure-refetch risk is absent (keyed queries like `["swarm","hud",activeWorkspaceId]` refetch on key change; server-fn queries like `() => fMissions()` hold no client workspace closure); driven by the AppShell switcher (`AppShell.tsx:516`) + create/delete paths, so not staged-but-never-wired; the guard avoids needless clears on a same-workspace re-select. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` on the 3 touched files = 0 errors (1 pre-existing `react-refresh` warning on the untouched `useWorkspace` export); `bun run build` Ō£ō (4.28s); `bun test` 274/274 (4 new in `workspace-query-scope.test.ts`). **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** the cache reset is correct, gate-green, and driven, BUT most server-fn reads are still user-scoped server-side today (e.g. `missions.functions.ts` / `guardrails.functions.ts` reference no `workspace_id`), so the full user-visible "no cross-workspace flash" lands as reads become workspace-filtered (WM-F9b); and the two-seeded-workspace Playwright assertion needs a publish. No live behavioral test of the switch was run, so not Ō£ģ. **UI breadcrumb:** AppShell > workspace switcher. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F6 (move product between workspaces) or WM-M9 (remove self-serve BYOK).
**[F-BUILDER-MULTIFILE, 2026-06-19 23:39, parallel/build lane cycle 1] Scoped multi-file build: pre-declared touch list + max-files cap on a Studio changeset (ŌŚÉ; pure logic unit-tested, server+UI gate-green, live-verify pending publish + migration sync).** The thin slice of I1: a scope contract over a multi-file changeset so a session stays inside its sanctioned blast radius before the confirm-gated commit. **What it does:** additive migration `20260619270000_studio_multifile_constraints.sql` (a mission-keyed `studio_changeset_constraints` table ŌĆö `allowed_paths text[]` + `max_files int` ŌĆö RLS mirrored from `studio_changesets`: workspace-member read, owner write); pure, unit-tested logic in `src/lib/ai/studio-hunks.ts` (`matchesTouchList` exact/dir-prefix/`*`+`**` globs, `evaluateFileSetPolicy` in/out-of-policy split + over-cap count, `applyChangesetHunkSelections` cross-file merge primitive); server fns in `studio.functions.ts` (`setChangesetConstraints` declare/clear mission-keyed, `enforceTouchList` drop out-of-scope staged files, `dispatchStudioSession` optional pre-declaration, `getStudioSession` returns `constraints` + `fileSetPolicy`); and a `Build > session > Changes > Scope` card (live in/out-of-scope + over-cap status, touch-list editor + max-files input, one-click "Apply scope", per-file "out of scope" badge). **Decisions:** (1) enforcement is operator-layer, not agent-tool ŌĆö the agent's `studio.stage`/`studio.commit` tools live in the forbidden chokepoint (`tools/registry.server.ts`), so the human curates against the policy before approving the commit; staying strictly in lane. (2) The cap is a warning, never an auto-drop (which files to shed is the operator's call). (3) The changeset-wide "merge across files" stays a pure tested helper, NOT a server endpoint, since the operator path drives per-file curation via the existing `applyStagedHunkSelection` ŌĆö an un-driven server fn would be a "staged but never driven" gap (caught + removed in adversarial review). (4) `getStudioSession`'s constraints read degrades to an unconstrained policy if the table is unsynced (pre-migration window), so the session read never errors. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on all 5 changed files; `bun test src/lib/ai/studio-hunks.test.ts` 24/24 (58 asserts) covering glob edge cases (single vs double star, dir prefix, zero-segment globstar), policy split + over-cap, and cross-file merge; full studio suite 56/56; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.09s); authored-diff scan for em/en dashes + control bytes 0 hits. NOT a behavioral live test (the agent loop + the new migration cannot run locally ŌĆö no AI key, table syncs via Lovable on publish), so marked **ŌŚÉ**, not Ō£ģ. **UI breadcrumb:** Build > session > Changes > Scope. **Branch:** `parallel/build` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Lane queue now DRY** (┬¦15 stop-and-report; K2b/BLD-05/BLD-04 are out of lane).

**[WM-F6, 2026-06-19 23:42, overnight cycle 46] move product between workspaces (ŌŚÉ; transactional `move_product` RPC + server fn behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod, UI deferred).** Products could not move; cross-workspace consolidation (paid/team) needs it. Built the backend per the founder ruling (keep building backend, batch UI to the design pass). **Key finding (verified live before building):** the spec's "harden product-level scoping first (product_id has no RLS on those ~10 tables today)" is ALREADY satisfied - querying `pg_policies` on prod shows every product-scoped table is read-gated by `is_workspace_member(workspace_id)` (SELECT) and `is_workspace_member(workspace_id) AND user_id=auth.uid()` (UPDATE/DELETE). So reassigning `workspace_id` IS the move: destination members gain access and source-only members lose it automatically, with NO separate RLS-hardening migration. **What it does:** migration `20260619280000_wm_f6_move_product.sql` adds a SECURITY DEFINER `move_product(_product_id, _dest_workspace_id)` that, after a guard (caller is owner/admin of BOTH workspaces via WM-F3 `can_manage_workspace`, both workspaces in the SAME account via WM-M2 `workspaces.account_id`, a `FOR UPDATE` lock on the product), atomically reassigns `workspace_id` on the product (`projects`) + 13 product-scoped tables. New `moveProduct` server fn in `projects.functions.ts` (validated wrapper calling the RPC via `context.supabase` so the RPC's `auth.uid()` checks apply). **Decisions / the untyped-client trap (HARD GATE 4):** verified the live schema before writing - the product foreign key is `project_id` on 8 tables (signals/themes/opportunities/prds/docs/tasks/decisions/conversations) but `product_id` on 4 (ai_events/connection_bindings/rag_chunks/studio_changesets); a single wrong column name would silently leave orphan rows tsc can't catch, so each UPDATE uses the right column (and `project_id OR product_id` for the 8 tables that carry both). Also caught 3 product-scoped GRANDCHILDREN that carry `workspace_id` but link to the product only via a parent - doc_versions (doc_id), messages (conversation_id), learnings (opportunity_id/prd_id) - and move them through their parent so they don't orphan; the remaining `workspace_id` tables (missions/agent_runs/budgets/evals/...) are workspace-scoped not product-scoped and correctly stay (memory stays at the workspace, per spec). connection_bindings/studio_changesets DO move (same-account moves only + connections are account-level, so the bound resource stays valid). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint src/lib/projects.functions.ts` 0; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.38s); full `bun test` 274/274; AND a two-pass `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` behavioral dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (Lovable MCP, stubbing the unpublished WM-M2 `account_id` + WM-F3 `can_manage_workspace` + WM-F9 notes/prototypes `workspace_id`, simulating the owner's JWT): moving a real product (`9857019eŌĆ”`: 9 signals / 2 prds / 10 tasks / 3 decisions / 8 messages) to a same-account destination reassigned the product + EVERY child/grandchild (signals left in src = 0, messages moved 8/8 with 0 orphaned), a cross-account move was blocked ("A product can only move between workspaces in the same account."), and a non-manager caller was blocked ("You must be an owner or admin of the destination workspace."); rolled back, prod untouched. **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** the RPC + server fn are built and behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real prod schema, but there is NO UI affordance yet (deferred to the design pass), and live move activates on the founder's publish (depends on the unpublished WM-M2/F3/F9). **Follow-up WM-F6b:** scope `artifact_lineage` + other generic-provenance tables (their product linkage is via generic artifact ids across tables, deferred this cycle to avoid a wrong remap). **UI breadcrumb (once the UI ships):** Product > Settings > Move to workspace. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-M9 (remove self-serve BYOK) or the next non-gated WM/strategy item.

**[DATA-RETENTION, 2026-06-20 00:20, overnight cycle 47] AI-telemetry retention purge (ŌŚÉ; dormant, behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod).** **Pick rationale:** the WM backend lane is thinning; the last in-initiative item WM-M9 (remove self-serve BYOK) is best sequenced with the founder-gated pricing surfaces per its own spec (and removing a live capability at the AI chokepoint while credits are dormant is premature), so it was skip-and-queued. Cross-referencing `docs/planning/considerations.md` surfaced a clean, unclaimed, non-gated P1 gap the WM accounts/tenancy/enterprise thrust genuinely needs: `ai_events` (+ per-call siblings) grow unbounded - one+ row per AI call, forever - a cost/scale and data-minimization (GDPR/CCPA) problem enterprise/team buyers ask about. **What it does:** migration `20260620000000_data_retention.sql` adds `data_retention_enabled()` (a dormant flag returning false, mirroring `credits_enabled()`/`limit_gates_enabled()`) + a SECURITY DEFINER `purge_old_telemetry(_older_than_days integer default 180)` that self-gates on the flag, applies a hard 30-day floor (a mis-call with days=0 floors to 30, so it can NEVER delete recent data), and deletes `ai_events`/`prompt_runs`/`tool_calls` older than the window. New `retention-tick` hook (`src/routes/api/public/hooks/retention-tick.ts`, mirrors `credit-tick`: `requireHookCaller`-gated, `supabaseAdmin` service-role, pre-migration-tolerant). **Decisions:** (1) verified on the live schema that `token_usage` does not exist (token data lives in `ai_events`) and that the 3 target tables have NO inbound foreign-key references (so the deletes neither cascade nor restrict) before writing the purge; (2) made the purge STRICTER than the codebase's other SECURITY DEFINER RPCs - execute revoked from public/anon/authenticated, granted to `service_role` only - because a global telemetry purge is destructive and no authenticated user should trigger it; (3) the function self-gates (`{skipped:dormant}`) so even a direct pg_cron call is inert until the flag flips; (4) deferred the right-to-be-forgotten per-account/workspace erase cascade (DATA-RETENTION-b) as destructive + policy-coupled. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 (after the build regenerated `routeTree.gen.ts` to register the new route); `bunx eslint` 0 on the new hook; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.19s); full `bun test` 287/287; AND a `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` behavioral dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (Lovable MCP, backdating two real `ai_events` rows to 200d and 50d): flag false ŌåÆ `skipped:dormant`, deleted nothing (200d row survived); flag true ŌåÆ `purge_old_telemetry(180)` deleted the 200d row and KEPT the 50d row; `purge_old_telemetry(0)` floored to 30 days and deleted the 50d row; rolled back, prod untouched. **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** built + behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real schema, but it stays DORMANT until the founder (a) flips `data_retention_enabled()` to `select true` and (b) wires a pg_cron / external scheduler to POST `/api/public/hooks/retention-tick`; live purge activates only then. **Follow-up DATA-RETENTION-b:** the right-to-be-forgotten erase cascade. **UI breadcrumb:** none (cron + DB plumbing). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** the WM lane is near-dry on clean backend items; weigh WM-M9 (chokepoint, founder-surface-coupled) vs the next v9/v8/considerations item.

**[U6-AUDIT, 2026-06-20 00:50, overnight cycle 48] export audit log ŌĆö the remaining slice of U6 (ŌŚÉ; backend behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod, history UI deferred).** **Pick rationale:** the two highest-pure-impact remaining items (PROVIDER-FALLBACK resilience, WM-M9 remove-BYOK) BOTH touch the AI chokepoint AND cannot be behaviorally verified unattended (a fallback-on-outage feature is pure runtime behavior; the founder's guidance is "chokepoint better attended"), and shipping an unverifiable chokepoint change would be a claim outrunning verified wiring (HARD GATE 4) - so both were queued for an attended cycle, and I picked the cleanest fully-verifiable, my-lane, unclaimed item: U6-AUDIT (the remaining ~15% of U6, row 36), an enterprise/compliance audit trail aligned with the same enterprise-readiness thrust as DATA-RETENTION. **What it does:** migration `20260620010000_export_log.sql` adds an append-only `export_log` table (id/user_id/workspace_id/kind/target_id/sections/row_count/created_at) with `insert-own` + `read-own-or-workspace` RLS and DELIBERATELY no update/delete policy - so for authenticated users the trail is tamper-evident (Postgres default-deny on a command with no permissive policy), while an owner can audit ALL data egress from their workspace via the `is_workspace_member`-gated read. `exportProduct` + `exportWorkspace` now write one audit row per export (who, kind product/workspace, target id, which sections, total row_count). New `listExportLog` read fn (RLS-scoped, newest-first, capped at 100). **Decisions:** (1) the audit-write is BEST-EFFORT and wrapped in try/catch - the export is the user's data-portability right and must never fail because the audit row could not be written (e.g. pre-migration, before `export_log` is published); (2) append-only (no update/delete policy) over a "soft delete" so the trail cannot be tampered with by authenticated users; (3) write via the user's RLS-scoped `context.supabase` (cast to the untyped `SupabaseClient` for the not-yet-typed table, the codebase's established pattern) with `user_id` defaulting to `auth.uid()` and a with-check `user_id = auth.uid()`; (4) the DataExportCard history view is deferred to the design pass (founder ruling). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint src/lib/projects.functions.ts` 0; `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.25s); rolled back, prod untouched. **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** the audit table + the per-export write + the read fn are built and behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real schema, but U6 stays ŌŚÉ because its export-history UI (DataExportCard) is deferred to the design pass, and live audit rows accrue only after the founder's publish. **Adversarial review folded one fix:** wrapped `recordExport` in try/catch so an unexpected throw from `.insert()` can never fail the user's export (bulletproofing the best-effort intent). **UI breadcrumb (once the UI ships):** Settings > Data > Export history. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** the clean my-lane backend lane is thinning; the remaining high-impact items (PROVIDER-FALLBACK, WM-M9) are chokepoint + attended; weigh them vs the next clean considerations.md / v9 / v8 item.

**[APP-HEALTH, 2026-06-20 02:10, overnight cycle 50] public app-level health/readiness endpoint (ŌŚÉ; endpoint + pure assembly unit-verified, live DB-probe + alerting deferred).** **Pick rationale:** the chokepoint bundle (PROVIDER-FALLBACK / PLAN-ENFORCE / MODEL-REGISTRY-DEPRECATION) stays attended; the Data/Privacy vein is now well-mined (3 consecutive: retention c47, export-audit c48, sub-proc c49); the other clean queue items are parallel-lane-owned. Following `considerations.md`'s explicit P0-first precedence, the highest-priority clean, greenfield, zero-collision, fully-verifiable unattended gap is the SRE-lens P0 "App-level monitoring + alerting (not just AI telemetry)" - confirmed unbuilt, since `health.functions.ts` is only a migration-DRIFT checker (SSOT finding 4), not an external health signal. It is also genuinely greenfield (new files, zero blast radius to existing code), unlike a core-file edit such as KI-16's mission-advance cap. **What it does:** new route `src/routes/api/public/health.ts` (`GET /api/public/health`) returns HTTP 200 `{status:"ok",...}` healthy or 503 `{status:"degraded",...}` when a dependency is down, so an uptime monitor / load balancer reacts on the STATUS CODE without parsing the body; it runs a cheap, timeout-bounded DB reachability probe and reports per-check states (`worker`, `database`). New pure `src/lib/app-health.ts` (`assembleHealth(checks, nowIso)` ŌåÆ `{body, httpStatus}`). **Decisions:** (1) **public + unauthenticated** (monitors don't auth), so it is designed not to be an attack surface - it leaks NOTHING beyond ok/error check states (no error messages/stack traces; a test asserts the exact response key set), keeps the DB probe trivially cheap (one indexed-id head-read), and bounds it with a 2s timeout (a DoS-amplification guard so a slow DB can't pile up requests); (2) the HTTP status code carries the signal (200/503) so load balancers and monitors need not parse the body; (3) verified `profiles` is a REAL table (queried in onboarding/connections/calendar) before using it as the probe target - the untyped-client trap (HARD GATE 4); (4) kept the status assembly PURE (timestamp injected) so it is fully unit-testable, with only the live DB probe in the route; (5) liveness is implicit (reaching the handler means the worker serves) so no separate liveness check is needed. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bun run build` Ō£ō (3.68s, regenerated `src/routeTree.gen.ts` for the new route); `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on the 3 new files (after a prettier auto-fix); `bun test src/lib/app-health.test.ts` 5/5 (okŌåÆ200, db-downŌåÆ503, worker-always-ok, no-leak exact-key-set, purity); full `bun test` 303/303 (298 prior + 5 new). **Marked ŌŚÉ (not Ō£ģ):** the endpoint + the pure assembly are built and unit-verified, but the LIVE DB-probe behavior was not run unattended (no live worker; verify with a `curl` on the next publish), and the ALERTING half (wire a monitor ŌåÆ notify) + a status page are infra/founder + design-pass. **Adversarial review:** no runtime-fatal bug - confirmed `profiles` exists, the probe is timeout-bounded + leak-free, every probe path returns a `CheckState` (never throws out of the handler), and the route is a driven live endpoint (not staged). **UI breadcrumb:** none (infra endpoint; a future status page is design-pass). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** the clean unattended lane is thinning to lower-impact ops items; weigh the next `considerations.md` P0/P1 gap (e.g. a full-account GDPR data-portability export) vs surfacing to the founder that the high-impact remainder is the attended chokepoint bundle + founder-gated work.

Added the **branch link**: migration `20260618160000_d4_replay_branch_link.sql` adds `missions.replayed_from_mission_id` (additive, idempotent, FK `ON DELETE SET NULL` so deleting an original never orphans/cascades) + a partial index; `StartSchema` gained `replayedFrom`, written to the new mission in a SEPARATE pre-migration-tolerant update right after `createMission` (so chat's mission path is untouched and the replay still runs if the column is absent); `getMission` resolves `replayed_from_mission_id` via a SEPARATE error-tolerant read (the main select and the whole detail page keep working before the migration applies); the new mission shows a "Replayed from an earlier mission" link to the parent. Replay re-plans from the goal via the orchestrator, so the model affects both planning and execution (A/B a goal across models). **Decision:** the rich side-by-side checkpoint-diff is deferred as D4b; the branch link is the lightweight diff affordance (open both). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on the three touched files, humanization scan of additions clean, migration-safety hook passed. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (additive migration, tolerant set + read so pre-migration is safe, no redundant replay affordances between header + failure panel, model defaults to undefined when unset). **K2 (cycle 24) ┬Ę operator revert-to-revision (one-action rollback).** The Build engine recorded a revision per `studio.commit` (I1b) but had no way to roll back. K2 adds a confirm-gated "Revert" button on every prior revision in the Changes tab. New shared helper `src/lib/ai/studio-revert.server.ts` (`revertChangesetToRevision`) performs a NON-DESTRUCTIVE revert via the GitHub Git Data API: GET the target revision's commit tree, GET the current branch head, POST a new commit `{ tree: targetTree, parents: [headSha] }`, then PATCH the ref with `force:false`. History only moves forward (the revert is itself a normal, revertible commit) and a stale-parent race is refused by GitHub rather than clobbering work; the revert is recorded as the next revision. `revertToRevision` (server fn in `studio.functions.ts`) resolves GitHub auth for the changeset's workspace via `resolveGitHub` and delegates to the helper. The ChangesPanel button (`useConfirm`-gated) shows only while the branch is live (`committed`/`pr_open`) and never on the latest revision (a no-op). The helper is self-contained (its own gh fetch helpers, no `registry.server.ts` import) so a future `studio.revert` agent engine-tool can reuse it without a circular dependency. **No migration.** **Decision (operator-first):** shipped the operator door first because it needs no `agent_tools` migration, is self-authorizing (the human clicks), and is the literal "revert button" the spec names; the agent engine-tool (K2b) is deferred since the loop only exposes tools seeded in `agent_tools`. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on all three touched files, humanization scan of additions clean. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (non-destructive by construction, revision lookup scoped to the changeset, GitHub commit applied before the best-effort revision record so a DB hiccup can't falsely report a failed revert, queries RLS-scoped). Clean sync (no parallel commit). **Pending publish + live verify (GitHub mutation + UI).** **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/studio-revert.server.ts`, `src/lib/studio.functions.ts`, `src/components/studio/ChangesPanel.tsx`, `docs/features/studio.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**P4-GATE (cycle 23) ┬Ę eval-regression as a hard merge gate.** The Studio/Build merge tool `studio.pr.merge` was hard-gated only on CI (the J2 gate, `studio-ci.ts`). P4-GATE adds its quality-side twin so the BUILDŌåÆSHIP loop cannot ship code unattended while output quality is measurably regressing. New pure module `src/lib/ai/eval-gate.ts` (`evalRegressionReadiness` + `EVAL_REGRESSION_THRESHOLD_PTS = 10` + `SuiteScorePair`), mirroring `studio-ci.ts`: given the latest-vs-prior completed avg_score per suite (0-100), it blocks if any suite dropped Ōēź10 points, naming the worst. The merge tool (`registry.server.ts`) reads the user's completed `eval_runs` (latest two per suite, `.eq("user_id")` + `status='completed'` + non-null avg_score, ordered desc, capped at 80), fetches suite names, and throws `MergeBlocked` when not allowed, right after the existing CI gate, inside the same `if (!prJson.merged)` block. **Scale:** avg_score is 0-100 (confirmed via `20260614160000_p3_ki14_eval_score_0to100.sql`), so the threshold is 10 points on 0-100. **Semantics (J2-analogous):** evals run on a schedule (`eval-tick`), so the gate reads the already-measured trend and never triggers a run; it is read-only, degrades to allowed when no suite has two completed runs, and the operator can always merge from GitHub directly (the gate governs only the agent's tool). **No migration.** **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on both touched files, humanization scan of additions clean. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (0-100 scale correct, drop = prior minus latest is the correct direction, `Number()` coercion + the non-null DB filter make NaN/null safe, both queries explicitly user-scoped). Clean sync (no parallel commit this cycle). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/eval-gate.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `docs/features/studio.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**P5-ALERT (cycle 22) ┬Ę drift threshold ŌåÆ in-app Attention feed.** Drift was a passive watcher: the detector (`ai/drift.server.ts`) opens `drift_incidents` rows when a metric crosses the user's baseline, but they only showed on the `/drift` page. P5-ALERT surfaces them where the operator already looks: a 4th probe in `getNotifications` (`src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`) reads open `drift_incidents` (most-recent 6, over the existing `(user_id, status, detected_at)` index) and pushes them into the R3 Attention feed as severity-coded cards. Severity maps `critical` ŌåÆ warning, anything else ŌåÆ info (drift is a heads-up, never a human-decision "action"); the card names the drifted metric (latency / cost / token use / error rate / quality score, via a label map) with the signed `delta_pct` vs baseline + the surface and model, and links to `/drift`. **No migration** (live-derived from an existing table, same pattern as the approval/stall/budget probes), capped so a noisy week cannot flood the feed, degrades to no items on error. **No UI change needed:** both consumers (`NotificationsPanel`, `AttentionBell`) key off `severity`, not `kind`, so adding the `drift` kind to the union was enough. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on the touched file, humanization scan of additions clean. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (numeric `delta_pct` coercion is `Number.isFinite`-guarded, severity safe-defaults to info, query is RLS-scoped + explicitly `.eq("user_id")`). Clean sync (no parallel/runaway commit this cycle). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`, `docs/features/r3-notifications.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**F-AGENTS-MENTIONABLE (cycle 21) ┬Ę composer @-picker + case-insensitive parse, feature completed.** The server half of this feature (parse `@agentslug` ŌåÆ pre-planned single-step `mission_steps` dispatch via `advanceMissionCore`; see the cycle-19-labeled entry below for the server design) was auto-committed mid-build by a parallel process (`40646dce0a` + report `ffbf5c50c0`) while the main loop was still working the same worktree, so the committed `chat.ts` already matched the main loop's server work. This cycle layered the genuinely-new value on top: (1) the **composer @-agent picker** in `_authenticated.chat.tsx`, a floating list above the composer (reuses `listAgents`, filtered to enabled non-orchestrator agents) with arrow-key nav + Enter/Tab/click to insert `@slug `; the picker drives those keys ONLY while open, so the Enter-to-send path is byte-identical when it is closed and can never be hijacked; placeholder + helper line advertise the affordance; (2) a **case-insensitive parse fix** in `chat.ts` (`parseAgentMentions` `/gi` + lowercased candidate, `stripMention` `i` flag) so a manually-typed `@Strategist` resolves to the lowercase `strategist` slug, matching the composer's already-case-insensitive `detectMentionQuery`. **Why single-step DAG (not "just run the agent"):** `maybeCompleteMission` keys off `steps.length > 0`; a mission with zero steps and no orchestrator run hangs at `running` forever, so the mention pre-plans one step and lets the deterministic `advanceMissionCore` cron dispatch + finalize it (cheaper + faster than the orchestrator path, exact agent honored). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on both touched files, humanization scan of additions clean (zero em/en dashes). **Adversarial review folded one real fix:** the server parse was case-sensitive while the composer was not, so a typed `@Strategist` would silently miss; made both case-insensitive. **Process note (recurring):** a background process is committing/pushing autonomously again (same pattern as the F3 `c304bf6396` incident); logged in `session-decisions.md`. **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/routes/_authenticated.chat.tsx` (composer @-picker), `src/routes/api/chat.ts` (case-insensitive parse), `docs/features/agents-mentionable.md` (new), `docs/features/README.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**F3-CRON (cycle 20) ┬Ę continuous auto-cluster, built gated-off, verified + closed.** The auto-cluster cron deferred at cycles 11/17 (recurring AI spend = founder-gated) is now BUILT in the autonomous-safe shape: shipped off by default so applying it commits zero spend, with the recurring-spend scheduler left as the one founder activation step. Extracted the LLM clustering body into a shared core `clusterSignalsCore` (`src/lib/ai/cluster.server.ts`) called by both the user-triggered `clusterSignals` and a new `cluster-tick` hook (`src/routes/api/public/hooks/cluster-tick.ts`); the core explicitly filters `signals.user_id` so the service-role cron path (RLS off) clusters one owner at a time (never across users), passes `workspaceId` so the kill-switch + budget caps still govern spend, and stamps `themes.workspace_id` explicitly (the cron has no `auth.uid()` for the DB default). Owner-gated `getWorkspaceClusterSettings` / `toggleAutoCluster` server fns back a "Auto-cluster new signals" toggle in `SignalsPanel.tsx` (owner-only, shows last-run time). Migration `20260618140000_f3_auto_cluster.sql` adds `workspaces.auto_cluster_enabled` (NOT NULL DEFAULT false) + `last_auto_cluster_at` + a partial index for the cron query; additive, idempotent, zero spend on apply. The cron is batch-capped at 5 workspaces (oldest-run-first) and tolerates the pre-migration window (`42703`/`PGRST204` soft-pass). **Adversarial review (prior session) caught + fixed a service-role `workspace_id` NOT-NULL bug.** **Gate (this turn):** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green (the `cluster-tick` route bundles), `eslint` clean on all four touched files, F3 source + migration scan zero em/en dashes. **Activation (founder, section 4 of the SSOT):** apply the migration on publish, owners enable the toggle, then point pg_cron at the hook (snippet in the migration header). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/cluster.server.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/cluster-tick.ts`, `supabase/migrations/20260618140000_f3_auto_cluster.sql`; edited `src/lib/discovery.functions.ts`, `src/components/product/SignalsPanel.tsx`, generated `src/integrations/supabase/types.ts` + `src/routeTree.gen.ts`; `docs/features/f3-continuous-discovery.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, this log.

**O1 (cycle 19) ┬Ę provenance in the shared Lineage drawer ŌĆö gate-green, pending publish.** Extended the O1 provenance slice (root-signal trace) from the two drill surfaces (opportunity, spec/PRD) to the cross-cutting `LineageDrawer`, so "why does this exist?" is answerable wherever lineage opens, not only on two detail pages. **RULE ┬Ę data minimalism ("every field earns its place") + onboarding `role` removed ŌĆö landed on `main`.** Founder principle, made a standing convention: we capture nothing by default; no field, input, stored column, or pixel of screen real estate exists unless a _named consumer_ needs it (now, or with a documented credible near-term use), and a captured field ships in the same change as its consumer (no "collect now, use later"). Unearned capture costs the user's time, our storage, privacy surface, and maintenance, forever. **Applied immediately:** an audit of `profiles.role` found it is never mapped to anything ŌĆö no roleŌåÆagent config, settings, or gating; its only "use" was being incidentally swept into the chat-grounding JSON blob. The persona that actually customizes the workspace is the onboarding track selector, not a free-text role. So `role` was removed from `BasicDetailsStep` (name only now); it returns only when wired to a real consumer (e.g. role-based personalization). **What shipped:** new convention [`docs/conventions/data-minimalism.md`](./docs/conventions/data-minimalism.md) (the Value Test + the wiring rule + the narrow future-use clause + the `role` worked example), indexed in the conventions README, wired into [`AGENTS.md`](./AGENTS.md) ┬¦3.0b (sibling to the Engine-Room Doctrine) + a ┬¦5 trigger row ("adding a captured field ŌåÆ run the Value Test first"); `BasicDetailsStep.tsx` role field + state + write removed (docstring explains the name-only-by-design choice). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Files:** `docs/conventions/data-minimalism.md` new, `docs/conventions/README.md`, `AGENTS.md` (┬¦3.0b + ┬¦5), `src/components/onboarding/BasicDetailsStep.tsx`, this log.

**ONBOARDING ┬Ę basic-details step + credentials-only signup (fixes the OAuth `abc.def` name) ŌĆö shipped on `main` (no migration).** Founder report: a Google signup had no name, so the whole app addressed the user by the email local-part (`abc.def`). Root cause: identity capture was asymmetric ŌĆö email/password grabbed name inline at `/signup`, the Google path captured nothing and the `handle_new_user` trigger only ever set `full_name` (never `display_name`), so both greeting surfaces fell back to `email.split("@")[0]`. **Decision (founder deferred the call):** adopt the industry-standard split (Linear/Notion/Vercel) ŌĆö authenticate first, capture profile second, prefilled from the OAuth provider ŌĆö rather than keep name on the signup form for one path only. **What shipped:** (1) new `src/components/onboarding/BasicDetailsStep.tsx` ŌĆö first/last name + role, the single identity-capture surface for BOTH signup paths; rendered as the first gate in `OnboardingFlow` only when the profile lacks a `display_name`; prefills from auth `user_metadata` (`given_name`/`family_name`/`full_name`) for Google, blank for bare email, and NEVER seeds from the email local-part; on submit writes BOTH `profiles` (via `updateProfile`) AND auth `user_metadata` (via `supabase.auth.updateUser`) because Today reads the profiles row while the AppShell chip + chat header read the session metadata ŌĆö fixing one without the other leaves the wrong name on the other surface. (2) `/signup` reduced to credentials only (email + password + Google); name/role inputs removed; profile upsert now `{ onboarded: false }` so the gate routes into onboarding where the details step runs. (3) Fixed a pre-existing humanized-output violation (em-dash in the password placeholder). **Engine-Room:** none (calm-front identity capture). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green, and both screens visually verified on-brand via a throwaway preview route + Playwright at 1440px (Ember Editorial: parchment, ember reserved for the single CTA, serif italic-em title, mono-label kicker; preview route reverted before commit). Live walkthrough (fresh Google signup ŌåÆ name prefilled ŌåÆ setup) confirms on the next publish. **Files:** `src/components/onboarding/BasicDetailsStep.tsx` new, `src/components/onboarding/OnboardingFlow.tsx`, `src/routes/signup.tsx`, `docs/features/auth-flows.md`, `docs/features/onboarding-tracks.md`, this log.

**HOTFIX ┬Ę onboarding track-pick crashed every new user with an RLS error ŌĆö fixed on `main` (no migration).** The published demo blocked at "Setup ┬Ę Step 1 of 4": clicking any track (Solo PM / Founding PM / Tech Founder) raised **"new row violates row-level security policy for table 'projects'"**, and the user could not enter the app. **Root cause (systematic-debugging, traced through the migrations):** `seedWorkspaceForTrack` inserts into `projects` / `signals` / `opportunities` without setting `workspace_id`, trusting the `current_user_default_workspace()` column default added in the tenancy retrofit (`20260530120200_tenancy_c`). That migration also swapped those tables' write RLS from `auth.uid() = user_id` to **membership-keyed** `is_workspace_member(workspace_id)`. The default resolves to the caller's earliest `workspace_members` row ŌĆö but a brand-new user reaches onboarding (their first write) before that row reliably exists: `handle_new_user()` calls `ensure_default_workspace()` inside a swallow-all `EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS` block, that function isn't in our migrations (Lovable-managed, drift-prone, and the KI-13 saga shows the trigger body keeps getting reverted), and demo accounts skip the provisioning entirely. No membership ŌåÆ `is_workspace_member(NULL)` is false ŌåÆ the `projects` INSERT is rejected. Every track button fails identically because they all hit the same insert. **Fix:** made onboarding self-healing. New `ensureDefaultWorkspace(supabase, userId)` helper in `onboarding.functions.ts` resolves the default workspace via the RPC, else reuses an owned-but-unmembered workspace, else creates `workspaces {owner_id, name}` + the owner `workspace_members` row (all permitted to the user-scoped client by the `ws owner manage` / `owner manages members` policies); `seedWorkspaceForTrack` calls it first and sets `workspace_id` **explicitly** on all three inserts ŌĆö the path migration C documented as intended ("set workspace_id explicitly in server functions"). Defense-in-depth: onboarding can no longer fail this way even after signup provisioning is repaired. **Why a server-function fix, not a migration:** it ships on the next Lovable publish with no migration-sync gate (the exact gate that keeps reverting `handle_new_user`). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real gate), `eslint` clean, `prettier` clean, `bun run build` green. Live proof requires a fresh non-demo signup ŌåÆ pick a track after republish (could not reproduce locally ŌĆö Supabase MCP unauthenticated this session). **Standing follow-up:** the deeper signup-provisioning fragility (`ensure_default_workspace` absent from repo migrations + swallowed in the trigger) remains a known issue ŌĆö see `docs/planning/known-issues.md`. **Files:** `src/lib/onboarding.functions.ts`, `docs/features/onboarding-tracks.md`, `docs/planning/known-issues.md`, this log.

**Onboarding ┬Ę first-run gate fix + 4-step redesign ŌĆö shipped on `main`.** The founder published W6 and signed up with Google: onboarding never appeared, landing straight on Home. **Root cause:** the first-run gate (`_authenticated.tsx` + `onboarding-gate.ts`) redirects only on `profiles.onboarded === false`, but the only path that reliably wrote that flag was the email/password client-side upsert in `signup.tsx`; the Google (Lovable OAuth) path has no such write and leans on the unreliable `handle_new_user` trigger (KI-13), whose resilient body swallows a failed profile insert. So an OAuth signup had no profile row, and the gate's "missing row counts as onboarded" fail-open rule sent them past onboarding. **Fix:** the gate now treats a missing row as a brand-new account, upserts `{ onboarded: false }` (ignoreDuplicates, never clobbers an existing row) and routes into first-run, making the gate the single source of truth for every signup path (`82281c21c3`). **Redesign** (founder: "UI/UX looks crap, no value"): built in an isolated `git worktree` (a parallel session was actively resetting the main tree and had already wiped the uncommitted fix once) with `impeccable` (onboard) + `emil-design-eng` against the Ember Editorial canon; all 4 steps rendered + screenshotted via a throwaway preview harness (reverted before merge). Step 1 `TrackSelector` now names the outcome ŌĆö each persona card previews the real workspace + first teardown it delivers, read from the seed data ŌĆö instead of "we'll seed sample data"; steps 2-4 get serif italic-em titles (`listen` / `staff` / `goal`), value copy that names the outcome, and the user-facing em-dashes removed (humanized-output); ember reserved for the single CTA; staggered transform-only entrance + `.lift` press feedback, reduced-motion gated (`40a0f51a5b`, `00a051a1c3`). Logic, mutations, and the founder skip-as-primary ruling unchanged. **Verification:** `tsc` / `eslint` / `prettier` / `bun run build` all green; the OAuth round-trip is verifiable only on the next publish. **Files:** `src/lib/onboarding-gate.ts`, `src/components/onboarding/TrackSelector.tsx`, `src/components/onboarding/OnboardingFlow.tsx`, `docs/features/onboarding-tracks.md`, `docs/features/README.md` (W6 index row), `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

**DEC-02-LOOP ┬Ę the Critic promoted to a routable agent-loop tool ŌĆö built + tsc/build-verified on `main`.** Closes the v10 M-B "Critic as an explicit loop step" item with the _safe_ increment (recon blueprint from a 3-reader engine map): make the Critic a registered, agent-callable tool WITHOUT touching the fragile mission-DAG machinery. Before, `runCritic` was a private fn in `discovery.functions.ts` reachable only from 4 inline call sites; now the orchestrator or any specialist can red-team an opportunity/PRD **in-loop**. **What shipped:** (1) extracted `runCritic` + `CriticReview` verbatim into new `src/lib/ai/critic.server.ts` + a `runCriticTool({target_kind,target_id}, ctx)` adapter (never throws; returns `{ok, review}`); (2) `discovery.functions.ts` imports `runCritic` and re-exports the `CriticReview` type (Ōēł8 modules import it from there) ŌĆö the 4 call sites + `runCriticReview` ("Re-run Critic" badge) behave identically; (3) registered `critic.evaluate` (category `planning`) in `TOOL_REGISTRY`; (4) added `critic.evaluate` to `ORCHESTRATION_CONTROL_FLOW_TOOLS` in `loop.server.ts` so it runs inline (the verdict is advisory + side-effect-free beyond the row's `critic_review`; gating it could strand a run); (5) migration `20260617160000` seeds it into `agent_tools` for new users (via `seed_default_agent_tools`, mirrored verbatim + 1 row) and backfills existing users ŌĆö does NOT touch `handle_new_user`. **Deferred (Phase 2):** the full `mission_steps` DAG-node promotion ŌĆö the recon flagged it touches the handoff completion-guard (an unconsumed critic step hangs the mission / trips the orphan-sweep), bounded-retry on a non-deterministic judge, and verdict-routing; **hard rule: a `kill` verdict stays advisory, never auto-fails dependent steps.** **Adversarial review** (3 perspective-diverse lenses): behavior-equivalence APPROVE (byte-identical), engine-correctness/security APPROVE (RLS-scoped via `ctx.supabase`, no cross-tenant reach, no DAG/mission-advance edits), migration-safety APPROVE_WITH_FIXES (1 MEDIUM: aligned the DB tool description with the registry, added the omitted kill-criteria). **Verification:** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real gate); `bun run build` Ō£ō; prettier-clean. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/critic.server.ts` new, `src/lib/discovery.functions.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `supabase/migrations/20260617160000_dec02loop_critic_tool.sql` new, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/features/critic-agent.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

**Q1-MCP-P3 + AMBIENT-ARC (the two top P1 "buildable-now" picks, parallel + file-disjoint) ŌĆö built + tsc/build-verified on `main`.** A code-grounded P1 verify (10 candidates, one read-only agent each) found only three buildable with zero external blocker; these two are the top pair and touch disjoint files, so both shipped in one session. **WEDGE ┬Ę Critic-teardown first-run (the v10 launch wedge, P0 #2) ŌĆö SHIPPED to `main`.** Picked the next item in the v10 pick-order after LRN-02. **Recon first (background Explore agent) confirmed the wedge is pure integration, not new capability:** the Critic engine (`runCritic`, DEC-02), the `opportunities` table (`critic_review jsonb`), and the `VerdictChip`/`CriticBadge` renderers already exist, so there is **no new AI infra and no migration** ŌĆö the work is intake + surface. Fixed two ways: the component holds the result in local state and does **not** invalidate `["cold-start"]`, and the cold-start query now sets `refetchOnWindowFocus: false` + `refetchOnReconnect: false` so it only re-evaluates on a genuine remount. Also handled the no-AI-key path honestly (`review` can be `null` ŌåÆ "Saved, the Critic could not run" fallback, not a broken card), and swapped smart quotes for straight quotes in the one user-facing title line (humanized-output gate). **Verification: `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real type gate ŌĆö `bun run build` strips types without checking); `bun run lint` shows zero problems in the three changed files.** Full end-to-end (the real cited verdict) needs the deployed app ŌĆö local dev has no AI key, and cold-start needs an empty workspace. **LRN-02 ┬Ę Outcome reviews ŌĆö Historian verdict (predicted vs actual) ŌĆö SHIPPED to `main`.** Picked the v10 P0 #1 (`LRN-02` + `W1-AUTO`, the "close the loop / moat" item). **Recon first saved a rebuild:** the core was already built and the dashboard status was stale ŌĆö `recordOutcome` already takes a human verdict, re-scores the linked opportunity's ICE, writes a `learnings` row, and (W1-AUTO) calls `rememberOutcome`, which embeds the outcome into a recallable global `agent_memory` row so future runs compound it. The whole thing only DRAFTS ŌĆö no autonomous write. **Adversarial review (ecc:code-reviewer): APPROVE, 0 HIGH;** folded 1 MED (clear the stale `predicted` line via `onMutate` on a re-draft) + 1 LOW (dropped a no-op `fallbackModel` equal to the primary). Prompt-injection risk assessed LOW (user's own workspace data + enum-clamped output + human-confirm gate). **Verification: `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `bunx eslint` clean, `bun run build` green.** **Files:** `src/lib/outcome.functions.ts` (`suggestOutcomeVerdict`), `src/components/product/OutcomeCard.tsx`; `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log. **OPS-01 audio ┬Ę real ElevenLabs soundscapes generated (experimental free-tier set).** Connected the ElevenLabs MCP and generated the Flow-mode ambient tracks into `public/soundscape/`. Final set (all ElevenLabs **Sound Effects**, 5s, looped, ~80KB each): **Ocean ┬Ę Monsoon (rain + temple bells) ┬Ę Bansuri (flute texture) ┬Ę Forest (Himalayan) ┬Ę Heartbeat (bass-rich ~75bpm) ┬Ę Fireplace**; default is Ocean. Two iterations with the founder: the first cut included **Tanpura** and **Singing bowls**, both removed as too harsh; root cause documented (a 5s SFX loop repeats a transient _attack_ like a pluck/strike every 5s, so it "hits", whereas continuous textures like water, fire, rain, and forest loop invisibly), and the heartbeat was regenerated bassier/punchier. The **Music API (`compose_music`) is paid-only** (free tier returns 402), so real melodic/cultural music (lo-fi raga, a full bansuri melody, Balinese gamelan, a smooth long tanpura) is **deferred with a full pick-up plan + exact prompts** in `public/soundscape/README.md` (the "TODO when on a paid plan" + "Tried and rejected" sections). **B5 ┬Ę Product lifecycle (archive / restore / export / delete) ŌĆö SHIPPED to `main`.** Built the full product lifecycle onto the `/product` **Portfolio** (the continuation of B3), extracting the inline portfolio into `src/components/product/PortfolioBoard.tsx`. Four per-product actions: **soft archive + restore** (reversible ŌĆö an Undo toast, and a durable Archived section to restore from; archived products drop out of the sidebar + product tabs), **JSON export** of the product's whole footprint (project + signals + opportunities + specs + tasks ŌĆö the escape hatch / U6-lite), and an **honest export-then-delete**. The delete follows the destructive-actions doctrine: `useConfirm({ destructive, typedConfirm: name })` (type the exact product name) with **honest copy** ŌĆö because the FK is `on delete set null`, deleting a product _detaches_ its signals/opps/specs/tasks to the workspace rather than destroying them (the old AppShell sidebar delete's "everything inside it" copy was factually wrong); a JSON snapshot auto-downloads first as the safety net. **Server (`projects.functions.ts`):** new `setProjectArchived({id, archive})` (verified write ŌĆö `.eq("user_id").select("id")`, throws on 0 rows), `exportProduct({id})` (RLS-scoped reads), hardened `deleteProject` (now a verified delete, not a phantom-ok bare delete); the existing "own projects all" RLS (FOR ALL on user_id) already scopes it. **Adversarial review (ecc:code-reviewer) caught a real HIGH:** `useConfirm()` returns the confirm fn directly (AppShell does `const confirm = useConfirm()`), so my `const { confirm } = useConfirm()` yielded `undefined` and would have thrown on every delete at runtime ŌĆö **and the Vite build never caught it because esbuild strips types without checking.** Folded that + two LOWs (verified delete, partial index), and a separate `tsc`-only error the source review couldn't see: the TanStack server-fn boundary rejects a `Record<string, unknown>` return as non-serializable, so `ProductExport` now uses a recursive JSON-safe type. **Verification: `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real type gate ŌĆö `bun run build` alone is not), `bunx eslint` clean, `bun run build` green.** Collision-free from the parallel engine lane (owns AppShell, which keeps only its bare sidebar delete). **Files:** `src/components/product/PortfolioBoard.tsx`, `supabase/migrations/20260617120000_b5_project_archive.sql` new; **H2 ┬Ę Outcome roadmap (Now/Next/Later) ŌĆö SHIPPED to `main`.** Built the outcome/commitment layer over the agent-ranked opportunities, as a **Roadmap tab on `/product`** (`?tab=roadmap`). This is explicitly NOT the task/sprint kanban that v6 deleted: the human _commits_ an opportunity to a Now/Next/Later bucket and declares an **outcome** (what changes) + a **measure** (how we know), and the agent's continuous ICE ranking orders the cards _within_ each bucket. Reconciled the v6 `/roadmap` deletion this way (outcome curation, not manual sequencing) rather than reviving the kanban. **Build:** a four-column board (Backlog ┬Ę Now ┬Ę Next ┬Ę Later) with native HTML5 drag (no `@dnd-kit` ŌĆö that dep isn't installed and the supply-chain guard would block adding it), optimistic move (onMutate snapshot ŌåÆ onError rollback ŌåÆ onSettled invalidate), and inline outcome/measure edit per card. **Data:** new `roadmap.functions.ts` ŌĆö `getRoadmap` reads `select("*")` so it is **pre-migration tolerant** (until the next Lovable sync adds the columns, every opportunity reads as unplaced and sits in the backlog; reads never error), and `updateRoadmapItem` patches the three roadmap columns. Migration `20260617000000_h2_roadmap_outcome.sql` adds `roadmap_bucket` (CHECK now/next/later) + `roadmap_outcome` + `roadmap_measure` to `opportunities`, idempotent, with a partial index on committed items; the existing "own opportunities all" RLS policy (FOR ALL on user*id) already scopes the new columns, so no new policy. **Adversarial review (3 fixes folded):** (1) the write now does `.eq("user_id", ŌĆ”).select("id")` and throws if zero rows return, so an RLS-blocked or no-match update fails loudly instead of returning a phantom `ok:true` that would leave the optimistic UI lying; (2) added a keyboard/click bucket `<select>` per card (aria-labeled) so bucket-moves aren't drag-only (a11y); (3) the inline edit now resets its outcome/measure fields on save so a stale value can't leak into the next card opened. **Gate:** the place-into-bucket \_write* needs the migration, so it activates on the next Lovable sync; the board reads and renders today (everything in backlog). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bunx eslint` clean on all three files. Built collision-free from the parallel engine lane (`/product` + new files only; no AppShell/CommandPalette/Govern). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260617000000_h2_roadmap_outcome.sql`, `src/lib/roadmap.functions.ts`, `src/components/product/RoadmapBoard.tsx` new; `src/routes/_authenticated.product.tsx` (Roadmap tab wiring); `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

**OPS-01 follow-up ┬Ę Flow audio reworked from synthesis to real recordings + a custom timer (founder feedback).** The founder tested the shipped Flow mode and found all three synthesized presets (Rain/Wind/Deep, filtered white noise) harsh, which defeats a calm-focus feature. Reworked the audio engine: `src/lib/flow/soundscape.ts` is now a real-audio buffer player that fetches one looped recording per preset, decodes it once, loops it gaplessly via Web Audio (an HTMLAudioElement loop seams audibly), and crossfades on preset change with volume on a master gain. New presets are Rain/Ocean/Forest/Lo-fi/Heartbeat. The files live in `public/soundscape/<preset>.mp3` and are sourced separately, because I could not autonomously fetch great, no-attribution, loopable, license-clear audio (Pixabay is gated/403; Wikimedia Commons quality was poor and attribution-encumbered) and cannot audition for quality, so committing scraped audio would be a legal + quality risk. `start()` now resolves a boolean; when a file is absent the preset shows "This sound has no track yet" and stays silent while the rest of Flow mode (dim, timer, quieting) still works. Also added the requested **custom focus length**: a clamped minutes field (1 to 240) beside the 25/50/90/Open chips. `public/soundscape/README.md` documents the exact filenames, royalty-free/CC0 sources, and a per-file license-provenance table. **Verification:** 21 `bun test` green (+4 new: `presetSrc`, `clampMinutes`), `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean (same pre-existing provider+hook react-refresh warning), humanization gate clean, dev server serves `/` 200 with no errors. **Decision:** logged in `session-decisions.md` (reverses the original "synthesized in-browser" OPS-01 choice). **Files:** `src/lib/flow/{soundscape.ts,session.ts}` (+`session.test.ts`), `src/hooks/use-flow-mode.tsx`, `src/components/cadence/FlowWidget.tsx`, `public/soundscape/README.md` new; `docs/features/flow-mode.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, this log.

A guarded sweep swapped ~171 brand references across ~40 files (the capitalized brand token plus two HTTP user-agent strings; `git mv` of the v3 positioning file to `v3-positioning-cadence.md`), while genuine engineering terms (the cache fall-through and provider-resilience patterns) were deliberately protected by swapping only the capitalized brand form. **OPS-01 ┬Ę Flow mode (ambient calm-state) ŌĆö SHIPPED.** A one-click calm operating stance, living in the `AppShell` sidebar footer beside the theme toggle (chrome, not Today ŌĆö it's a global stance, so the home-and-today IA rubric puts it in the chrome). Turning it on dims the sidebar + TopBar (`html.flow`, lifting on hover; main content stays full), plays a synthesized ambient soundscape (Web Audio, no audio files: Rain/Wind/Deep presets are filtered looping noise with a slow LFO, + volume), runs a focus timer (25/50/90/open) that chimes and auto-exits at zero, and **quiets non-urgent notifications**. Quieting is the one structural piece: a `lib/notify.ts` facade re-exports `toast` with sonner's exact API, so a mechanical one-line import swap across **44 files** (`sonner` ŌåÆ `@/lib/notify`) routes every toast through it; while flow is on, success/info/message/default toasts are held in a buffer and replayed as one summary line on exit (`While you were focused ┬Ę N updates`), while errors/warnings (and anything `{critical:true}`) always pass through. State mirrors `use-theme.tsx` (context + `localStorage` + a documentElement class); no server table. A session resumes across reload (audio re-arms on a tap, per the browser autoplay policy). Engine-Room stamp recorded in the spec. **G3 engine lane ŌĆö adversarial review + 4 fixes (closeout).** Ran an `ecc:typescript-reviewer` correctness+security pass over the riskiest pieces (J2 merge gate, K1 release notes, I1 hunk apply). Fixed: **(HIGH/J2)** the CI gate fetched check-runs at `per_page=50` with no pagination, so a failing check beyond #50 (common in matrix builds) could read as green and let a red PR merge ŌĆö the dangerous false-allow direction; now `per_page=100` plus a fail-safe block when `total_count` exceeds the page (refuses rather than risks a false allow). **(HIGH/J2)** a closed-but-unmerged PR fell through to the GitHub merge call and returned a misleading "conflicts or pending checks" 405; now a clear `state != "open"` guard throws first. **(MED/I1)** stale hunk-ids from the UI under a concurrent edit could silently corrupt staged content (positional ids shift if `new_content` changed); added optimistic concurrency ŌĆö the UI passes the row's `updated_at` as `expectedUpdatedAt` and the server's UPDATE is conditional on it, returning a refresh-and-retry conflict instead of writing wrong content. **(MED/K1)** uncapped `studio_changeset_revisions.message` text flowed verbatim into the release-notes prompt (injection surface); each commit message is now capped to 500 chars (matching the work-order cap). The reviewer confirmed the rest correct: `overallFromChecks` priority ordering, `mergeReadinessFromCi` exhaustiveness, the `!merged` guard + gate placement outside `withIdempotency`, `applyHunkSelection` round-trips, the status='staged' guards, and K1 RLS tenancy. `bun test` 146 green, `bun run build` green. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (J2 gate), `src/lib/studio.functions.ts` (K1 cap + I1 concurrency), `src/components/studio/ChangesPanel.tsx` (I1 `expectedUpdatedAt`), active-task (closeout + post-deploy verify gate), this log.

**G3 / I1b ŌĆö Studio changeset revision history ŌĆö DONE (revert deferred). Engine lane complete.** Each `studio.commit` now records an atomic revision so the operator sees a changeset's commit history in-platform (not only on GitHub). Built: (1) migration `20260616230000_i1b_studio_revisions.sql` ŌĆö `studio_changeset_revisions` (changeset_id FK, revision_no, commit_sha, commit_url, message, files jsonb), RLS mirroring `studio_changes` (workspace via parent changeset), UNIQUE(changeset_id, revision_no) + index. (2) In `registry.server.ts` `studio.commit`, after the commit succeeds, a best-effort insert of the next revision (revision_no = count+1, sha/url/message + the file set), gated on `!outcome.cached` so an idempotency replay never double-records and wrapped in try/catch so a missing table (pre-sync) or any error never breaks shipping. (3) `getChangesetRevisions` read fn + `StudioRevision` type in `studio.functions.ts` (RLS-scoped, newest first). (4) A compact "Revisions (N)" strip in `ChangesPanel.tsx` (r-number, message, file count, short sha linking to the GitHub commit); the query degrades to a hidden strip if the table is absent pre-sync. **G3 / I1 (per-hunk accept/reject) ŌĆö operator curation of a staged changeset ŌĆö DONE; revision history deferred (I1b).** Multi-file staging already shipped (`studioStage`, up to 20 files); the gap was operator control before the gated commit (all-or-nothing). Built: (1) pure `src/lib/ai/studio-hunks.ts` ŌĆö `computeHunks(base, modified)` (LCS line diff to stable-id hunks) + `applyHunkSelection(base, modified, rejectedIds)` (rejected hunks revert to base; no rejections reconstructs `modified` exactly, all rejections reconstructs `base`), 11 tests incl. round-trips, partial accept, trailing-newline, create/delete edges. (2) Two workspace-scoped server fns in `studio.functions.ts`, gated to `status='staged'` (cannot curate after commit, since the content is then on the branch): `applyStagedHunkSelection` (recompute `new_content` from the rejected set via the same pure fn the UI used, so hunk ids line up) and `rejectStagedFile` (drop a whole file). (3) `ChangesPanel.tsx` UI (engine lane owns it; the I2 watch-lane must not touch it): when the changeset is `staged`, each file shows its hunks with tap-to-reject + an Apply button, plus a Reject-file button; refetches via partial key `["studio-session"]` so it stays decoupled from the I2 route. **G3 / J1 + J2 (honest path) ŌĆö test-authoring discipline + CI-green merge gate ŌĆö DONE.** Founder ruling: the Studio engine is GitHub-API-only (no Cadence execution sandbox), so a `studio.test.run` runner + `studio_test_runs` table would be speculative; tests run in the connected repo's GitHub Actions CI, which `github.ci.read` already reads. So the honest decomposition: J1 = the agent AUTHORS tests; J2 = enforce CI-green-before-merge. **J1:** migration `20260616220000_j1_studio_test_discipline.sql` rewrites the Studio (`builder`) agent system prompt to make test-authoring an explicit step (step 4 "INCLUDE TESTS", step 2 "note how the repo runs tests", step 7 "the tests you added") and restates the CI-green-before-merge loop; `CREATE OR REPLACE seed_default_agents` (other 3 agents reproduced verbatim, Studio prompt via `$studio$` dollar-quoting) for new users + a scoped `UPDATE ... WHERE slug='builder'` backfill for existing. Applies on the next Lovable sync. **J2:** new pure `src/lib/ai/studio-ci.ts` (`overallFromChecks` derives the verdict, `mergeReadinessFromCi` decides merge-readiness; 12 tests), now the single source of truth shared with `github.ci.read` (its inline derivation replaced). `studio.pr.merge` does a fresh CI read before merging and throws `MergeBlocked` while CI is red or pending (a Cadence-level gate independent of GitHub required-checks), kept outside `withIdempotency` so a blocked attempt re-checks each time and only a green merge caches. The gate is fail-safe (only ever blocks, never wrongly allows). With the J1 fix-on-red prompt, the self-correct loop closes without speculative orchestration. Known limit: a perpetually-queued check reads `pending` forever and blocks Cadence-merge (operator merges on GitHub if needed). **Verification:** `studio-ci.test.ts` 12/12, full `bun test` 135 green, `bun run build` green. Migration unverifiable live until Lovable sync (Supabase MCP unauthenticated here), like every migration in this repo. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/studio-ci.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new, `supabase/migrations/20260616220000_j1_studio_test_discipline.sql` new, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (import + shared verdict + merge gate + tool description), dashboard/active-task/this log.

**G3 / I3 ŌĆö branch isolation per mission, collision-safe branch naming ŌĆö DONE.** The Studio build engine already isolates concurrent missions well: per-path `builder_file_claims` (a second mission touching the same file gets a typed `BuilderFileConflict`, claims auto-released on merge/terminal), a per-mission `studio/*` branch, idempotent commit/PR/merge, and a clean openŌåÆsquash-mergeŌåÆrelease path. The one latent isolation bug: the branch fallback `studio/${missionId.slice(0,8)}` truncated the mission UUID to 32 bits, so two concurrent missions whose UUIDs shared a leading hex prefix would compute the SAME branch and silently build on each other's head (the file-claim guard only catches same-FILE collisions, not two missions sharing a branch with different files). Fixed by binding the branch to the changeset's own UUID: new pure `src/lib/ai/studio-branch.ts` `studioBranchName(missionId, changesetId)` ŌåÆ `studio/<mission8>-<changeset12>`, an always-valid single git ref segment, now the only place the branch name is computed (`registry.server.ts` `studio.commit`). Backward-compatible: only the first-commit fallback changed; existing changesets keep their persisted `branch`, and no consumer recomputes the name (`studio.functions.ts` reads `changeset.branch` from the DB). No migration. **Verification:** new `studio-branch.test.ts` 6/6 (incl. the explicit regression: two missions sharing an 8-hex prefix now get different branches), full `bun test` 123 green, `bun run build` green. Engine-core lane, serial; next J1. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/studio-branch.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (import + branch line), dashboard/active-task/this log.

**M-A Slice 1 ┬Ę Autonomy on Today (the observing -> proving -> trusted progression made visible) ŌĆö BUILT (working tree).** The trust progression was real in the data (the per-agent arc + the Gauntlet's autonomy ratio) but invisible on the home surface, so the "ambient" claim rang hollow. New pure `src/lib/autonomy-progression.ts` (+`.test.ts`, 8 cases: boundaries at 1/3 and 2/3, ordering, a guard that the copy never says "promote") reuses the existing server fn rather than a new query layer. **Review:** a 3-lens adversarial workflow (honesty/claim-vs-wiring, correctness/edge-cases, design-system) raised 23, adversarially verified down to a confirmed set; folded the real fixes (an em-dash placeholder removed, my new code-comment em-dashes scrubbed, and a comment that wrongly said "no auto-advance exists" corrected, since the per-agent arc does auto-advance via `auto_advance_agent_arc`). **Viral loop ┬Ę per-IP rate limit on the public `/d/<slug>` page ŌĆö DONE (closes the one deferred gate before heavy promotion).** The shareable-decision page was the only public, unauthenticated read surface with no rate limit (the explicitly-deferred item from the 2026-06-16 share-security re-verification). Added a per-IP cap on the anonymous `getPublicDecision` read: 600 reads / 1-hour rolling window per client IP, mirroring KI-10's ingest limiter shape. The guard runs _before_ the DB read, keyed on `cf-connecting-ip` (Cloudflare-set ŌåÆ unspoofable on the Workers deploy; `x-forwarded-for`/`x-real-ip` are dev fallbacks). It is **fail-open** by construction (any DB error or unresolved IP ŌåÆ the read proceeds), so the limiter can never make a legitimate shared link 404; a blocked caller sees the same "not available" page as a private/missing slug, which is fine because slugs are unguessable CSPRNG (this is anti-DoS, not anti-enumeration). The window/limit math is a pure `decidePublicReadRateLimit` with 7 `bun test` cases (boundary at exactly windowMs, increment, block + retry-after, count-overshoot race, custom params); the DB wrapper uses `onConflict: "client_ip"` on the UNIQUE key so a window reset UPDATEs rather than inserting a duplicate. Bundle-safety verified: the service-role `supabaseAdmin` import (a lazy Proxy) compiles into the server-only chunk and leaks nothing to the client bundle (grep-confirmed). **Verification:** `bun test` 108 green (+7), `bun run build` green, client bundle clean of `SERVICE_ROLE`/the limiter table. **Gate:** the migration applies on the next Lovable sync (until then `public_decision_rate_limits` doesn't exist, the checker fails open, and reads are unlimited ŌĆö exactly today's behavior). Built file-disjoint from the parallel M-A Slice 2 (Today) lane. **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616190000_p3_public_decision_ratelimit.sql`, `src/lib/decisions-ratelimit.server.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/decisions-share.functions.ts` (guard + IP resolver) edited; `docs/features/shareable-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C pricing and paywall foundation: plan tier + entitlements + billing surface + gated Stripe (BUILT, working tree).** The monetization foundation from v7 section 9. `workspaces` gains `plan_tier` (free/pro/team, default free), the two stripe ids, and `plan_updated_at`, with a `BEFORE INSERT OR UPDATE` trigger (`protect_workspace_billing_columns`) that makes the billing columns service-role-write-only: a non-service-role INSERT is forced to free with no billing ids, a non-service-role UPDATE preserves the prior values. So a free user cannot self-grant a paid plan by PATCHing or INSERTing the column directly (the `ws owner manage` RLS policy is FOR ALL, so both write paths had to be guarded, not just UPDATE). Pure `src/lib/entitlements.ts` (free does not persist memory, retention 14 days; pro and team persist forever; Critic-everywhere + team-only shared memory / approval lanes) with 9 `bun test` cases and a fail-safe `normalizePlanTier` that defaults unknown values to free. `src/lib/billing.functions.ts`: `getBillingState` (authed, pre-migration tolerant, defaults free) + owner-only `createCheckoutSession` (Stripe Checkout via the REST API over fetch, no SDK dependency, gated on `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` + a price id). `src/routes/api/stripe/webhook.ts` verifies the Stripe HMAC signature with Web Crypto + a replay window (accepts any of multiple v1 sigs for key rotation) and maps subscription state to `plan_tier` via the service-role client (gated on `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`; a 200 no-op until configured). A Settings -> Plan tab (`BillingTab`) shows the current plan, the three tiers, and an owner-only Upgrade CTA that degrades to an honest "billing not connected yet" until keys exist (nothing is charged). **Deferred on purpose:** the memory-expiry enforcement (free memory expiring) is kept out of this lane to stay file-disjoint from the parallel M-A Slice 2 (Today) work; it lands as a clean additive follow-up (an `expires_at` + a recall-path filter) after Slice 2. **Verification:** `bun test` 117 green (+9), `bun run build` green, client bundle grep-clean of `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` / service-role; a focused adversarial security review verdict was clean on the criticals (INSERT + UPDATE self-grant both closed) with one LOW folded in (the webhook now accepts any of multiple v1 signatures for key rotation). **Gate:** migration `20260616200000` applies on the next Lovable sync; live charging waits on the founder provisioning the Stripe secrets (`STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`, `STRIPE_PRICE_PRO`, `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`). Built file-disjoint from M-A Slice 2. **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616200000_mc_plan_tier.sql`, `src/lib/entitlements.ts` (+`.test.ts`), `src/lib/billing.functions.ts`, `src/routes/api/stripe/webhook.ts` new; `src/routes/_authenticated.settings.tsx` (Plan tab + `BillingTab`) edited; `docs/features/pricing.md` (new) + features index, `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C memory expiry: the "charge for memory persistence" gate is now enforced (BUILT, working tree).** The plan-tier foundation defined the entitlement (`memoryPersists`); this wires the mechanic. Free workspaces keep distilled `agent_memory` for 14 days then it expires; pro and team keep it forever. Implemented entirely additively so it never touched the parallel M-A Slice 2 files (which only added `ExecutedCard.tsx` + `today.functions.ts` + the Today route): a `BEFORE INSERT` trigger (`set_agent_memory_expiry`) stamps `agent_memory.expires_at` from the owner's plan (free = `created_at` + 14 days mirroring `FREE_MEMORY_RETENTION_DAYS`, pro/team = NULL), so the TS write path (`rememberOutcome`) is unchanged and pre-migration tolerant; the `match_agent_memory` recall RPC gains `AND (expires_at IS NULL OR expires_at > now())` so the loop never recalls expired memory (body copied verbatim from the P1 rescope with the one predicate added, security boundary `user_id = COALESCE(auth.uid(), for_user)` preserved); and the daily `memory-tick` cron hard-deletes expired rows (pre-migration tolerant: a missing-column error is ignored, the existing decay passes still run). Existing rows are grandfathered (`expires_at` NULL = never expires) so nothing is retroactively wiped, including the demo seed. **Adversarial review (NEEDS-FIXES, both folded before commit):** (A) a free user could self-grant permanent memory by inserting an explicit far-future `expires_at` (the trigger now only honors a client-supplied value for the service-role; every other caller has it recomputed from the plan, so the value is uncheatable); (B) non-owner team members got FREE expiry (the paid check now keys on `workspace_members` membership, not just `owner_id`, so owners and invited members of any pro/team workspace keep memory). Recall-boundary, trigger-cannot-break-inserts, paid-never-swept, and grandfathering all reviewed clean. **Verification:** `bun test` 117 green, `bun run build` green. **Gate:** migration `20260616210000` applies on the next Lovable sync, after `20260616200000` (plan_tier), in filename order. Built file-disjoint from M-A Slice 2 (which had already landed). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616210000_mc_memory_expiry.sql` new; `src/routes/api/public/hooks/memory-tick.ts` (expiry sweep) edited; `docs/features/pricing.md` (How it works + deferred flipped), `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C scope ruling: pricing ENGINE only, gates DORMANT at the prototype stage (founder, 2026-06-16).** The founder clarified that at this working-prototype stage we build the pricing engine (plan tiers, entitlements as data, billing surface, Stripe plumbing) but do NOT wire active paywall gates yet, since the product itself is not fully built. So the memory-expiry enforcement shipped just above (the only active gate) is made dormant rather than reverted: a `memory_expiry_enabled()` SQL flag (returns false) gates the stamp trigger, so while off every memory row stays `expires_at = NULL` (never expires) and the recall filter + the `memory-tick` sweep are automatic no-ops. The code is built and reviewed; flip the flag (`CREATE OR REPLACE ... SELECT true`) when ready to enforce. Critic-everywhere and other entitlement gates are explicitly NOT wired now. The entitlements map still documents the intended per-tier policy as pure data (nothing reads it to block). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616210000_mc_memory_expiry.sql` (flag + trigger guard), `docs/features/pricing.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.
