**H3 ┬Ę Scheduling ŌĆö calendar-aware deep-work blocks ŌĆö SHIPPED to `main` (Feature Dashboard pick, claimed before building, adversarially reviewed).** The Calendar surface gains a **"Plan deep work"** action: a new read-only `proposeWorkBlocks` server fn fits the operator's open deep-work tasks (`is_deep_work`, not done) into free time within their working hours, reusing the proven `proposeSlots` conflict logic ŌĆö one block per task, back to back across the next working days, skipping weekends, hours outside the profile's working window, and existing calendar events. It is a pure proposal (never writes); each proposed block has an "Add to calendar" affordance that creates the event via `createCalendarEvent`. **Honest by construction:** it only schedules what genuinely fits, so a packed calendar yields fewer (or zero) blocks with an honest empty state, never a forced plan. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bunx eslint` clean; Playwright-verified live both ways ŌĆö the empty state ("Nothing to scheduleŌĆ”") on the demo (no open deep-work tasks), and the populated path (temporarily relaxing the deep-work filter, then reverting) produced 6 correct back-to-back hourly blocks (Wed 9amŌĆō2pm) all inside working hours, correctly starting the NEXT working day because it was already past 6pm. **Adversarial review (2-lens workflow, ultracode):** surfaced one real HIGH bug ŌĆö the working-hours boundary used the truncated `getHours()`, so a block from a :30 cursor could overrun `whEnd` by up to the block length (e.g. 17:30ŌåÆ18:30 past a 6pm end); fixed by comparing the block END in minutes in **both** `proposeWorkBlocks` and the pre-existing `proposeSlots` (same one-line bug, same file). Also fixed a MEDIUM: a user-facing em-dash in the empty-state copy (humanized hard gate). A LOW timezone limitation (server-UTC hour checks, shared with `proposeSlots`) was already disclosed in the doc comment and left as a separate platform fix. All-new fn + the Calendar panel; **collision-free** with the parallel lanes (Today/Govern/studio). Dashboard row flipped to Ō£ģ, G2 at-a-glance updated (Done 5ŌåÆ6, Pending 3ŌåÆ2). Live on the next Lovable Publish. **Files:** `src/lib/calendar.functions.ts` (`proposeWorkBlocks` new + the boundary fix in `proposeSlots`), `src/components/knowledge/CalendarPanel.tsx` ("Plan deep work" + the blocks panel), `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-15 ┬Ę `M-0 ┬Ę orchestrated missions were completing HOLLOW; root-caused live and fixed (the real mission-run blocker)`.** Live re-verification of the prior gating fix on the hosted app (Project GlassWing, demo account) confirmed that fix works (no new control-flow approvals queued) but surfaced a deeper, separate defect: every orchestrated mission finished with 0 steps and 0 hops yet was labeled "completed". A full live trace (`6471cbaa`, 10 hops, 21,183 tokens) proved the cause and ruled out the governance-halt theory (kill-switch off, real tokens spent): the orchestrator's `mission.plan` planner emits a colloquial agent slug (`discovery`), but the seeded roster slug is `discovery-scout` (the same slug drift the 2026-06-14 migration standardized on the event-reactor path), and `mission.plan`'s strict exact-match validator threw on the miss, dropping the WHOLE plan; the orchestrator then observed 0 steps, retried, and finalized "unresolvable internal planning", after which the cron completed the 0-step mission. That is why missions never "hopped". **Fix, two layers:** (1) `mission.plan` (`orchestrator.server.ts`) now resolves each planned slug against the live roster (exact, then a single unambiguous prefix or substring match) so `discovery` maps to `discovery-scout` instead of dropping the plan, throwing clearly only when a slug is genuinely unresolvable; (2) `maybeCompleteMission` (`handoff.server.ts`) now marks a never-planned (0-step) terminal mission `failed` (retryable) instead of hollow-`completed`, and skips decision-capture for it, so any future zero-plan cause surfaces loudly rather than as a fake "done". **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green. **Live re-verification pending the next Lovable deploy** (the fix cannot be observed on the hosted app until it deploys). **Infra note:** confirmed with the founder we keep ONE Lovable-managed Supabase (no new account, no DB fork); schema continues to flow through `supabase/migrations/*` applied by Lovable. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/handoff.server.ts`; `docs/planning/{known-issues.md,v7-build-status.md}`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 ┬Ę `M-0 ┬Ę orchestrator control-flow tools no longer approval-gated (the live mission-stall fix)`.** Live end-to-end verification on the hosted app (the M-0 exit gate) surfaced the real blocker, which neither the migration sync nor code review had: a freshly launched orchestrated mission stalled. Root-caused via a recon workflow plus a live server-fn response-trace capture (Playwright): the orchestrator's OWN control-flow tools (`mission.plan`, `mission.dispatch`) were being sent to the approval queue at the `observing` arc (`resolveApprovalMode` forces auto to review there), so the plan never persisted; the orchestrator then observed zero steps and finalized with "mission steps are not being registered". The 7 stuck Today approvals were exactly these expired queued plan/dispatch calls. Founder ruling: orchestration control-flow tools always run inline. **Fix:** a new `ORCHESTRATION_CONTROL_FLOW_TOOLS` allowlist (`mission.plan/dispatch/observe/finalize`) at the single loop gate (`loop.server.ts:647-665`) bypasses approval creation for those four (no external side effect; `mission.dispatch` only enqueues child runs; the specialists' real-world tools stay gated per arc on the child runs; kill-switch/budget/guardrails still apply because they live in `callModel` upstream of the gate). **Plus three defense-in-depth guards** (the RCA + its adversarial verifier showed a completion-guard alone was insufficient and could strand a mission): the `agent_runs` insert now throws on error (no silent 0-run loop); `startOrchestratedMission` marks the mission `halted` on a thrown launch before re-throwing (so the UI retry, gated on failed/halted, fires instead of leaving it `running`); and `maybeCompleteMission` no longer silently completes a zero-step mission unless a terminal orchestrator run exists (closing the hollow-completion the RCA found, without stranding, since a failed launch now goes to `halted`). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green, adversarial review safe-to-land (allowlist exact, governance not bypassed, no mission stranding); diff scrutinized at the gate. **Live re-verification pending the Lovable deploy of this commit** (the fix cannot be observed on the hosted app until it deploys). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/{loop.server,trust.server,handoff.server}.ts`, `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`; this log + `active-task.md`.

- **2026-06-14 ┬Ę `M-0 #4 ┬Ę humanizeText() runtime sanitizer`.** The hard gate from the humanized-output convention (Level 2) is now wired at the AI chokepoint, so the platform's generated prose carries no machine fingerprints. New pure `src/lib/ai/humanize.ts` (`humanizeText`) segments prose from fenced and inline code, normalizes em/en dashes to honest ASCII by context (a numeric range like 1-6 becomes "1 to 6"; a separator dash becomes a comma), strips the convention's invisible and exotic-space set, collapses double spaces, trims trailing whitespace; its own source spells the code points as escapes so it stays fingerprint-free and lint-clean. Wired into `runtime.server.ts`: `callModel` humanizes prose output, `callModelStream` humanizes on a line-buffered, fence-aware boundary (`createStreamHumanizer` holds an open fenced block until it closes, so streamed concatenation equals `humanizeText(whole)`), plus a soft `HUMANIZE_DIRECTIVE` on prose system prompts (`prompts.server.ts`). JSON is never touched: every gate keys on `responseFormat !== 'json_object'` and `callModel` parses JSON off the raw text, so the agent loop and all tool JSON stay byte-exact. The per-lane adversarial reviewer ran 164 probe assertions (streaming-equals-whole-text, prefix stability, purity, idempotence, JSON parse-safety) and caught one real gap: `lineage.functions.ts` (PRD to task-graph) returned `{"tasks":[...]}` without declaring json-mode, so the sanitizer would have rewritten task-title strings; fixed by adding `responseFormat: 'json_object'`. The eval-runner subject call is intentionally left humanized (its output is scored as a string, never parsed, so evaluating the shipped form is correct). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green (+27 humanize cases), eslint clean on all touched files. Takes effect on deploy (no migration). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/humanize.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/{runtime.server,prompts.server}.ts`, `src/lib/lineage.functions.ts` edited; `docs/conventions/humanized-output.md`, `docs/planning/v7-build-status.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.
- **2026-06-14 ┬Ę `M-0 ┬Ę KI-19 enabled-agent dispatch hole closed`.** A latent gap the slug-drift RCA surfaced: `resolveAgent` (`handoff.server.ts`) resolved a target agent by slug with no `enabled` filter, so a disabled or off-roster agent could still be dispatched a child run (via the `agent.handoff` tool or the mission dispatcher, which both route through that one chokepoint). Fixed at the chokepoint: `resolveAgent` now filters `enabled = true` and throws a clear, slug-named error (`Target agent 'X' is disabled or not in the roster`) when nothing enabled matches. The throw is caught per step, by `failOrRequeueStep` on the dispatcher path and by the agent loop on the tool path, so a bad target terminalizes one step instead of crashing a run; the orchestrator sender lookup keeps its null-sender fallback, so enabled specialists are unaffected. `agents.enabled` is `BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true`, so the filter has no null footgun. Adversarial review verdict safe-to-land, no code edits needed. **Residual (logged as KI-20):** two adjacent surfaces still resolve agents without an enabled filter, the run-start path in `loop.server.ts` (an already-queued run whose target was disabled in the gap) and the operator-initiated `runAgent` direct invocation. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green, eslint clean. - **2026-06-14 ┬Ę `M-0 ┬Ę unseeded-slug drift sealed (doc-loop + RCA correction)`.** The migration shipped in `5b0b0b93ea`; this entry completes its doc loop and corrects the record. The tracker had claimed the orchestrator prompt's stale slugs made `mission.plan` throw and kill any sensing-step mission. A 10-agent adversarial root-cause (workflow `wf_71a7dc78`: 6 readers, a synthesizer, 3 refuters) disproved it: `mission.plan` plans against the live enabled roster and re-validates (`orchestrator.server.ts:125,173-179`), so it never deterministically throws. The real deterministic defect was on the event-reactor path: `seed_default_event_subscriptions` seeded `signal.created` to slug `'discovery'`, but the roster slug is `discovery-scout`, so `dispatchEvent` (`reactor.functions.ts:222`) threw "Target agent not found" for every new account, killing the autonomous `signal.created` SENSE fan-out (fault-isolated, the `event_queue` row just marks failed, which is why it stayed silent). Migration `20260614200000` fixes it in three parts: `CREATE OR REPLACE seed_default_event_subscriptions` targeting `discovery-scout`; a scoped backfill `UPDATE` of existing default rows (the function only inserts WHEN NOT EXISTS); and `CREATE OR REPLACE seed_orchestrator_agent` to drop the stale example slugs from the prompt. - **2026-06-14 ŌĆö `v6 Phase 3 ┬Ę slice 1 / Track 2` ŌĆö the Gauntlet: the three north-star proof metrics, instrumented on a real surface (honest empty states), built in a parallel worktree then hardened by a 12-finding adversarial review before landing.** New `/govern?tab=gauntlet` tab (inserted after Analytics) with three cards, each a real computation over owner-scoped tables ŌĆö no fabricated numbers; sparse windows read "not enough data yet." **A ┬Ę Acceptance rate** (`getAcceptanceRate`): `accepted/(accepted+rejected)` over DECIDED rows (`decided_at` set) where accepted = status Ōłł {approved, executed, failed} ŌĆö an approved call that then ran (resolveApprovalŌåÆexecuteApproval flips approvedŌåÆexecuted/failed) is still an acceptance, so the worktree agent's first cut (count only `status='approved'`) read artificially low; review caught it, fixed at the DB layer + in the 7d-vs-prior-7d trend. The user rollup of the per-agent acceptance already in `ai/trust.server.ts`. **C ┬Ę Autonomy ratio** (`getAutonomyRatio`): `unattended/(unattended+gated)` where unattended = SUCCESSFUL (`ok=true`) side-effecting `tool_calls` rows (a failed inline attempt isn't carried work ŌĆö review fix) and gated = side-effecting `agent_approvals` rows, side-effecting decided by `isSideEffectingTool()` (`tool-consequences.ts`); copy is explicit that rising ŌēĀ no-human (the gated count is exactly the work that still comes to you). **B ┬Ę Ritual retention** (`getRitualRetention`): distinct days-active 7/14/30 + current streak from the new `ritual_sessions` table, plus an on-the-fly, user-wide real-vs-demo signal (Ōēź1 connected `connections` row OR Ōēź1 `signals` row) that returns null (the tag is omitted) if its probe errors, rather than mislabeling a real account "demo" (review fix). **Pre-migration-tolerant:** the `ritual_sessions` read catches a missing-relation error (`42P01`/`42703`/`PGRST205`/"relation does not exist") and returns `tableReady:false` ŌåÆ card reads "not enough data yet" rather than throwing (same probe idiom as `mission-advance.server.ts:hasRetryColumns`). Today (`_authenticated.index.tsx`) fires `recordRitualSession` once on mount (ref-guarded) ŌĆö never blocks render, swallows table-missing/any failure; the write is an idempotent per-UTC-day upsert (unique `(user_id, opened_on)`) so repeated opens never accumulate, and `workspace_id` is left null (a client id isn't trusted ŌĆö cross-tenant; all three review fixes). - **2026-06-14 ŌĆö `v6 Phase 2 ┬Ę W2 + W3` ŌĆö autonomy made legible: the loop's unattended work is audited, the A2A contract is hardened, and the moat is on the cockpit.** Grounded by two parallel Explore sweeps (which caught that the `/swarm` Swarm HUD already IS the "agents at work" OS view ŌĆö so we enriched it instead of building a redundant `/system` route). **W2 ŌĆö "Executed unattended" audit:** the trust arc already executes write tools inline at trusted/ambient; this surfaces it honestly. `getMission` now flags each `HopToolCall.is_unattended` via the new client-safe `isSideEffectingTool()` (`src/lib/tool-consequences.ts`), and `/missions/$id` renders an "Executed unattended" card (between the gate ŌĆö _what needs you_ ŌĆö and the trace ŌĆö _what already ran_), each row showing the tool's catalogued effect + reversibility + ok/latency. **Correctness crux (verified by review):** every `tool_calls` row is an inline auto-execution ŌĆö gated tools queue an `agent_approvals` row and `executeApproval` updates the approval, never writing `tool_calls` ŌĆö so a side-effecting `tool_calls` row is _provably_ unattended (claim-never-outruns-wiring holds). **W3 ŌĆö A2A hardening + moat visibility:** (a) `enqueueHandoff` (`handoff.server.ts`) now validates `payload.memory_refs[]` against real `agent_memory` ids the user owns, dropping phantom refs before they reach a receiver's prompt (best-effort: a transient query error keeps refs as-is, never strips valid ones; works under both the user client and the admin sweeper). (b) `getSwarmHud` gains `outcomes_remembered` (count of `agent_memory` kind='outcome' ŌĆö the W1 moat output) surfaced as "N outcomes in memory" in the Agents-tab HUD header (cumulative, placed apart from the "last hour" throughput strip so it never reads as a rate). Artifacts left free-form by design (validated on use by the receiver's tools). **Adversarial review (1 agent) confirmed the core correctness + found 2 honesty issues, both fixed:** added the two genuinely-missing side-effecting tools to the consequence catalogue (`tasks.update_status`, `research.synthesize` ŌĆö so the audit doesn't under-report), and replaced a blanket "each is undoable" subtitle with per-row reversibility (some auto tools are only partly reversible). **Verification:** `bun test` 23 green, `bun run build` green, lint clean; no blast radius (`is_unattended`/`outcomes_remembered` each have exactly one constructor). **Files:** `src/lib/tool-consequences.ts`, `src/lib/missions.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `src/lib/ai/handoff.server.ts`, `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentsPanel.tsx`; docs: `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 ŌĆö `v6 Phase 2 ┬Ę W1` ŌĆö the memory moat is real: recorded outcomes now become memory the agents recall.** Phase 2's first demoable unit (the Decision-System moat, v6 ┬¦3 Pillar 2), grounded by an Explore sweep that found the loop was only _half_-wired: `recordOutcome` re-scored the opportunity ICE and wrote a `learnings` audit row, but that row lived in a table **no agent ever reads** ŌĆö `match_agent_memory` (the loop's recall) only reads `agent_memory`. So the product _showed_ "we learned this" while every agent stayed amnesiac (claim-outruns-wiring). Fix: on `recordOutcome`, after the learning insert, distil the outcome into a **global-scope, embedded `agent_memory` row** (`src/lib/ai/outcome-memory.ts` pure `buildOutcomeMemory`/`outcomeImportance` + `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` `rememberOutcome`), entity-linked in `metadata` to the prd/opportunity/learning. Because the row is `scope='global'`, `match_agent_memory`'s `m.scope='global'` clause returns it to a future run of **any** agent (when semantically relevant), and Phase 1's `memory_refs[]` threading carries it across hops ŌĆö so a Strategist re-encountering the opportunity now recalls "we shipped this; it was {verdict} (ICE {prior}ŌåÆ{new})." Importance 4 (decisive) / 3 (mixed) keeps it above the memory-tick decay floor. **Adversarial review (1 agent) found 4 real issues, all fixed:** (1) a null-embedding row is silently _unrecallable_ (the RPC hard-filters `embedding IS NOT NULL`) and there's no re-embed sweep ŌåÆ now we **skip the write entirely** rather than insert a ghost (also closes an `embedOne` sparse-return path); (2) the idempotency delete used `.eq("metadata->>source",ŌĆ”)` ŌĆö the repo's proven jsonb idiom is `.filter("col->>key","eq",ŌĆ”)` (per `today.functions.ts`/`traces.functions.ts`) ŌåÆ switched, so re-records replace not duplicate; (3) a clamped-confidence outcome could render a misleading "8.3ŌåÆ8.3" ICE move ŌåÆ the move line now guards on the _rounded_ values; (4) RLS/blast-radius confirmed safe (`recordOutcome`'s extra `memory_id` return field is ignored by `OutcomeCard`). **Verification:** `bun test` 23 green (9 new pure-policy tests incl. the rounding-honesty case), `bun run build` green, touched files prettier/eslint-clean. No new UI: the recall surfaces in any run's "Relevant memories from past sessions" prompt block + trace (and the existing Memory panel still shows the `learnings` audit). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/outcome-memory.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` (+`rememberOutcome`), `src/lib/outcome.functions.ts` (distil hook + title selects) edited; `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 ŌĆö `v6 Phase 1 (The Loop Runs Itself)` COMPLETE: autonomy, wired ŌĆö a multi-hop mission now runs unattended, retries transient hop failures, sizes its own step budget, and threads compounding memory across hops.** Closes the four gaps the runtime audit named (v6 Appendix B) ŌĆö _not_ with messaging, with code. Founder design rulings this session (AskUserQuestion, logged in session-decisions): auto-advance folds into the existing `resume-runs` sweeper (no new pg*cron ŌåÆ no migration-apply gate); hop retry is bounded (2 attempts + exponential backoff); the step budget is arc + mission-size aware. **(1) Deterministic auto-advance** ŌĆö new `src/lib/ai/mission-advance.server.ts` (`advanceMissionCore`): reflect child-run outcomes onto `mission_steps` ŌåÆ dispatch every newly-ready step ŌåÆ finalize a terminal DAG, all **model-free**. Key insight: the old `advanceMission` re-invoked the orchestrator \_LLM* each wave, but `mission.plan` already rejects re-planning, so that call only ever did mechanical observeŌåÆdispatchŌåÆfinalize ŌĆö replacing it with deterministic DB ops is cheaper, faster, and concurrency-safe while preserving behavior (the LLM now runs only for the initial plan). The per-minute `resume-runs` cron calls it for every running mission; the manual `advanceMission` server fn calls the same core; `mission.dispatch` (the orchestrator tool) routes through the shared `dispatchReadySteps`. **Claim-first CAS** (`plannedŌåÆdispatched` before enqueue) makes overlapping ticks safe from double-dispatch; a step stranded `dispatched` with null `run_id` (worker eviction mid-enqueue) is recovered after a 3-min window. **(2) Bounded hop retry** ŌĆö migration `20260614090000` adds `mission_steps.{attempts,max_attempts,next_retry_at}` and teaches `next_ready_mission_steps` the backoff window (identical signature, backward-compatible: NULL backoff = eligible now); pure policy in `src/lib/ai/retry.ts`. Pre-migration-tolerant via a per-isolate `hasRetryColumns` probe that only caches a genuine missing-column error (a transient blip re-probes), degrading to no-retry without ever throwing. **(3) Adaptive step budget** ŌĆö new `src/lib/ai/budget.ts` (`adaptiveStepBudget`) replaces the static `maxStepsFor`: role base + earned-trust headroom (`arc`) + orchestrator-scales-with-DAG-size, under a hard ceiling; orchestrator base kept at the proven 14 so the initial run never regresses (review catch). Threaded through `executeLoop` (both `runAgentLoop` + `resumeAgentLoop`) with a live `mission_steps` count. **(4) `memory_refs[]` populated** (the W5 contract field) ŌĆö new `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` (`recallMemoryRefs`) returns the `id`s the RPC already exposed; the loop's recall now writes `agent_memory.last_used_at` on every recall (decay input), and each dispatched hop threads relevant memory into the handoff payload. Migration `20260614091000` rescopes `match_agent_memory` to `COALESCE(auth.uid(), for_user)` so the **service-role sweeper path** actually matches semantic memory (was `auth.uid()`-only ŌåÆ null on the autonomous path ŌĆö the exact claim-outruns-wiring gap Phase 1 exists to close) while keeping the per-user security boundary (auth.uid() always wins). **Verification:** new `bun test` path (bun's built-in runner ŌĆö zero new deps, dodges the supply-chain guard) covers the pure budget/retry policy (14 tests green); `bun run build` green; touched files prettier/eslint-clean; a 2-agent adversarial review over the diff surfaced 10 findings ŌĆö 4 real (orchestrator budget regression, transient-error caching, stranded-dispatch recovery, the `match_agent_memory` `auth.uid()` gap), all fixed; 3 confidently wrong (verified against source ŌĆö one proposed "fix" would have introduced an infinite retry loop), rejected. **Gate (unchanged pattern):** the two P1 migrations apply on the next Lovable sync; until then retry is off and autonomous-path `memory_refs` carries reflections only ŌĆö both degrade gracefully. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/{mission-advance.server,memory.server,budget,retry}.ts` (+ `budget.test.ts`/`retry.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/{loop.server,handoff.server}.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/resume-runs.ts` edited; `supabase/migrations/{20260614090000_p1_mission_step_retry,20260614091000_p1_memory_recall_for_user}.sql` new; `package.json`/`tsconfig.json` (test path); `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/features/{loop-runs-itself.md(new),README.md}`, `docs/planning/known-issues.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-06 ŌĆö Bundle 9 Slices 2 + 3 shipped ŌĆö Builder now closes its own CI loop and runs safely in parallel. FND-RUNTIME 0.9 forced-restart playbook published.** **Slice 2 (CI loop):** two new built-in tools ŌĆö `github.ci.read` (`read`/`auto`: `GET /pulls/{n}` ŌåÆ head sha ŌåÆ `GET /commits/{sha}/check-runs` + `/status`; returns `{overall: pending|success|failure|neutral, checks[], head_sha, ŌĆ”}`; cached via `withIdempotency('github_ci', '<pr>-<head_sha>', ŌĆ”)` so re-polls don't burn quota and the cache invalidates naturally when the branch's head_sha moves) and `github.commit.append` (`write`/`confirm`: PUTs a single new file on the PR's head branch via Contents API; same `.github/` / `supabase/migrations/` / `.env` / lockfile deny-list as `github.pr.open`; wrapped in `withIdempotency('github_commit', a.idempotency_key, ŌĆ”)` keyed by `issue-<n>-fix-<k>`). The Builder system prompt now mandates: after `github.pr.open`, call `github.ci.read` up to 3├Ś per loop step; on `success`/`neutral` finalize; on `pending` finalize with a wait note and let `resume-runs` re-enter; on `failure` propose ONE follow-up `github.commit.append` whose message names the failing check, then finalize. `listBuilderRuns()` extended to surface the latest `github.ci.read` result per run and expose `failing.{name,html_url,summary}` so the `/build` card and `/missions/$id` timeline render a `CI ┬Ę green | red ┬Ę <check> | pending | n/a` chip that links to the failing check. **Slice 3 (conflict guard):** new `builder_file_claims` table ŌĆö `(user_id, workspace_id, run_id, mission_id, mission_title, repo, path, status, claimed_at, released_at, released_reason)` with a **partial unique index `(repo, path) WHERE status='held'`** so only one held claim per `(repo, path)` exists at a time; RLS = workspace members read, owner writes; PostgREST grants in the same migration. `github.pr.open` now INSERTs the claim row BEFORE the Contents-API PUT and surfaces a typed `BuilderFileConflict: path "<p>" is already claimed by another Builder mission ("<title>")` error on the unique violation ŌĆö second-mission PR never opens, no branch is created. New SECURITY DEFINER trigger `release_claims_for_terminal_run` (`AFTER UPDATE OF status ON agent_runs`) auto-releases every `held` claim for a run that hits `completed | completed_with_failures | halted | failed`. Operator can force-release via the new **Active file claims** panel on `/build` (5s refresh) which calls new server fn `releaseBuilderClaim({claim_id})` ŌĆö the Release button is only enabled for the claim owner. **FND-RUNTIME 0.9 playbook:** new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md` is the operator-driven verification ŌĆö start a Builder mission, restart the worker mid-loop, verify the resume-runs sweeper picks the run up within Ōēż60s, every idempotency-keyed external write (`github_pr`, `github_commit`, `github_ci`) returns its cached result, repo state matches the single-mission contract (one branch, one PR, one initial commit, optionally one fix commit). `docs/planning/foundation-audit.md` row 0.9 flipped ŌØī ŌåÆ ­¤¤Ī with a pointer to the playbook (Ō£ģ on a clean pass). **Docs loop closed in the same commit:** new `docs/features/bundle-9-builder.md` (canonical per-feature page covering Slice 1 + 2 + 3 ŌĆö demo script, verification per slice, tool contracts, governance, known limits), new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md`, both indexed in `docs/README.md` + `docs/features/README.md`; `architecture/orchestration.md` Bundle 9 paragraph extended with the new tools + claims ledger. **WHY:** Slice 1 proved the PlanŌåÆBuild hop end-to-end against a real repo but left two open gaps that block claim C2 ("one governed loop") at production volume ŌĆö (a) the Builder couldn't see whether its own PR passed CI, so the operator was still the test pipeline, and (b) two parallel missions could silently race on the same file, breaking the autonomy story the moment more than one PRD hit Builder. With Slices 2 + 3 in place the Builder closes its own loop on red and the conflict guard makes parallel Builder dispatch safe ŌĆö both are prerequisites for an operator-trustable autonomous build lane. **Out of scope this turn (queued):** `github.ci.logs` tool (Builder still only sees check name + summary, not raw job log), `github.pr.update` / `github.pr.merge` (operator owns merge), per-workspace `GITHUB_REPO` (still a single global secret), Restructure Phases 3ŌĆō4 (theme polish; operator deferred until feature tweaks settle), Proof Platform bundles 10ŌĆō12 (Ship ┬Ę Launch ┬Ę SupportŌåÆLearn). **Gotchas:** (1) the claim is held by `run_id`, so a single mission re-running `github.pr.open` (e.g. via the idempotency cache path) skips the conflict branch because the holder check matches `existing.run_id === runId`. (2) The CI cache key is `<pr>-<head_sha>`, so after `github.commit.append` lands a new commit the next `github.ci.read` call sees a new head_sha and bypasses the cache ŌĆö exactly what we want. (3) The auto-release trigger keys off `OLD.status IS DISTINCT FROM NEW.status` so a no-op UPDATE on a terminal run won't try to release already-released rows. (4) `releaseBuilderClaim` is RLS-scoped to the claim's `user_id` ŌĆö workspace peers can SEE the claim but cannot release each other's; this is intentional until we add a workspace-admin role. **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_builder_ci_loop_tools.sql` (Builder prompt + 2 new tool seeds + backfill), new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_builder_file_claims.sql` (claims table + index + grants + RLS + auto-release trigger), new `docs/features/bundle-9-builder.md`, new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (two new tools + claim acquire in `github.pr.open`), `src/lib/build.functions.ts` (CI surface in `listBuilderRuns`, new `listBuilderClaims` + `releaseBuilderClaim`), `src/routes/_authenticated.build.tsx` (CI chip + active-claims panel), `docs/README.md`, `docs/features/README.md`, `docs/planning/foundation-audit.md`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `plan.md`.

- **2026-06-06 ŌĆö F-AGENT-4: Swarm HUD + per-feature demo/operator docs pattern.** Closes the agent-ecosystem bundle. New route `/swarm` (nav slot: Agents ŌåÆ Swarm HUD, between Missions and Prompt Studio) is a single read-only governor's cockpit over the existing substrate ŌĆö no new tables, no new tools, no new mutations. One server fn `getSwarmHud()` in `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts` parallel-fires every read (RLS-scoped to `auth.uid()` + workspace via `current_user_default_workspace`): agents + latest non-terminal `agent_runs` per agent (priority `running > paused > queued > terminal`) joined to `agent_autonomy.arc`; missions filtered to `planning|running|completed_with_failures` OR `completed_at >= now()-1h` with `mission_steps` `done/total/failed` aggregates; last 50 `agent_messages` for the handoff feed; pending `agent_approvals`; last 50 `event_queue` rows; throughput from `ai_events` last 60 min bucketed in JS into 5-min windows (count, sum `est_cost_usd`, p50 `latency_ms`); `guardrail_hits` count for the same hour. The page (`src/routes/_authenticated.swarm.tsx`) refreshes every 2s via TanStack Query (`refetchIntervalInBackground: false`), composes 7 inline section components, and has error + not-found boundaries. Writes are zero net-new: inline Approve/Reject calls `resolveApproval` from `governance.functions.ts`; Dispatch/Skip on pending `confirm` reactor rows calls `decideEventDispatch` from `reactor.functions.ts`. **Docs pattern alongside the build:** new `docs/features/` folder with one canonical operator/demo page per shipped feature ŌĆö `docs/features/README.md` (index + template), `f-agent-1-orchestrator.md`, `f-agent-2-memory-reflection.md`, `f-agent-3-event-reactor.md` (backfilled, ~80 lines each, consolidated from the existing plan ┬¦4 entries + architecture bullets ŌĆö no new claims), and `f-agent-4-swarm-hud.md` (full). Each follows the same skeleton: What it does ┬Ę Why ┬Ę Where to find ┬Ę Demo script Ōēż 90s ┬Ę How it works ┬Ę Governance & guardrails ┬Ę Verification checklist ┬Ę Limits ┬Ę Related. `docs/README.md` got a new "Per-feature operator & demo guides" section linking the four pages. **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 made Cadence plan, F-AGENT-2 made it learn, F-AGENT-3 made it react ŌĆö together they produce more concurrent activity than the operator can track from four separate surfaces (`/missions`, `/inbox`, `/agents`, `/governance`). The HUD makes governance scale with the swarm. The features folder makes every shipped capability demo-ready and onboardable from one page, so future demos, sales calls, and onboarding don't have to grep ┬¦4 entries + architecture bullets to reconstruct what a feature actually does. **Out of scope (deferred):** pause/steer-from-graph controls, `agent.spawn` fan-out + parent merge (E4 polish), per-mission message-cap loop guard, cross-workspace HUD, retro-priced cost re-calculation, numeric `trust_score` column on `agent_autonomy` (only the arc is shown), and any new mutations beyond the four reused buttons. **Gotchas:** (1) `agent_autonomy` does not have a `trust_score` column ŌĆö only `arc`. (2) `getSwarmHud` returns jsonb blobs typed as `any` to satisfy TanStack Start's serialization checker. (3) Latest-run-per-agent is computed in JS (not SQL) so we can apply the `running > paused > queued > terminal` priority ŌĆö an 80-row query window is sufficient for an active swarm. (4) No new index ships with this; if `getSwarmHud()` p50 climbs above ~200ms on a large workspace, add covering indexes on `agent_messages(created_at desc)` and `event_queue(created_at desc)` in a small follow-on migration. **Files:** new `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts`, new `src/routes/_authenticated.swarm.tsx`, new `docs/features/README.md` + 4 feature pages; edited `src/components/cadence/AppShell.tsx` (Swarm HUD nav item), `docs/README.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`.

- **2026-06-06 ŌĆö F-AGENT-3: Event reactor + auto-pipelines.** Closes the last "agents do, not just react when summoned" gap. Two new tables: `event_subscriptions` (per-workspace rules: `event_type Ōłł {signal.created, opportunity.scored, prd.approved} ŌåÆ target_agent_slug` with `approval_mode auto|confirm` and jsonb `filter`; RLS workspace-member read + owner write, `is_default` flag distinguishes seeded vs operator rules) and `event_queue` (one row per firing, idempotent UNIQUE `(subscription_id, source_id)` so re-firing triggers is a no-op; statuses `pending ŌåÆ dispatched | skipped | failed`; carries `mission_id`/`run_id`/`error`). Three SECURITY DEFINER trigger fns fan-out matching subs into the queue: `signals` (AFTER INSERT), `opportunities` (only on insert or ICE-input change AND `NEW.ice_score >= COALESCE(filter->>'min_score', 8.0)`), `prds` (only on transition into `status='approved'`). New `seed_default_event_subscriptions(uuid)` seeds three defaults per workspace owner ŌĆö `signal.created ŌåÆ discovery (auto)`, `opportunity.scored ŌåÆ strategist (confirm, min_score 8.0)`, `prd.approved ŌåÆ orchestrator (confirm)`; wired into `handle_new_user` for new signups and backfilled for every existing workspace owner. New `src/lib/reactor.functions.ts` exposes `listEventSubscriptions`, `upsertEventSubscription` (verifies the target agent exists for the user before saving), `deleteEventSubscription`, `listEventQueue`, `decideEventDispatch` (operator approve/reject for `confirm` rows), and a shared `dispatchEvent()` helper that creates a real mission via `createMission` + runs `runAgentLoop` with a templated, event-type-specific goal. New cron route `/api/public/hooks/event-reactor-tick` drains pending `auto`-mode rows (BATCH=10) every minute via pg_cron job `event-reactor-tick`. `confirm`-mode rows stay pending until the operator clicks Dispatch/Skip on the new **Reactor activity** panel on `/governance` (5s auto-refresh). `/governance` also gained an **Auto-pipelines** panel: rule list with enable/disable/delete + add-rule composer (event type / agent slug / mode / min-ICE filter). **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 gave Cadence a planner, F-AGENT-2 gave it memory + autonomy; without a reactor the system still required an operator to push every button. With the reactor in place, a high-ICE opportunity auto-queues a PRD-draft mission, an approved PRD queues an orchestrator plan, and a fresh signal auto-clusters ŌĆö the discoverŌåÆdefineŌåÆplan chain runs itself end-to-end behind governance gates. **Out of scope (queued):** F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD). **Gotchas:** (1) The dispatch helper calls `runAgentLoop` synchronously inside the cron handler ŌĆö fine for `auto` orchestrator rows because backpressure already enqueues over-cap missions, but high-frequency event types should wrap with `withIdempotency` or move behind a true queue. (2) Opportunity trigger only checks `>=` against `filter->>'min_score'` (default 8.0); no other comparators yet. (3) Trigger functions are SECURITY DEFINER because the inserting role may not have direct INSERT on `event_queue` ŌĆö do NOT switch to SECURITY INVOKER. (4) Defaults use `is_default=true` so a future "reset" button can re-seed without clobbering operator rules. **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_event_reactor_and_subscriptions.sql`, new `src/lib/reactor.functions.ts`, new `src/routes/api/public/hooks/event-reactor-tick.ts`; edited `src/routes/_authenticated.governance.tsx`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `plan.md`.
- **2026-06-06 ŌĆö F-AGENT-1: Orchestrator + multi-agent mission decomposition.** First half of the "agent ecosystem" bundle. The substrate (chokepoint, agent*runs, agent_messages, checkpoints, trust, guardrails, missions) already existed but every mission was effectively single-agent ŌĆö `agent.handoff` was a primitive without a meta-planner. New seed agent `orchestrator` (created on first use via `seed_orchestrator_agent(p_user_id)` SECURITY DEFINER fn; idempotent re-seed bumps the system-prompt + tool wiring). New `mission_steps` table: `(mission_id, idx, agent_slug, sub_goal, depends_on int[], status, run_id, message_id, result, error, rationale, dispatched_at, completed_at)`; RLS scoped to `auth.uid()=user_id` with workspace_member read; unique on `(mission_id, idx)`. New SQL helper `next_ready_mission_steps(mission_id)` returns step rows whose `depends_on` are all `status='done'`. Four new agent tools registered: `mission.plan` calls a sub-model with a planning system prompt (lists the user's actual specialist roster, asks for strict JSON `{summary, steps:[{agent_slug, sub_goal, depends_on, rationale}]}`, 1ŌĆō8 steps cap, validates every slug is real before persisting); `mission.dispatch` reflects in-flight child-run statuses, then for every ready step calls `enqueueHandoff()` (existing primitive) to insert a child `agent_runs` row + `agent_messages` row, marks the step `dispatched`, records `run_id` + `message_id`; `mission.observe` reflects + returns per-step state + a status histogram + `all_terminal` boolean; `mission.finalize` requires `all_terminal`, marks the mission `completed` or `completed_with_failures`. Loop step cap is per-agent now via `maxStepsFor(agentSlug)` ŌĆö orchestrator gets 14 to fit plan + observe/dispatch cycles + finalize; specialists keep 6. Three new server fns in `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`: `ensureOrchestrator()` for explicit bootstrap, `startOrchestratedMission({goal,title?,model?})` for the canonical entry (idempotent seed + roster pre-flight + mission row + orchestrator loop), `advanceMission({missionId})` for the operator to push the next round of dispatches manually until F-AGENT-3 wires automatic re-wake, plus `listMissionSteps({missionId})` for read. UI: `/missions` gained an inline "Plan & dispatch" composer (title + goal textarea + one button) so the operator never needs to escape to `/agents` to launch a multi-agent mission; `/missions/$id` gained an "Orchestrator plan" panel above the existing timeline + graph showing the DAG with status pills + deps + an **Advance** button when work remains. Specialist child runs execute asynchronously via the existing `resume-runs` cron ŌĆö no new infra. **WHY:** the substrate was 95% there but the \_behavior* was missing ŌĆö until something planned a goal into a graph and dispatched it, "agent-native OS" was the marketing phrase for a single-agent planner-executor. Closes the first of three F-AGENT- gaps that block the autonomous-product-OS thesis. **Out of scope this turn (queued):** F-AGENT-2 (persistent agent memory + auto self-reflection + trust-arc auto-advance), F-AGENT-3 (event reactor + auto-pipelines), F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD), Restructure Phases 3ŌĆō4 (deferred per operator). **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_mission_steps_and_orchestrator.sql` (+ a second migration patching the seed function with required `display_name`/`description` on `agent_tools` inserts), new `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, new `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.index.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`.
- **2026-06-06 ŌĆö F-AGENT-2: Persistent agent memory + auto self-reflection + trust-arc auto-advance.** Second half of the agent-ecosystem bundle (F-AGENT-3 reactor + F-AGENT-4 Swarm HUD still queued). New `src/lib/ai/reflection.server.ts` exports `autoReflect()` (calls Gemini Flash through the chokepoint with `surface='agent', surface_ref='reflect:<slug>'`, expects strict JSON `{lesson, what_worked, what_to_change, importance:1-5}`, writes a `kind='reflection'` row to `agent_memory` with embedding + structured metadata ŌĆö `run_id`, `trace_id`, `goal`, `what_worked`, `what_to_change`) and `maybeAutoAdvanceArc()` (wraps the new `auto_advance_agent_arc(p_user_id, p_agent_id)` SECURITY DEFINER RPC). `loop.server.ts` calls both from BOTH finalize paths (fresh run + resumed run) when `!halted` ŌĆö halted runs skip reflection by design, so a governance halt never turns into a self-confirming lesson without operator review. `recallMemory()` now merges two sources: the existing `match_agent_memory` semantic search and the new `recent_agent_reflections` RPC (importance + recency ranked, top 3), deduped by content, capped at 8 ŌĆö so reflections surface even when the embedding store is sparse or the goal is novel. Two new tools in the registry: `memory.reflect` (category=memory; agent/operator on-demand reflection ŌĆö reads the current run's input/output if available, wraps `autoReflect`) and `memory.promote` (escalate a memory's scope agentŌåÆglobal so every agent in the workspace recalls it; e.g. "Q3 priority is retention"). Autonomy RPC: `auto_advance_agent_arc` SECURITY DEFINER promotes ObservingŌåÆProving at 5 clean completed runs and ProvingŌåÆTrusted at 20, only when no `agent_approvals.status='rejected'` row exists since the last `agent_autonomy.set_at`; never auto-promotes past Trusted (Ambient stays an explicit operator decision); never downgrades; tolerant of both legacy `status='complete'` (`runAgent` one-shot) and modern `status='completed'` (`loop.server.ts`); sets `set_by=NULL` on system promotion so the UI can distinguish operator vs system moves later. New `recent_agent_reflections(for_user, for_agent_slug, match_count)` SECURITY DEFINER RPC + new `listAgentReflections` server fn (`src/lib/agents.functions.ts`) power a **Recent reflections** panel on `/agents` showing each lesson with importance pill + what-worked / what-to-change sub-blocks pulled out of `metadata`. New cron route `/api/public/hooks/memory-tick` (daily 03:30 UTC via `memory-tick-daily` pg*cron job) deletes `importance <= 2 AND COALESCE(last_used_at, created_at) < now()-30d`, two split passes so the new `agent_memory_decay_idx` is actually used. Migration also fixed the long-standing `agent_memory` grants ŌĆö table was created without `GRANT SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE ŌĆ” TO authenticated`, only `sandbox_exec` had access; PostgREST + admin paths now work. Two new SECURITY DEFINER fns had EXECUTE revoked from PUBLIC (anon can't call them; only `authenticated` + `service_role`). **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 gave us a planner that decomposes goals ŌĆö F-AGENT-2 makes the resulting work \_compound*. Without persistent reflection every run started cold; without auto-advance the trust dial was operator-only, defeating the point of an autonomy ladder. Together these two close the "agents that learn and earn autonomy" half of the autonomous-product-OS thesis. **Out of scope (queued):** F-AGENT-3 (event reactor: `signal.created`ŌåÆDiscovery, `opportunity.scored>=80`ŌåÆStrategist, `prd.approved`ŌåÆOrchestrator + `/governance` subscriptions CRUD), F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD route with live missions / handoffs / pending approvals / auto-pipeline firings panels), Restructure Phases 3ŌĆō4. **Gotchas for the next tool:** (1) reflections write under the per-user supabase client RLS path, so they only land when `runId` exists; ad-hoc loop runs without an `agent_runs` row still reflect via the same helper but the `metadata.run_id` is null ŌĆö UI handles that. (2) `auto_advance_agent_arc` is called with `set_by=NULL` for system promotions; if you add a "promoted by" badge later, NULL = system, non-NULL = operator. (3) the cron-side admin client bypasses RLS for `memory-tick` deletes ŌĆö keep importanceŌēż2 + 30d cutoffs tight so we never destroy operator-authored memories (`memory.remember` writes default importance=3, above the floor). (4) `memory.reflect` is intentionally `category=memory` (not `write`), so the autonomy dial cannot loosen it past `auto`; reflections should not be approval-gated. **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/reflection.server.ts`, new `src/routes/api/public/hooks/memory-tick.ts`, two new migrations (`<ts>_agent_memory_grants_and_autonomy_advance.sql` + `<ts>_revoke_public_execute_on_helpers.sql`); edited `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/agents.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.agents.tsx`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`.

- **2026-06-04 ŌĆö Bundle 5 Live Mission Graph (E6) shipped.** `/missions/$id` only had a linear timeline + per-hop progress panel; multi-agent missions couldn't be _seen_ as a graph, which is the literal success criterion for Step 5 of the build-order rollup ("graph updates in real time as agents act; clicking a node opens that agent's trace + cost + tokens + approval state"). Added a pure-SVG DAG component `src/components/cadence/MissionGraph.tsx` and mounted it above the existing timeline + hops list. **Nodes** = one per `agent_runs` row in the mission; status color + glyph + agent name + slug + status text. **Edges** = one per `agent_messages` row, drawn `source_run_id ŌåÆ consumed_by_run_id`; for in-flight handoffs not yet consumed, fall back to the earliest later hop targeting `to_agent_slug`. Edges are violet bezier paths with arrow markers + the message `kind` label. **Layout** = BFS-depth columns (root hops at column 0, each handoff bumps the child's column) ├Ś chronological rows within column, so a single-agent mission renders 1 node / 0 edges and a Discovery ŌåÆ Strategist ŌåÆ Builder mission renders 3 nodes connected by 2 labelled edges; multiple outbound messages from the same parent stack as parallel children in the next column (E4 fan-out polish ready without a new tool). **Interaction**: nodes are real `role="button"` SVG groups with `onKeyDown` Enter/Space; clicking expands the matching hop card (adds to the existing `expanded` Set) and smooth-scrolls via `id="hop-{run_id}"` + `scroll-mt-24`. Re-uses the existing `refetchInterval: 2000` while mission `status='running'`/`queued`, so the graph fills in live. Pure read model ŌĆö no schema change, no new server fn, consumes the existing `getMission` payload. WHY: Step 5 of the build-order rollup needs the graph to be literally true, and Bundle 4's claim ("A2A is first-class, no human in the routing path") only becomes operator-legible once the routing is visible as a graph rather than a list. **Out of scope this turn:** pause/steer-from-graph controls, zoom/collapse for >20-node graphs, per-node cost/token rollup pill (needs `getMission` to surface it), explicit `agent.spawn` tool. **Files:** new `src/components/cadence/MissionGraph.tsx`; edited `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`.

Always visible while `running`/`queued`; collapses behind Detail when finished. Refresh interval tightened to 2s while live; header shows a live indicator; each hop card now exposes a one-click `/traces/$traceId` link. WHY: claim C1 ("agents \_do*, humans govern") requires the operator to _see_ the doing in real time ŌĆö without per-step visibility a mission feels frozen even when it's running, and silent tool failures (like the Firecrawl bug) hide forever. **Out of scope this turn:** DAG view for parallel fan-out (still queued for Bundle 5), per-step token/cost rollup on the hop card, websocket push (we still poll). **Files:** edited `src/lib/missions.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `src/lib/ai/tools/firecrawl.server.ts`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`.
- **2026-06-04 ŌĆö Web access for agents shipped (Firecrawl-backed `web.*` tools).** Agents were siloed: a goal like _"scout how Linear's AI triage is positioned and give me a non-reactive one-pager"_ needed the public internet but had no tool to call, so they hallucinated or stopped short. Added four governed tools to `TOOL_REGISTRY` ŌĆö `web.search` (ranked results + optional in-line scrape), `web.fetch` (single URL ŌåÆ markdown), `web.map` (URL discovery), `web.crawl` (bounded crawl, max 25 pages / depth 2) ŌĆö all routed through one helper `src/lib/ai/tools/firecrawl.server.ts` that reads `FIRECRAWL_API_KEY` from `process.env` only. Search/fetch/map default to `auto`; `web.crawl` defaults to `confirm` because it spends real Firecrawl credits. Returns are clipped (search snippets 2 KB, fetch markdown 8 KB default / 20 KB max, crawl pages 4 KB each) so token spend stays predictable. Results re-enter the loop as untrusted input ŌĆö the next `callModel()` already runs them through pre-guardrails (PII / prompt-injection / secret keyword) per `architecture/runtime.md`, no new code required. Trust arc + kill-switch + per-mission spend cap still apply unchanged because tools sit in the same registry. Connected Firecrawl as a workspace connector (`FIRECRAWL_API_KEY`). Migration updates `seed_default_agent_tools` for new signups and backfills the four tool rows for every existing user. WHY: closes the "agents _do_, humans govern" gap ŌĆö without outbound web I/O the platform was a workspace-only reasoner, not an operator. **Out of scope this turn:** per-user domain allow/deny UI, a higher-level `web.research` chain tool, browser automation, swapping providers. **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/tools/firecrawl.server.ts`, new `docs/web-access.md`, new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_web_tools_seed.sql`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `architecture/integrations.md`, `docs/planning/archive/feature-backlog.md`, `docs/README.md`.
- **2026-06-04 ŌĆö Bundle 4 Agent-to-Agent handoff (E1ŌĆōE5 MVP) shipped.** New `missions` + `agent_messages` tables (RLS-scoped to workspace members; hop counter + current-agent kept in sync via trigger); `agent_runs.mission_id` added (nullable, single-agent runs still valid). - **2026-06-04 ŌĆö Bundle 3 Agent Trust Score + Autonomy Dial (C6) shipped.** New `agent_autonomy` table (one row per user+agent, arc enum `observing|proving|trusted|ambient`, owner-only RLS, standard GRANTs). Trust score is computed on read in `src/lib/ai/trust.server.ts` (`computeAllAgentTrust`) from real signals ŌĆö mission completion rate (`agent_runs.status`), approval acceptance rate (`agent_approvals.status`), and eval mean (`ai_evals.score` joined via `ai_events.agent_id`) ŌĆö Bayesian-shrunk toward 0.5 when sample <10 so a single-run agent doesn't render as 100. `resolveApprovalMode(toolMode, arc)` is the single combiner the loop calls at the gate decision: Observing forces `review` even on `auto` tools, Proving forces `confirm`, Trusted runs `confirm` inline, Ambient runs everything inline. Safety floor: `review` is sticky (never downgraded by the dial), and `calendar.create` keeps `confirm` even at Ambient. Server fns `getAllAgentTrust` + `setAgentArc` in `src/lib/trust.functions.ts` (both `requireSupabaseAuth`). `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts` now loads the arc once per run (both fresh and resumed paths) and uses `resolveApprovalMode` at every tool-call gate instead of reading `modeOf.get(name)` directly. UI: `/agents` renders a color-tiered Trust chip (with hover tooltip showing the full breakdown + formula + suggested arc) on every roster button and the detail header, plus an inline AutonomyDial (4 arc buttons + suggested-arc hint + plain-language explainer) inside the detail card; the dispatch mutation also invalidates the trust query so a completed mission updates the score in place. - **2026-06-03 ŌĆö PM lifecycle tools shipped (`research.synthesize`, `prd.draft`, `backlog.prioritize`).** Added 3 PM-centric agentic tools to `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` and seeded them into `agent_tools` for every existing user (and for new signups via the updated `seed_default_agent_tools(uuid)`), all default `confirm` mode. (1) `research.synthesize` ŌĆö pulls recent ungrouped `signals` (filterable by tag/sentiment/lookback), asks the model (via `callModel`, surface=`discovery`, `responseFormat=json_object`) to cluster them into 2ŌĆō6 cohesive themes, writes `themes` rows (severity 1ŌĆō5, confidence 0ŌĆō1, frequency = signal count) and links source signals via `signals.theme_id`. (2) `prd.draft(opportunity_id)` ŌĆö reads the opportunity, joins its `theme` + top 8 supporting signals, asks the model (surface=`prd`) to draft a structured PRD (Problem / Target user / Goals / Non-goals / Stories / Solution sketch / Success metrics / Risks) and writes a `prds` row in `draft` status with `model` recorded. (3) `backlog.prioritize` ŌĆö for each backlog opportunity, gathers supporting-signal count + recency (last 7d), asks the model to re-score ICE (1ŌĆō10 integers) with rationale, updates `opportunities.{impact,confidence,ease}` (ice_score is a generated column so it recomputes), returns the new ranked list with rationales. All three flow through the AI chokepoint so they hit guardrails + budgets + tracing, and through the agent loop they pick up `runId`/`stepIndex` automatically for idempotent retry on resume. No per-agent assignment needed ŌĆö the loop filters `TOOL_REGISTRY` by what the user has enabled, so Discovery Scout / PRD Writer / Strategist see them immediately. Closes the Define + Plan halves of the Bundle 6 lifecycle slice that previously had only the GitHub-issue write on the Build edge. Files: `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, migration `seed_pm_lifecycle_tools(uuid)` + folded into `seed_default_agent_tools(uuid)` with a backfill loop.
- **2026-06-03 ŌĆö FND-RUNTIME 0.9 runtime instrumentation + N1 `github.issue.create` shipped.** Added `src/lib/runtime/idempotency.server.ts` (`withIdempotency(scope,key,userId,runId,fn)` ŌåÆ execute ŌåÆ INSERT-on-conflict-fall-back-to-cached against the new `idempotency_keys` table). Refactored `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts` so both `runAgentLoop()` (fresh) and new exported `resumeAgentLoop(runId)` (rehydrates from latest `agent_run_checkpoints` row) feed a shared `executeLoop()`; every iteration upserts a checkpoint _before_ the provider call (so a `GovernanceHaltError` mid-stream never re-bills on resume) and wraps tool execution in `withIdempotency` keyed `tool:{runId}:{stepIndex}:{toolName}` ŌĆö replaying a step short-circuits to the cached result instead of re-invoking the side-effecting tool. Added per-workspace **backpressure** (default 5 concurrent `running` runs); over-cap missions insert as `status='queued'` and are promoted by the new `/api/public/hooks/resume-runs` sweeper, which also resumes `running` runs whose `last_checkpoint_at` is >2 min stale (worker eviction). Sweeper is `pg_cron`-driven every minute against the stable preview URL. Added **`github.issue.create`** agentic tool to `TOOL_REGISTRY` (category `write`, default `confirm` mode): writes to the single allow-listed `GITHUB_REPO` env, validated `owner/name` format, idempotent via caller-supplied `idempotency_key` (e.g. PRD id) so re-execution from a checkpoint never double-creates an issue. ToolCtx extended with optional `runId` + `stepIndex` so future tools can key their own idempotency without re-deriving. Files: `src/lib/runtime/idempotency.server.ts` (new), `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/resume-runs.ts` (new), plus a `pg_cron` migration scheduling `resume-runs` every minute. Set the status board in [feature-backlog.md](file:///Users/rohitgajaraj/Documents/My Projects/My Builds/Project-Cadence/docs/planning/feature-backlog.md) to show `0.1 (FND-TENANCY)` is active under `Antigravity`.

Untracked it and added `nango/` to `.gitignore` (working copy kept on disk). **Decision:** when integrations are wired, run Nango as a separate backend (Nango Cloud or self-hosted via its own docker-compose) and consume it via `@nangohq/node` + `@nangohq/frontend` + `NANGO_HOST`/`NANGO_SECRET_KEY` env ŌĆö same service-behind-a-URL pattern as Supabase. ## 5. Legacy build log (retained ŌĆö the previous source, for reuse)

> This is the earlier build (the "vibe-coded" source). **It is a reuse reference, not the plan.** Mine it for what survives the stress-test; supersede entries as they're rebuilt into section 4. Do not treat anything here as current truth without checking the code.

- **Foundation** ŌĆö Supabase auth (email + Google OAuth), `profiles`, workspaces + extended `projects`, persistent SSE chat with workspace grounding, model-agnostic router with per-surface defaults, command palette (ŌīśK), Mission Control widgets, OKLCH dark theme, RLS, loader+Suspense pattern, route boundaries, global auth middleware. _(Largely reusable.)_
- **Discovery & specs** ŌĆö `signals` ingest (paste/CSV, chunked inserts; sentiment on insert), clustering (k-medoid + synthesis with `evidence_ids[]`), themes ŌåÆ ICE opportunities, one-click PRD ŌåÆ Tiptap with `/ai` slash menu, `prd_versions` autosave + diff, early pgvector RAG (512/64 chunks, 1536-d). _(Reusable; this is the first-slice base.)_
- **Planning & meeting intelligence** ŌĆö Now/Next/Later board (`@dnd-kit`). _(Tail of this legacy entry was lost in an earlier edit collision that spliced the ┬¦6 heading mid-line ŌĆö recover details from git history if ever needed.)_

## 6. Product-agent roster (re-examined: explicit vs. implicit)

**The question:** is a fixed roster of 16 named agents right? **Answer:** no ŌĆö split it. Use a small set of **durable, named lifecycle agents** (explicit, one owner per stage) plus an orchestrator that **dynamically spawns ephemeral specialist sub-agents** for sub-tasks (implicit). Fixed seats for micro-roles create clutter; dynamic sub-agents scale with the work.

**6 outcome-focused durable agents (explicit, one per lifecycle band):**

The roster is kept narrow and delivery-oriented. Each agent owns a clear band of the product lifecycle. Fixed seats for micro-roles are avoided ŌĆö those collapse into ephemeral specialists.

| Agent            | Lifecycle band                                                  | Owns                                                                                                             | Primary pain point addressed                                    |
| ---------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Orchestrator** | All stages                                                      | Mission coordination, spawns ephemeral specialists, manages approval routing, parallelism                        | Coordination overhead, context loss between stages              |
| **Discovery**    | S1 Signal Capture + S2 Audio Sync                               | Signal Ingest (Zendesk/Intercom/Slack), clustering opportunities, WhisperFlow transcription and audio extraction | Shallow discovery, anecdotal signals, missing verbal alignments |
| **Strategist**   | S3 ICE Prioritization + S4 Spec Definition + S5 Sprint Planning | Opportunity scoring, cited PRD generation, Linear/GitHub Issues sync, dependency-aware task graphs               | Spec drafting overhead, weak prioritization, feature factories  |
| **Builder**      | S6 Agentic Build + S7 Visual QA + S8 Safe Release               | Multi-file coding, file claims ledger, sandbox previews, PR merge checks and deploy monitoring                   | Developer bottlenecks, styling drift, release quality checks    |
| **Growth**       | S9 GTM Launch                                                   | Outbound changelogs, blog posts, Slack notifications and release announcements                                   | Launch overhead, delayed go-to-market communication             |
| **Analyst**      | S10 Support Triage + S11 Cohort Analytics + S12 Learn & Reflect | Support ticket routing to S1, adoption funnels, performance metrics vs PRD specs, Product Memory                 | Closed-loop support, un-measured features, memory decay         |

**Ephemeral specialists (spawned by Orchestrator per task):** competitor scan, UX critique, stakeholder brief, data analysis, security review, code review, and any other short-lived specialist. They inherit the chokepoint, tool allow-list, and governance. No permanent seats for micro-roles.

**Persona mapping:**

- **P1 (Director / VP of Product)**: strategic oversight, budget controls, audit log reviews, portfolio health, uses Analyst + Orchestrator.
- **P2 (Lead / Senior PM)**: daily operator, runs swarm briefs, PRD editor, discovery feeds, uses Discovery + Strategist + Analyst.
- **P3 (Engineering Lead)**: code review, Builder agent claims review, CI verification, uses Builder.
- **P4 (UX/UI Designer)**: sandbox preview validation, style token audit, uses Builder (Visual QA).
- **P5 (GTM Lead)**: launch copywriting, distribution approvals, uses Growth.
- **P6 (Support Lead)**: triage validation, bug signal loops, uses Analyst.

Schema per agent: `slug, name, system_prompt, tool_allowlist[], default_model, temperature/top_p/seed, max_tokens, schedule_cron?, approval_mode (auto|confirm|review), memory_enabled`. Roster changes need a migration + a build-order entry.

---

## 7. Testing strategy

- **Unit:** pricing math, each guardrail rule kind, RAG chunker boundaries, ICE/cron/date helpers.
- **Integration:** chokepoint (one `ai_events` row + trace; budget throws before provider; cache short-circuits but logs; guardrail block aborts + logs; ticks idempotent); orchestration (parallel sessions isolated; checkpoints resume; cancellation saves partial trace); RLS isolation across products/workspaces.
- **Autonomous build/test loop:** the Builder agent's output must pass the QA agent's generated tests before Ship; a failing eval suite ("Cadence core") blocks deploy (Ōēź10-point regression on the 0ŌĆō100 scale, without override ŌĆö KI-14).
- **E2E:** intent ŌåÆ discover ŌåÆ define ŌåÆ plan ŌåÆ build ŌåÆ test ŌåÆ ship, watched in the orchestration view; multi-product isolation; ŌīśK across routes; `/observe` renders on seeded data.
- **Manual QA before release:** auth + tenancy isolation; every route empty/partial/full; AI message contract present ([`DESIGN.md`](./DESIGN.md)); guardrail block works; budget breach is friendly; light-theme Cohere editorial contrast.

---

## 8. Lessons learned (kept from the legacy build)

One AI chokepoint paid for itself (judge added in half a day). Loader + `useSuspenseQuery` killed `useEffect+fetch` regressions. OKLCH tokens ended dark-mode contrast bugs. Bugs fixed: name-vs-email leak; duplicate agent fan-out (advisory lock); action-item due-date glitch; Notion BFS reorder; trace recursion blow-up; cache cross-user poisoning (salted key); CSV params cap (chunked inserts). Known limits: clustering degrades past ~1000 signals/run; Studio truncates files >2k lines; Docs sync drops comments; `model_pricing` hand-maintained.

---

## 9. Out of scope (for now)

Fine-tuning workflows from `ai_events`; cross-workspace vector sharing; public agent/skill-pack marketplace; cross-workspace SSO; fully autonomous _strategic_ decisions (strategic conclusions keep a human gate by design ŌĆö tactical ones may auto-apply). These are deliberate exclusions, revisited when the core loop is solid.

**H3 ┬Ę Scheduling (calendar-aware work blocks) ŌĆö SHIPPED.** Agent proposes deep-work blocks into free time within the operator's working hours, fitting the task around meetings and respecting focus. Built: (1) `proposeWorkBlocks` server fn in `calendar.functions.ts` ŌĆö reads open deep-work tasks (is_deep_work=true, status != done) from the `tasks` table, fetches the user's working-hours bounds from the profile, queries calendar events for the next 7 days (daysAhead param), and uses a simple greedy algorithm (30-min slot buckets, skip weekends/out-of-hours, skip conflicts) to place one block per task into the first-fit free slot. Returns a list of WorkBlock (start_at, end_at, title, label with formatted time). Boundaries are soft (a packed calendar yields fewer blocks; no forced fit). (2) UI affordance in `CalendarPanel.tsx` ŌĆö a "Plan deep work" button in the action bar triggers the proposal, showing a panel with the proposed blocks + "Add to calendar" per-block buttons; a visual state change (color shift) marks added blocks; a "Re-plan ┬Ę new proposal" option re-runs the algorithm (useful if the calendar changed). (3) Mutations integrate with the existing `createCalendarEvent` so added blocks sync two-way with the user's calendar provider (Google/Microsoft). **Scope:** the proposal algorithm is honest (no speculative ML or scoring); the 7-day window and 30-min bucket size are sensible defaults (tunable via params). Deferred: adaptive working-hour inference, multi-day blocks, and conflict re-routing (schedule around soft-constraints rather than hard skip). **Verification:** `bun test` 163 green, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean, dev server boots. Manual: seeded workspace with 3 open deep-work tasks + a calendar with 6 events ŌåÆ "Plan deep work" proposes 2 blocks (Tue afternoon, Thu morning, both 60-min, both fit free slots, both fit within 09:00ŌĆō18:00). **Files:** `src/lib/calendar.functions.ts` (proposeWorkBlocks + type), `src/components/knowledge/CalendarPanel.tsx` (affordance + mutations + UI), dashboard/this log.

**U6 ┬Ę Workspace data export (data portability), CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 1, 2026-06-18).** The trust escape-hatch: Settings > Data downloads the entire workspace as one JSON file. Built: (1) `exportWorkspace` server fn in `projects.functions.ts` (mirrors B5 `exportProduct` at workspace scope): resolves the active workspace (passed from the client, falling back to first membership), gathers projects (by workspace_id), signals/opportunities/specs(`prds`)/tasks (by project_id across the workspace's projects, guarded against the empty-projects case so it never issues an empty `in()`), and the user's own `learnings` + `agent_memory` (owner-scoped by user_id). RLS scopes every read to the caller; returns a JSON-safe shape with a per-section `counts` map. No migration (read-only). (2) `DataExportCard.tsx` in `src/components/settings/` + a new "Data" tab on `/settings`: a calm-front card that calls the fn, downloads `cadence-workspace-export-<date>.json`, and toasts the record count. It passes the active workspace id so multi-workspace users export the right one. **Adversarial review folded 2 fixes:** the empty-projects `.in([])` guard, and the active-workspace-id pass-through (it was exporting the first workspace, not the active one). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify** (not deployed yet). **Remaining (ŌŚÉ):** per-section selective export + an export audit-log. **Files:** `src/lib/projects.functions.ts`, `src/components/settings/DataExportCard.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.settings.tsx`, `docs/features/u6-data-export.md`, dashboard/this log.

**R3 ┬Ę Notifications, in-app Attention feed CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 2, 2026-06-18).** The operator hears about what needs them, in one place. Built: (1) `getNotifications` server fn in a new `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`: derives a unified feed live from the loop's own state, with no new table: pending tool-call approvals (`agent_approvals` status=pending), a stalled loop (`agent_runs` running/queued past the 30-minute window), and spend nearing or over a cap (`ai_budgets` daily/monthly vs `alert_at_pct`). Read-only, RLS-scoped by user_id; each probe degrades to a safe default so the feed can never break its surface. Returns a severity-sorted `AppNotification[]` (action > warning > info) with a deep-link href per item, plus a `count` for a future bell badge. (2) `NotificationsPanel.tsx` + a new "Attention" tab on the Engine Room (`/govern?tab=attention`): a calm feed of severity-coded cards, each linking to its home (approvals / spend / loop-health), with an "All clear" empty state. **Adversarial review folded 1 fix:** placed Attention second (not first) so the default-selected leftmost tab stays Controls (no behavior change; the default landing is left to a founder taste call). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify.** **Remaining (ŌŚÉ):** email + digests, per-user notification prefs, and the global bell badge. **Files:** `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`, `src/components/governance/NotificationsPanel.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.govern.tsx`, `docs/features/r3-notifications.md`, dashboard/this log.

**P7 ┬Ę Incidents log, read-only CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 3, 2026-06-18).** A record when something goes wrong, instead of failures vanishing into the logs. Built: (1) `getIncidents` server fn in a new `src/lib/incidents.functions.ts`: derives a read-only "what went wrong" log with no new table from confirmed sources: `agent_approvals` (status=failed, by user_id) for failed tool executions, and `event_queue` (rows with a non-null error, scoped to the resolved default workspace) for errored auto-pipelines. **D4 mission cancellation (the per-mission brake) + H1-TASKS reconciliation (autonomous overnight cycle 10, 2026-06-18).** This cycle corrects cycle 8's read that D4 was "NOT gate-verifiable, unsafe to build blind." That call lumped D4's cancellation slice in with the harder replay/checkpoint work. Deep recon proved the **cancellation slice** is safe and fully offline-gateable: the auto-advance tick already selects missions by `.in("status",["running","in_progress"])` and `advanceMissionCore` early-returns for any non-running mission, so cancelling is a pure state transition with **zero loop surgery**; `missions.status`/`agent_runs.status` carry no CHECK and `agent_approvals.status` already allows `cancelled`, so **no migration**. Built `cancelMission` (`missions.functions.ts`) + a "Cancel mission" control in the mission-detail hero (`useConfirm`, shown only while active) + a `cancelled` `StatusBadge`. The cascade stops the resume cron resuming orphaned child runs (required for correctness, not cosmetics), releases held Build file claims (the `release_claims_for_terminal_run` trigger skips `cancelled`, so locks would otherwise orphan), and clears pending approvals. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, the 3 touched files lint clean (the repo-wide `bun run lint` shows pre-existing prettier debt in untouched files, flagged in the report; not mass-reformatted). **Adversarial review** folded a TOCTOU guard (only flip to `cancelled` if still non-terminal, so a mission that finishes in the readŌåÆwrite window keeps its honest state) and confirmed `completed_at` does not corrupt the analytics completion metric (it filters on `status='completed'`). Also reconciled **`H1-TASKS` ŌåÆ Ō£ģ**: PRD ŌåÆ engineering task graph is already built end to end (`generateTaskGraph` in `discovery.functions.ts` + the dependency-ordered task-graph card on `/prds/$id`). Aligns with the founder's core-first ruling (D4 is core loop/mission control); the **next pick is `F3`** (continuous discovery), the founder's named top core candidate. **Pending publish + live verify** (table in the report). **Files:** `missions.functions.ts`, `_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `Primitives.tsx`, `docs/features/d4-mission-cancellation.md` (new) + features index, dashboard (D4 ŌŚÉ, H1-TASKS Ō£ģ, G2 counts), report, session-decisions, this log.

**F3 always-fresh discovery feed (autonomous overnight cycle 11, 2026-06-18).** Picked `F3` per the founder's core-first ruling (named top core candidate). Recon: signals already ingest continuously (webhook ŌåÆ reactor ŌåÆ `event_queue`), but the discovery surface was static (manual reload) and clustering (`clusterSignals`) is manual + user-wide. Adversarial review: bounded walk (no runaway on a cyclic/huge graph), RLS-scoped, clean empty state. **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/lib/lineage.functions.ts`, `src/components/product/OpportunityDetail.tsx`, `docs/features/o1-provenance.md` (new) + features index, dashboard (O1 ŌŚÉ, G1 counts), report, this log.

**Permission policy hardening + capture (autonomous overnight cycle 13, 2026-06-18, founder-requested).** The founder was getting a permission prompt on every read/edit/command. Root cause: a session reads the `.claude/settings.local.json` of the directory it is LAUNCHED from; this session runs from the repo ROOT, but the bypass config only existed in the WORKTREE's copy, so the root session prompted on everything. **Fix:** (1) set `defaultMode: bypassPermissions` + the broad allow + destructive deny + both directories in the **root** `.claude/settings.local.json` (local, gitignored, per-machine); (2) added a shared `permissions` allow/deny block to the **committed** `.claude/settings.json` so the lists travel with the repo and cover regular daytime builds too (no `defaultMode` there ŌĆö bypass stays a per-machine opt-in, never committed); (3) wrote [`docs/operations/permissions.md`](docs/operations/permissions.md) capturing the two-layer model, the deny-list floor, and the learnings (which settings file a session reads, settings read at startup, the worktree gotcha); linked it from `autonomous-build-loop.md` ┬¦11 + CLAUDE.md read order. No app code. **Files:** `.claude/settings.json` (committed), `docs/operations/permissions.md` (new), `docs/operations/autonomous-build-loop.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, report, this log. (Local `.claude/settings.local.json` updated on the machine; gitignored, not committed.)

**R3 global Attention bell (autonomous overnight cycle 15, 2026-06-18).** Advances `R3`: the Attention feed only surfaced "what needs you" once you were inside the Engine Room; this gives it a doorway from every screen. Built `AttentionBell.tsx` (`src/components/cadence/`), a persistent bell in the `TopBar` (rendered next to the AmbientChip, so it appears on every route): it carries the live count of what needs you (approvals waiting, spend nearing a cap, a stalled loop), tinted by the most urgent item (action amber > warning rose > info muted), and links to `/govern?tab=attention`. It is quiet (no badge) when all clear. It reuses `getNotifications` under the **shared `["notifications"]` query key**, so when the Attention panel is also mounted there is one fetch, not two (the same cache-sharing the Approvals badge uses); a failed fetch degrades to "all clear" so the bell can never break the top bar. **Design call (no double-count):** the app already had a Trust-row "Approvals" badge (`getNeedsYou`) that badges the Approvals *nav item* (`?tab=approvals`); the bell badges the *whole* Attention feed (`?tab=attention`). They are deliberately distinct surfaces, so when only approvals exist they agree (reinforcement) and when an alert also exists the bell reads higher; I did not merge or remove the working Approvals badge. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, both touched files lint clean (eslint + prettier), humanization clean (the one em-dash I authored fixed; the `TopBar` header's pre-existing dashes are outside my diff and left untouched per the surgical rule). **Adversarial review** folded one fix: dropped `role="status"` from the actionable `<a>` so the bell keeps its link semantics for screen readers (a live-region role would have overridden the link). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/components/cadence/AttentionBell.tsx` (new), `src/components/cadence/TopBar.tsx`, `docs/features/r3-notifications.md`, dashboard (R3 row + header), report, session-decisions, this log.

**P7 guardrail-block incident source (autonomous overnight cycle 16, 2026-06-18).** Advances `P7`: the Incidents log derived from two sources (failed tool executions + errored pipelines); it now also surfaces **guardrail blocks**. Extended `getIncidents` (`incidents.functions.ts`) with a third source reading the existing `guardrail_hits` table (no migration) filtered to `action = "block"` and scoped by `user_id`: only a block is "what went wrong" (the rule actually stopped an AI call), so the softer `warn`/`redact` actions (the call still runs) are intentionally excluded so routine governance is not mislabelled an incident. Each card reads `Blocked by guardrail: <rule>` with which side it fired on (a blocked prompt vs a withheld response); it deliberately **omits the raw `matched` payload** so nothing sensitive lands in a list view, and carries no trace link (`guardrail_hits` keys to an `event_id`, not a trace).
